Why You Bought This Book
Before I get started, there’ s one thing I know for certain about
you and it’ s this: Y ou’re reading this book for one simple reason
—trust.
Somewhere along the wa y, you trusted someone or sever al
someones. Y ou trusted them enough to believe that there was
something to this whole “B2B Influencer Mark eting” thing and
maybe you should read a book on it.
Maybe it was trust in me.
If that is the case, first of all, thank you. I’ve both been in and
around mark eting spaces long enough that you ma y have
stumbled across my work somewhere, lik ed it, and were willing
to give this book a try .
Or, ma ybe you trust the publisher, K ogan Page. They’ve been
publishing excellent business books since Carl Y astrzemski
(Yaz) won the triple crown back in 1967 for the Sox.
That’ s a long time.
What’ s most lik ely, though, is that a friend or colleague
recommended this book to you. Y ou happened to be looking to
build or expand your influencer mark eting progr am and were
looking for a fr amework to accomplish that. They
recommended it and, on their word, you pick ed it up.
I only bring this up because trust is one of the most important
throughlines in this book.
Influencer mark eting is first and foremost about trust. I’ve
talked with a bunch of experts, exchanged DMs with an untold
number of people across our networks, read books, listened to
podcasts, and even recorded a few of my own.
Just about every single time, the topic of trust just k eeps
coming up.
Trust between the creator and the compan y. Trust between
your internal teams. Trust with prospects and customers.
Collabor ating with influencers and creators isn’t lik e running
a PPC ad campaign. Y ou can’t just increase your bids or go after
a new k eyword to tackle low conversion. Just lik e in your real
relationships, once trust is lost it’ s gone. It ma y not be for good
but at the very least, it’ s going to tak e you a good long while to
rebuild. Y ou can probably think of a few br ands off the top of
your head that have done that (we can too but we’re not going
to name names).
The last thing before we get started is that I hope you’ll trust
in me b y the end of this book. Obviously , I can’t just sa y “Trust
me, this works!”. I am a guy from Boston, I’m sk eptical at a
baseline.
Instead, I hope you’ll stick with me as I help guide you
through establishing an influencer mark eting progr am.
The Rise and Rise of Inﬂuencer Marketing
Whenever someone sa ys influencer mark eting, most mark eters’
minds immediately shift to B2C. After all, influencer mark eting
progr ams have been around for decades.
Consider those old-school, late-night infomercials and
product endorsements lik e Chuck Norris selling the T otal Gym.
That’ s influencer mark eting at its finest because who wouldn’t
want a gym that could mak e you into, well, Chuck Norris?
Fortunately , I can mak e that jok e knowing he’ s not reading this
because Chuck Norris doesn’t read books. He stares them down
until he gets the information he wants.
In a more fictional example, Coca-Cola had perhaps one of the
most famous instances with Santa Clause hawking Coca-Cola in
the mid-20th century . In a campaign created b y Haddon
Sundblom, they used his image alongside their soda to mak e
use of his “friendly , warm, and gr andfather-lik e image” and,
well, the fact that he was Santa (Coca-Cola United, 2018).
Obviously , not everyone can get a mythical holida y legend to
represent their br and but not all br ands are Coca-Cola.
Fast-forward to now and one really can’t escape influencer
mark eting. If you spend an y time on an y social media network,
you’re eventually going to come across an influencer. This tak es
man y forms but in man y cases, it’ll be someone with a
following promoting one product or another to their audience.
Sometimes they ma y be affiliates offering a discount code.
Other times, they ma y be promoting a little bit more subtly and
creating content in collabor ation with a br and.
The reason it’ s been around so long is simple: It works.
There’ s a looming caveat to that statement, however—if B2B
mark eters want to lever age influencer mark eting, it can’t be a
complete port over of what our B2C counterparts are doing.
B2B Marketing: Always Playing Catch-up
B2B mark eting has a reputation for being a bit of a laggard
behind B2C. It is true, but in my defense, it’ s not without reason.
For starters, B2C usually has a far lower barrier to entry . In
man y cases, B2C mark eters aren’t promoting high-tick et items
or even long-term contr acts. Even in those r are corner cases
where they are, B2C br ands are often speaking directly with the
decision-mak er.
One person can enter their sales funnel and go through the
entire buying journey within the span of a few minutes. All
that’ s left is for them to enter their credit card information, and
boom, they’re a customer. In these cases, B2C br ands that
partner with influencers can easily prove R OI, showing that
more dollars spent on influencer partnerships mean an X-
multiple return on the bottom line.
B2B buying motions, meanwhile, are only getting longer and
more complicated. The median B2B sales cycle in SaaS hovers
around 2.5 months (Štefanović, 2023). That’ s an extremely long
time to k eep a single person engaged, never mind the entire
buying committee.
Making matters worse, whenever economic conditions
tighten, budgets (especially those on Revenue teams) are under
intense scrutin y. Sales and Mark eting leaders are often caught
scrambling to justify each and every headcount, expense, and
piece of tech under their purview . With buyers having limited
budgets and having to put their reputations on the line
internally , it’s no wonder that it’ s harder than ever for
mark eters to reach their audience.
Yet not all hope is lost. In spite of all of the obstacles listed
above, influencer mark eting can be hugely successful for B2B
organizations and can overcome all of these challenges.
Inﬂuencer Marketing Is the Future in B2B
I’ve been throwing out a lot of terms. B2B vs B2C doesn’t really
matter. When it comes down to it, though, people are people
and we lik e to deal with, you guessed it, people.
It doesn’t matter whether it’ s a new blender or a cutting-edge,
industry-leading, G2 leader mark eting automation platform—
customer journeys in B2B and B2C start in the same place,
talking to those around us.
Once we’ve identified a problem, we ask our friends, our
networks, and the communities we trust in order to guide our
buying decision. Therein lies a huge opportunity for an y B2B
brands that learn how to partner with influencers.
Influencers have been gaining significant clout over the last
few years. There are more platforms for them to be on than
ever. There are more br ands looking for partnerships. They are,
on balance, simply better content creators.
On the flip side, people simply don’t trust faceless companies
anymore. Ma ybe it’ s from all the data breaches, ma ybe it’ s
because br ands are harder to distinguish from one another, or
maybe it’ s a lack of connection. Whatever it is, people look to
influencers and thought leaders in their industry or specialty in
order to help sift through all the noise.
The br ands and mark eters that follow the advice laid out in
this book can have a voice in those conversations b y partnering
with the right influencers in a people-first, effective, and
scalable manner. I truly believe that influencer mark eting will
be one of the most powerful forces affecting B2B in the years to
come.
Why I wrote this book
The reason I wrote this book, first and foremost, is exactly what
I just said. I believe in influencer mark eting and in my years
spent using it to build a pipeline for companies.
If you don’t know me, first of all, hello! Second, let me give
you a little back ground:
I’m Nick Bennett. I’ve been involved in influencer mark eting
in one form or another for the greater part of my career. After
years dedicated to driving revenue growth and retention for
high-growth startups, I have since cofounded T ACK and ClubPF.
My core mission is championing a people-first go-to-mark et
strategy where the sole focus of an y mark eting efforts is
remembering that the individual is at the heart of every
experience.
GTM stands for “Go-to-Mark et.” It refers to the over arching
strategy and approach that a compan y emplo ys to bring its
product or service to mark et effectively . The G TM str ategy
encompasses various elements such as product positioning,
target mark et identification, distribution channels, pricing
strategies, and mark eting tactics.
In the context of my mission at T ACK, a people-first G TM
strategy means prioritizing the needs, preferences, and
experiences of individual customers above all else. It involves
understanding the unique challenges, desires, and behaviors of
your target audience and tailoring your mark eting efforts to
resonate with them on a personal level. This approach
emphasizes building meaningful relationships with customers,
fostering trust, and delivering value at every touchpoint of their
journey with your br and.
I have experience with influencer mark eting on both sides of
the equation. I consider myself a creator and I have built
various progr am types throughout my career. Since this book is
a distillation of my experience as well as conversations with
dozens of experts around the world, it’ll get confusing if I k eep
switching back and forth.
But enough about me, let’ s talk about you.
Who this book is NO T for
I hate to start on a negative note but figure we should get this
out of the wa y. Influencer mark eting isn’t easy . No matter what
industry , what product or service you’re selling, or how far
along your progr am is, it will tak e time, effort, resources,
consistency , and tenacity . If an y of these sound lik e you, it might
be worth reexamining whether it’ s a fit for you or your
compan y’s GTM motion.
Marketers Who Want a Shortcut or Quick Fix
If there’ s one cliché mark eters love to march out, it’ s this: X is
not a silver bullet. W ell, add influencer mark eting to that list.
Influencer mark eting is all about relationships—both with your
audience as well as with the creators and influencers you’re
collabor ating with. There’ s no wa y to shortcut building that
trust.
Marketers Who Want a Passive Program
With influencer mark eting you can’t just set it and forget it.
Above all, an effective influencer mark eting progr am involves
hands-on time working with the influencer(s) and potentially
being there throughout the content creation. Even the most
talented influencer is going to want you to help come up with
ideas that support both your br and and theirs.
Marketers Who Want to Dictate Orders
If you’re looking to give 10 people with 10K+ followers an
identical message to post, you’re not doing influencer
mark eting, you’re spamming. First of all, the audience will
know that it is #sponsoredcontent and they’ll tune out just the
same wa y they do with a banner ad. Influencer mark eting is not
like PPC ads and they’re not affiliates, they’re collabor ators.
I don’t want you to waste your time so if an y of these apply to
you, you can put this down and go about your da y. Ma ybe tak e a
walk or something, I’ve heard the weather is lovely there this
time of year.
Who You Likely Are
Now that we know who you’re not, I’ve written this book with a
few different reader goals in mind.
Increasing Traction Within Your ICP or New Sectors
When you boil it down, Mark eting as a discipline is about
spreading awareness of a solution to a particular problem or
set of problems. If you’re not getting tr action within your ideal
customer profile (ICP) or you’re moving your solution into
wholly new sectors that don’t even think  they have a problem,
you’re going to be lacking in authority and trust. Influencer
mark eting progr ams can allow you to borrow authority and, b y
extension, trust in order to expand reach and br and awareness.
Expanding Channel Exposure Within Your Programs
Depending on who you ask, it could be an ywhere from 10 to 50
touches before a cold lead becomes a sale. Influencer mark eting
can help amplify your campaign efforts.
Looking to Expand Your Existing Inﬂuencer
Marketing Program
Maybe you’re an old hand at this and simply looking for a wa y
to get better. If this is the case, you’ll find sever al new wa ys to
think about building a bigger progr am, and how to expand your
suite of influencers you collabor ate with.
Even if none of these is an exact fit, B2B influencer mark eting
is only going to get more powerful as time goes on.

1
The History and Evolution of
Influencer Marketing
Let’s open with a question: how man y times do you think you’re
sold to in a da y?
After all, on every digital space from F acebook to blogs, news
sites—heck they’re even selling ad space on the homepage of
people’ s Xboxes—we’re drowning in ads to the point that, while
nobody is quite certain, estimates think we see around 5,000
10,000 ads a da y (Camargo, 2024).
Now for a follow-up question: How man y of those do you
think are relevant or you’ll actually pa y attention to?
That answer we do know: V ery, very few . Banner ad
blindness is real, and our br ains have an exceptional ability to
filter out useless information. The result isn’t fewer ads but
more ads and more competition. That’ s a whole lot of money
you need to pour into paid media campaigns only to get a 2
percent return r ate in PPC (Drexler, 2024). This is just accepted
as the cost of doing business and “how things are done.”
But obviously the title of this book gives awa y what I think is
a better course of action: Influencer mark eting is a more
efficient wa y to capture attention.
Let’s think about your aver age scroll through social media
and think of a similar question to our first one: How man y
times do you find yourself captivated b y a product
recommendation from someone you follow?
Maybe it was a skincare routine from a beauty guru, a tech
gadget review from a savvy creator, or even a fitness tip from a
health influencer. In those moments, you experienced the
power of influencer mark eting—a phenomenon that has
reshaped how we discover, trust, and engage with products and
services.
Did the br and have to pa y for that exposure in some fashion?
Yes. But is it at the same r ate you’d need for a 2 percent return?
Hardly .
I don’t want to pretend lik e this is a new idea though. From
humble beginnings when big-name celebrities endorsed
products, to the present da y where niche creators hold swa y,
the evolution of influencers is a captivating tale of adaptation
and innovation.
A Short His tory of Inﬂuencer Marketing
Influencer mark eting has a long, storied past that’ s as
fascinating as it is relevant. In a wa y, influencer mark eting is
built into our DNA as humans. In the da ys before social media,
TV, or even r adio, people relied on good old-fashioned word of
mouth to spread news. And who better to spread this news than
those with the biggest mouths and the widest networks? These
folks were the original influencers, shaping public opinion one
juicy tidbit at a time.
As far as using influencers to shape buying decisions, we’ve
got to fast-forward a few millennia to 18th-century England.
The Pioneering Years (18th and 19th Centuries)
Long before the advent of the digital age, the roots of influencer
mark eting can be tr aced back to the pr actice of utilizing
celebrities to endorse products. This tr aditional form of
mark eting relied on the star power of iconic figures to swa y
consumer preferences and establish connections between
brands and their target audiences.
Who, then, would be a bigger star than the Queen of
England?
That’ s exactly what Josiah W edgwood, a savvy English potter,
thought when creating a r ange of cream-colored earthenware.
Its name, though not very subtle, was “Queensware.”
Why?
Because Queen Charlotte herself used it, of course! W ell,
allegedly . Either wa y, Queensware was perhaps the first
example of celebrity endorsement, and bo y, did it work.
Wedgwood became synon ymous with luxury and quality ,
setting the standard for br ands to come.
While it’ s clear that not everyone can secure a queen’ s
endorsement for their product, and the impact toda y might not
mirror that of sever al centuries ago, the evolution of influence
has found its modern counterparts.
By the mid-20th century , the explosion of celebrity culture
brought figures lik e Marilyn Monroe, Charlie Chaplin, and
sports icons lik e Babe Ruth to the forefront of public attention.
These celebrities were the early pioneers, la ying the
groundwork for what would eventually evolve into influencer
mark eting.
When Iconic Celebrities Become Brand
Ambassadors (Early 20th Century)
Marilyn Monroe was not only one of the most iconic celebrities
of her time, she was also a sought-after br and partner. During
her lifetime, she famously endorsed Chanel No5 perfume, which
solidified her status as a glamorous symbol of femininity and
beauty . Even decades after she passed, Monroe’ s face can still
be seen from time to time, such as in a 2013 ad campaign for
Sexy Hair, a br and looking to capture the elusive 18–34 female
demogr aphic (Arend, 2014).
Likewise, Babe Ruth, one of the greatest baseball pla yers of
all time, didn’t sh y awa y from helping mark et products. He was
attached at various times to br ands lik e Old Gold cigarettes as
well as various sports par aphernalia such as baseball bats and
gloves. His endorsement of these products reinforced his image
as a dominant athlete and helped promote the br ands to
aspiring athletes and sports enthusiasts.
The mor al of this story is that br ands recognized the
aspir ational appeal of these personalities. They were willing to
spend money in order to “borrow” their fame and reputation
and create a positive association in the minds of buyers.
Celebrity endorsements provided a direct line to consumers,
relying on the public’ s admir ation and trust in these figures.
Most of the previous examples were done either in print or in
person but in the second half of 20th century that would change
with the widespread adoption of television.
Moving Into the Television Age (Mid-to-Late 20th
Century)
Celebrity endorsements tr ansitioned seamlessly to this new
medium with TV commercials featuring beloved actors,
musicians, and athletes became a staple of advertising.
Traditional print formats still pla yed a significant role, with
celebrities gr acing covers of magazines and participating in
promotional campaigns.
But while tr aditional celebrity endorsements were impactful,
they were not without challenges.
The reach was limited to the availability of tr aditional media
channels, and measuring the direct impact on sales was often
challenging. Moreover, the cost associated with securing a
celebrity endorsement made it a str ategy accessible primarily
to larger corpor ations.
Take, for instance, the association between Michael Jordan
and Nik e’s Air Jordan sneak ers. Michael Jordan’ s legendary
bask etball career and his charismatic persona made him one of
the most influential athletes of all time. While Nik e wasn’t
cemented in the cultur al subconscious as yet, they also weren’t
a tin y shop putting out a few pairs of sneak ers a year.
Nike’s partnership with Michael Jordan in the mid-1980s did,
however, revolutionize the sneak er industry . The Air Jordan
line of bask etball shoes not only showcased innovative
technology but also embodied Michael Jordan’ s style and
competitive spirit. Through captivating advertisements and
iconic br anding, Nik e established a powerful connection
between Michael Jordan and the Air Jordan sneak ers.
Consumers, particularly bask etball fans and aspiring athletes,
admired Michael Jordan’ s skills and personality . By wearing Air
Jordans, they felt a sense of connection to their idol and aspired
to emulate his success on the court. The partnership between
Michael Jordan and Nik e transcended mere product
endorsement; it became a cultur al phenomenon that continues
to influence sneak er culture and sports mark eting to this da y.
As the century wore on, mass media gave guys lik e Don
Draper even more new wa ys to convince people to buy stuff—
and they quickly realized the power of having popular figures
represent their products.
Take Coca-Cola, for instance. The soft drink giant made a
habit of partnering with the hottest stars of the da y. I mean if
you can get “Mean” Joe Green or Michael Jordan to endorse
your product, you’re probably going to see a health y boost in
sales. As the media age turned from analog to digital, celebrity
endorsements gave wa y to influencer mark eting.
The Digital Age and the Birth of the Creator
Economy (2000–Present)
Now it’ s time to move into more recent history that has a huge
bearing on how influencer mark eting functions toda y. Believe it
or not, the actual term “influencer mark eting” only dates back
to the mid-2000s.
The mid-2000s mark ed the dawn of the digital age, witnessing
the emergence of the first influencers on platforms lik e
MySpace and early blogs. These early influencers were often
enthusiasts and hobb yists who gained popularity through their
authentic content. The term “influencer mark eting” wasn‘t
coined yet, but the seeds were planted for what would become
a revolutionary mark eting str ategy .
Despite bold new wa ys to reach audiences, influencer
mark eting, at its core, still involves collabor ating with
individuals who have a significant and engaged following on
digital platforms to promote products or services. The term
itself gained tr action as mark eters began recognizing the
unique influence wielded b y individuals on emerging social
media platforms. In a global survey among mark eters (Statista,
2023), around 40 percent of respondents said they invested
more than 40 percent into digital influencer mark eting.
The specific origin of the term “influencer mark eting” is
somewhat elusive, as it has become part of the mark eting
lexicon organically . However, it gained notable attention in
mark eting circles during the rise of social media influencers on
platforms lik e MySpace and early blogs.
The rise of social media did something to influencer
mark eting that other media did not: It made it possible for
everyone to be an influencer, specifically one of three types:
Macro, micro, and nano.
Macro-Inﬂuencers
Macro-influencers are often what people think of when the
topic of influencers comes up. These are the individuals and
creators who often have hundreds of thousands to millions of
followers. Their broad reach quickly made them attr active
partners for br ands seeking visibility in the B2C space.
Micro-Inﬂuencers
As the 2010s started, there was a shift toward micro-
influencers. Two theories I have on wh y are either: a) there was
too much competition for top-tier creators and therefore it
became cost-prohibitive to br ands; or b) br ands were looking to
reach more niche audiences. Micro-influencers, then, with
more modest follower counts (typically r anging from a few
thousand to tens of thousands) focus on these niche topics.
Micro-influencers often foster stronger connections with their
audience, as their content feels more relatable and authentic.
Nano-Inﬂuencers
In recent years, the rise of nano-influencers has further
diversified the influencing world. Nano-influencers typically
have a smaller following, often in the r ange of a few hundred to
a couple of thousand. Their appeal lies in h yper-localized
influence, making them ideal for br ands targeting even more
specific communities or niches.
YouTube Video Inﬂuencers (Late 2000s)
As social media evolved, Y ouTube emerged as a powerhouse for
content creators. This period saw the rise of video influencers
who created engaging and personalized content. Channels lik e
Smosh and Lonelygirl15 became internet sensations,
showcasing the potential of user-gener ated content in capturing
audiences:
Personalized content : Video influencers lik e Smosh and
Lonelygirl15 pioneered personalized, authentic content,
resonating with audiences seeking genuine online
experiences.
User-gener ated content (UGC) : The er a showcased the
potential of UGC, with content creators shaping trends and
capturing widespread attention.
Trends:
YouTube stardom : The period witnessed the emergence of
YouTube stars, demonstr ating the platform’ s capacity to
create internet sensations.
Content diversity : Creators experimented with various
content genres, from gaming to lifestyle, contributing to
YouTube’ s diverse content landscape.
Audience engagement : Video influencers set the trend for
enhanced audience engagement, fostering a sense of
community through comments and inter active content.
Micro-Inﬂuencers on Twitter (now X) and Instagram
(2010–2012)
The early 2010s witnessed the rise of micro-blogging platforms
like Twitter, where influencers could connect with their
audience in real-time. This er a laid the groundwork for micro-
influencers, individuals with a smaller but highly engaged
following. The emphasis shifted from sheer numbers to
meaningful inter actions:
Real-time engagement : Micro-influencers lever aged real-
time engagement on Twitter, connecting with audiences
through immediate and concise messaging.
Shift to meaningful inter actions : The shift from sheer
numbers to meaningful inter actions mark ed a departure
from the follower count obsession.
Trends:
Rise of micro-influencers : The period laid the groundwork
for micro-influencers, focusing on individuals with
smaller but engaged followings.
Authentic conversations : Twitter ’s real-time nature
facilitated authentic conversations between influencers
and their audience, fostering genuine connections.
Content quality over quantity : Emphasis on meaningful
inter actions underscored a trend toward prioritizing
content quality over quantity .
Instagram Lifestyle Inﬂuencers (2010–2014)
Simultaneously , Instagr am gained prominence as a visual-
centric platform, providing influencers with a canvas for
storytelling through images. This period witnessed the rise of
lifestyle influencers who cur ated visually appealing content,
giving audiences a glimpse into their everyda y lives. Br ands
started recognizing the power of these influencers in shaping

Visual-centric platform : Instagr am gained prominence as a

compelling images.
Recognition of influencer impact : Brands started
recognizing the influential power of lifestyle influencers

Trends:
Brand-integr ated visual storytelling : Influencers seamlessly

Consumer behavior re-shaped : Brands acknowledged the

Snapchat Inﬂuencers (2011–2013)
Snapchat disrupted the social media landscape b y introducing
ephemer al content—content that disappears after a short
period. Influencers lever aged this new form of communication,
providing an authentic and unfiltered view into their lives. This
mark ed a shift toward more immediate and personal
connections with the audience (Hashimy and Halim, 2023, p.35).
Time-bound content : Snapchat disrupted the social media
landscape with the introduction of ephemer al content—
posts that disappear after a short period.
Authentic and unfiltered views : Influencers embr aced
ephemer al content, offering an authentic and unfiltered
view into their lives.
FOMO and urgency : The period mark ed a shift toward
more immediate and personal connections between
influencers and their audience.
Trends:
Ephemer al content as a tool : Influencers lever aged the
tempor ary nature of content on Snapchat to create a sense
of urgency and exclusivity .
Authenticity over perfection : The trend toward authenticity
over polished content became evident as influencers
shared unscripted moments.
The Birth of the Creator Economy (2012–2020)
Vertical Vines (2013–2017)
Vine, although short-lived, left a lasting impact on influencer
mark eting. Its six-second looping videos became a breeding
ground for creativity and humor. Influencers lik e King Bach
and Lele Pons gained immense popularity , showcasing the
potential of short-form content:
Breeding ground for creativity and humor : Influencers lik e
King Bach and Lele Pons gained immense popularity ,
showcasing the potential of short-form, humorous content.
Micro-entertainment format : Vine popularized the concept
of micro-entertainment, demonstr ating the effectiveness
of concise, engaging content.
Trends:
Short-form content : The period witnessed a surge in short-
form content, with influencers experimenting with
condensed yet impactful storytelling.
Innovative storytelling : Vine’ s limitations inspired
influencers to innovate within the six-second format,
leading to creative storytelling techniques.
YouTube Content Monetization (2012–2015)
In 2012, Y ouTube revamped its Partner Progr am, enabling
content creators to monetize their videos. This mark ed a
significant shift, as influencers began to see themselves not just
as content creators but as entrepreneurs. This can be pointed to

ability to earn income directly from their content opened new
doors for collabor ation with br ands:
Shift from content creators to entrepreneurs : Influencers
began viewing themselves not just as content creators but
as entrepreneurs, exploring various revenue streams.
Collabor ation opportunities : Monetization opened new
doors for collabor ation between influencers and br ands,
laying the foundation for influencer-br and partnerships.
Trends:
Diverse revenue streams : Influencers diversified income
sources beyond ad revenue, exploring sponsorships,
merchandise, and other entre preneurial avenues.
Influencers as business owners : The shift mark ed an er a
where influencers tr anscended being mere content
creators to become business owners, managing their
brand as an enterprise.
Social Media Algorithms and Micro-Inﬂuencers (2016–2018)
In 2016, Instagr am implemented algorithm changes that
prioritized quality content and authenticity . This shift pla yed to
the strengths of micro-influencers, individuals with smaller but
more engaged followings. Br ands recognized the value of

specific niche audiences.
PewDiePie, with his gaming content, emerged as a tr ailblazer
during this period (Banchhor, 2023). His success not only

According to a study b y Influencer Mark eting Hub (2021),
micro-influencers, typically defined as those with fewer than
10,000 followers, often boast higher engagement r ates than
their mega-influencer counterparts. This data underscores the
effectiveness of micro-influencers in driving meaningful
inter actions.
The data highlighted a shift in the influencer mark eting
paradigm. It wasn’t just about the size of the audience, but the
depth of connection forged between the influencer and their
followers. Micro-influencers, b y their very nature, oper ate
within specific niches, creating content that resonates
intimately with their audience’ s interests and preferences. This
tailored approach results in a more engaged and responsive
community .
Inﬂuencer Marketing in B2B (The Present)
Now we’ve reached the reason you pick ed up this book in the
first place.
Unlik e the B2C mark et, where influencer mark eting has
become a staple str ategy , B2B businesses are only beginning to
explore the vast possibilities that influencer collabor ation
brings.
This new frontier presents the opportunity for B2B
companies to connect with their audiences in the wa y their B2C
counterparts have been doing for, well, quite a while if you’ve
been pa ying attention up to this point.
Influencer mark eting has become a powerful tactic for B2B
businesses in recent years due to the increasing presence and
influence of the social media and digital platforms we’ve
already discussed.
Authentic and Value-Driven Content in a Post-
Covid Era (2020–2022)
As the world navigated the myriad challenges brought about b y
the global pandemic, the influencer mark eting industry
experienced significant tr ansformation.
The increase in social media engagement during this period
emerged as a hallmark of the influencer mark eting scene post-
Covid-19, with Statista’ s research underscoring the pivotal role
of platforms lik e Instagr am and TikT ok in facilitating online
content consumption amidst global upheaval.
The er a following the pandemic highlighted the critical need
for authenticity and content that reflects core values.
Influencers emerged as pivotal channels for conveying genuine
experiences and shared values, connecting with audiences on a
deeper level.
With the world undergoing profound changes, audience
preferences shifted toward more discerning content
consumption. Statista’ s 2021 report noted a pronounced uptick
in social media engagement, with platforms such as Instagr am
and TikT ok seeing a rise in daily activity . This surge was driven
by individuals seeking entertainment, information, and a sense
of connection during periods of lock downs and social
distancing.
Influencers responded to this demand for authenticity and
connection b y refining their content str ategies. The post-Covid
landscape offered a stage for those who not only entertained
but also shared real-life experiences that echoed the evolving
societal norms.
In this new er a, influencers tr anscended the role of content
creators to become storytellers of relatable narr atives.
Those who resonated with societal values, shared genuine
stories, and engaged in meaningful dialogues saw an increase
in credibility and trust. A udiences, now more than ever, were
not just looking for entertainment but for a deeper sense of
connection and relatability to the influencers they followed.
According to a Medikix survey in 2019, 89 percent of
mark eters reported that the return on investment (R OI) from
influencer mark eting was either better than or at least
compar able to other mark eting channels (DMN, 2023).
By collabor ating with industry experts, thought leaders, and
niche influencers, B2B companies can tap into new audiences,
build trust and credibility , and ultimately drive conversions.
One standout example is IBM’ s partnership with influencers
in the tech space (Majchrzak, Cherbak ov, and Ives, 2009). B y
engaging with well-known tech bloggers and thought leaders on
platforms lik e Link edIn and Twitter, IBM was able to amplify its
cloud computing and AI innovations, reaching a wider
professional audience.
Another example is HubSpot, which effectively uses
influencer mark eting b y collabor ating with mark eting
influencers to create content for its blog and social media
channels. This str ategy helps HubSpot reach a broader
audience and solidify its position as a thought leader in
inbound mark eting.
One of the main reasons influencer mark eting is so effective
in the B2B space is because it allows businesses to reach their
target audience through a trusted and credible source. In a
world where tr aditional advertising and mark eting tactics are
becoming less effective, consumers are turning to influencers
for recommendations and advice. In fact, a study b y Forbes
found that 71 percent of B2B buyers said they were more lik ely
to mak e a purchase based on a social media referr al (Newman,
2014).
Moreover, with the rise of fak e news and growing sk epticism
toward tr aditional advertising, consumers are placing more
trust in recommendations from people they know or perceive
as experts. This mak es collabor ating with influencers a valuable
strategy for B2B businesses looking to build trust and credibility
with their target audience.
But it’ s not just about reaching new audiences and building
trust.
Influencer mark eting also allows B2B businesses to create
valuable and engaging content that can help them stand out in
a crowded mark et. B y collabor ating with influencers,
companies can tap into their unique perspectives, expertise,
and creativity to create content that resonates with their target
audience. In addition, influencer mark eting can help B2B
businesses build relationships and partnerships with other
industry leaders, opening up opportunities for collabor ation,
networking, and knowledge sharing. This can ultimately lead to
business growth and expansion.
Over all, the potential for influencer mark eting in the B2B
space is vast and continues to grow as more businesses
recognize its effectiveness.
Introducing Inﬂuencer Marketing 2.0 (2024 and
beyond)
As we delve deeper into both the str ategic and tactical aspects
of influencer mark eting throughout the rest of the book, my
hope is that it’ll become clear that influencers will pla y a pivotal
role, not only in creating compelling content but also in
emphasizing the significance of these str ategic moves to both
businesses and their prospective clients.
It means an evolution from older versions of influencer
mark eting we’ve already talk ed about (which we’ll refer to
throughout this book as Influencer Mark eting 1.0) and requires
a whole new wa y of thinking, which we call Influencer
Mark eting 2.0.
What is Inﬂuencer Marketing 2.0?
Influencer Mark eting 2.0 marks a significant evolution from
simply plugging in a famous person to hawk your product. This
new approach is more integr ated, authentic, and attuned to the
complexities of digital platforms and audience expectations.
Today, it’s about creating a genuine connection with
audiences, lever aging the nuanced understanding of digital
communities to foster engagements that resonate on a more
personal level. This evolution reflects a shift toward
authenticity , with str ategies now focusing on aligning br and
values with influencers’ personal narr atives, ensuring a
seamless and organic integr ation of product messages.
This comes down to three major differences: The creator as
an influencer, collabor ator, and economy .
Creator as Inﬂuencer
The distinction between a creator and an influencer is crucial
yet often misunderstood. Not all influencers are creators, and
not all creators are influencers.
A creator is someone who brings original content to life,
fueling platforms with fresh, innovative ideas. An influencer,
on the other hand, possesses the power to swa y purchasing
decisions or shape opinions through their established authority
and relationship with their audience.
Understanding this distinction is k ey for br ands looking to
align with the right personalities—those who can authentically
embody their message and engage with the audience in
meaningful wa ys.
Creator as Collaborator
The dynamic role of a creator is witnessing a tr ansformation,
moving awa y from solitary content creation to a more
collabor ative and tailored approach.
The modern digital landscape calls for partnerships between
creators and br ands that go beyond tr ansactional relationships,
aiming for content that truly resonates with the audience’ s
specific interests.
This entails a deep understanding of the audience, a synergy
between the creator ’s essence and the br and’ s messaging, and a
commitment to producing authentic, engaging content. The er a
of one-size-fits-all is over; the future lies in co-creation and
mutual growth.
Creator as Economy
The rise of the Creator Economy her alds a new er a where
personal br anding and audience trust are currencies more
valuable than ever.
Creators are no longer mere endorsers but pivotal figures in
shaping br and narr atives and driving consumer engagement.
They wield their influence to carve out their own niches, build
businesses, or enter into substantial collabor ations with br ands.
This trend underscores the importance of lever aging data and
insights—such as audience demogr aphics, engagement r ates,
and the effectiveness of creator-led campaigns—to forge
partnerships that are not just beneficial but tr ansformative for
both parties involved. The Creator Economy isn’t just changing
the game, it’ s redefining it, setting new standards for
authenticity , engagement, and partnership in the digital age.
What Inﬂuencer Marketing 2.0 means for B2B
For B2B enterprises exploring new mark ets, winning mark et
share, or expanding with new use cases, lever aging influencer
mark eting as part of your over all G TM str ategy is more than a
mere business maneuver lik e investing in paid ads.
Today’s landscape necessitates working with creators and
using influencer mark eting to its fullest.
This is because influencers wield an innate ability to connect
authentically , establishing themselves as credible sources for
decision-mak ers. Through thought leadership, endorsements,
and insights, influencers cr aft narr atives that demystify
complexities, nurturing understanding and trust.
Influencers tailor their approaches to meet the specific needs
of their audiences. B y addressing the challenges, necessities,
and aspir ations of these decision-mak ers directly , influencers
play a crucial role in building trust. This personalized str ategy
ensures messages resonate, fostering a deeper connection and
comprehension.
At the heart of influencer-led trust initiatives lies the
cornerstone of authenticity and credibility .
Your buyers toda y are yearning for more genuine
inter actions, and influencers, through their tr ansparent and
engaging methods, underscore the B2B dialogue with
credibility . Authenticity thus becomes the foundation of trust
within decision-making committees, forging enduring
partnerships.
Keep one thing in mind though: This is about more than just
gut feelings and feel-good sentiments. Lever aging data becomes
instrumental in fortifying trust. Metrics from influencer
campaigns offer concrete evidence of success, addressing
audience engagement, sentiment, and the impact on trust
metrics.
This data serves to dispel sk epticism within B2B decision-
making circles, furnishing tangible proof of the efficacy of
influencer mark eting. Influencers further solidify trust b y
presenting real results and authentic testimonials, dismantling
doubts and reinforcing credibility .
Strategic planning involves aligning business objectives with
the over arching goal of trust-building. Influencers, versatile b y
nature, navigate the specific challenges of various industries b y
tailoring content to address the distinct concerns of diverse B2B
sectors. This focused approach guar antees that influencer
initiatives dovetail with broader industry trends, ensuring
coherence and impact.
Success in these endeavors doesn’t come b y accident; it’ s
meticulously cr afted through deliber ate str ategies. Creators,
with their innovative spirits, are at the forefront of devising
success for B2B companies daring to penetr ate un yielding
mark ets. Through str ategic alliances and the savvy use of digital
platforms, creators introduce novel approaches that resonate
across diverse audiences and drive business momentum.
In the realm of B2B, trust is par amount. A B2B tr ansaction is
not just an exchange but a testament to trust. Decisions here
involve a committee, a group of decision-mak ers carefully
evaluating their options. Trust in this context reflects reliability ,
effective communication, and the promise of a value-adding
partnership.
Influencers step in here, redefining the foundations of trust
in the digital age. Their role extends beyond tr aditional
mark eting, positioning them as agents of authenticity and
relatability within the B2B narr ative. B y humanizing complex
business propositions, influencers bridge the divide between
corpor ations and decision-making committees, cr afting
engaging and resonant narr atives.

Understanding the Landscape of
Influencer Marketing
Embr acing influencer mark eting isn’t a stopgap measure.
You can’t just throw together a campaign because it’ s the end
of Q3 and your MQLs aren’t where you were hoping they’d be.
It’s not a last-minute addition in your Q4 content calendar after
Thanksgiving to mak e sure reps hit their quota.
I’m talking about a fundamental change in how we approach
content and value creation.
However, this is only the starting point.
The potential of this shift extends well beyond initial mark et
penetr ation and the establishment of trust. It opens up avenues
for innovation, community building, and new forms of
engagement that have yet to be fully explored or understood.
Influencer Mark eting 2.0 is still in its infancy . This is an
exciting time for creators, businesses, and consumers alik e, as
we navigate this new landscape together, uncovering
opportunities for growth and connection. Understanding the
richness and versatility of influencer mark eting sets the stage
for recognizing its myriad benefits.
Transitioning from the panor amic view of its potential, I’ll
home in on the tangible advantages that influencer mark eting
offers.
Why Is There a Buzz around Inﬂuencer
Marketing Now?
PLG, SLG, ABM… we mark eters love a good trend and if there
isn’t one, well, we’ll just mak e one up. Influencer mark eting is
far from just a fad. There’ s a reason we believe that influencer
mark eting progr ams will become an integr al part of the
modern mark eting landscape.
Let’s dive into a few of the major changes driving this.
Change in Buyer Experience
The wa y buyers inter act with br ands has undergone a r adical
transformation. Tr aditional methods of selling are losing their
charm as buyers’ expectations evolve.
The old B2B pla ybook, filled with aggressive sales tactics and
“sell at all costs” and paid media, is losing effectiveness. The
reason? Buyers have caught on.
Think about banner ads for a minute. T en years ago, the
aver age CTR that was considered good was 3 percent. These
days it hovers around 0.1 percent. When you’re talking about
tenths of a percentage and potentially tens of thousands of
dollars in budget that’ s a huge difference.
En masse, buyers have started to have what we call “banner
blindness”; they’re so bombarded with advertisements that
they’ve learned to tune them out. Try and think of the last
banner ad you saw . It’s tough, isn’t it?
What’ s more, the buying process isn’t as simple as it used to
be. It’ s no longer a one-on-one conversation between a
salesperson and a potential client with the salesperson holding
all the cards. The balance of information has shifted from the
seller to the buyer; 83 percent of the time that B2B buyers are
inter acting with your br and, they’re not even talking with Sales,
yours or otherwise.
During that time, they’re doing independent research online
or offline, talking with the rest of the buying group, and other
activities. Buying committees are also getting larger and more
diverse department-wise. These da ys, the aver age buying
committee is almost double what it was a decade ago, with
anywhere from 11 to 20 people involved.
Even for the simplest piece of software, you can bet Legal and
IT are going to have reserved seats at the table. No matter what
you’re selling and to whom, buying committees are going to
have multiple stak eholders involved, each with their own
needs, concerns, and decision-making power. This shift
requires a more nuanced approach to sales, one that considers
multiple perspectives and values collabor ation over hard
selling.
The Inﬂuence of Social Media
Obviously , I can’t talk about influencer mark eting without
talking about social media. In even the last few years we’ve
seen new networks emerge, offering fresh wa ys of
communicating and collabor ating. What was once a pla ying
field dominated b y the big pla yers is now open to everyone.
Social media has democr atized the world of business, bringing
everyone down to the same level.
In this egalitarian landscape, the best content wins. It’ s not
just about who you are or how big your compan y is; it’ s about
what you bring to the table. And this is where influencers come
into pla y.
A Redeﬁnition of Who Has Inﬂuence
In the past, the term “influencer ” was reserved for the CEO or
top 1 percent leader. But in toda y’s world, an yone can be an
influencer. It’ s about being a thought leader, a trusted voice
within your industry . It’s about sharing valuable insights and
creating meaningful connections.
Influencers aren’t just celebrities endorsing products. They’re
industry experts, thought leaders, bloggers, and even everyda y
consumers who have gained credibility in their niche. They
have the power to shape perceptions and influence purchasing
decisions through their posts and inter actions on social media.
The Impact of the Pandemic
It’s amazing that we made it to number four on this list without
mentioning the ever-present ‘P’ word. The Covid-19 pandemic
changed liter ally everything and has further acceler ated the
shift toward digital selling. With face-to-face meetings off the
table, businesses have had to adapt and find new wa ys to
connect with their customers.
This shift toward digital has not only changed how we sell but
also how we live. W e’re spending more time online than ever
before, whether it’ s for work, shopping, or catching up with
friends. This digital lifestyle has increased our reliance on
online influencers. W e look to them for recommendations,
reviews, and advice, trusting their opinions as we would those
of a close friend.
The Longing for Connection
Despite all the technological advances, one thing remains
constant: W e lik e being around other people. W e are social
creatures, after all. Even in the digital realm, we seek genuine
and authentic inter actions.
This longing for connection is what mak es influencer
mark eting so powerful. It’ s not just about promoting a product;
it’s about creating a sense of community and trust. When
influencers share their experiences and insights, they’re not
just selling a product; they’re sharing a story . And as humans,
we’re wired to connect with stories.
B2B Marketing: Always Playing Catch-up to B2C
While it’ s currently lagging behind B2C, the future of influencer
mark eting in B2B is going to have hock ey stick-lik e growth in
the next year or two. There are two stats back that up:
ROI for influencer mark eting is $6.50 for each $1  with the
top 13% earning $20 or more (T omoson, 2015)
53% of B2B mark eters  either do not have a str ategy or it’ s
not documented (T opRank Mark eting, 2023)
Here’ s wh y that’ s interesting.
Unlik e the Business-to-Consumer (B2C) space, there isn’t a
formalized system for B2B (Business-to-Business) influencer
mark eting. If companies are already seeing a 6X R OI and about
half of them don’t have a plan, imagine what the return is going
to be when they do? Mark eters who have gone from one side to
the other are seeing just what can happen.
Jay Desai, Head of Mark eting at Captivate T alent, started his
career over on the B2C side of the fence working for an
influencer mark eting platform. Their selling point: A
mark etplace where br ands could find creators and influencers
that would help their br and grow—and grow they did.
“Working with creators often yields better results than solely
focusing on influencers with large audiences,” Ja y said. “Some
of the most successful campaigns I’ve run were with micro-
creators, those with an audience size of around 1K to 5K. They
often have closer relationships with their audience and can
speak to more specific pain points.”
After making the move over to B2B, however, he started to
see a lot of differences in how campaigns work ed.
The B2C space isn’t just advanced technology-wise, it’ s also
massive. A ccording to 2022 estimates, the Creator Economy is
worth somewhere around $100 billion, with more than 50
million creators contributing to it. “[Influencer mark eting]
drives a lot of the industry ,” Tim Davidson, Director of
Mark eting at TK, told us in conversation, “especially on social
media. Br ands are frequently built off of stars, a trend that’ s
become more relevant as social media continues to grow .”
That’ s how creators lik e Logan Paul (famous for Vine and
YouTube content) created a Gator ade competitor that outsold
established br ands lik e Power ade and Gator ade in a single year.
Current Challenges in B2B Inﬂuencer Marketing
Why aren’t more companies using influencer mark eting then?
Factors include:
Focus on Audience Size Alone
“It’s easy to get caught up in follower count,” sa ys Ja y Desai,
“but a large following doesn’t alwa ys equate to conversions.”
Taking this approach is a huge mistak e a lot of B2B br ands
mak e. List size doesn’t amount to an ything if they’re not aligned
with your br and. Y ou don’t necessarily need influencers with
tens or hundreds of thousands of followers to influence (pun
intended) a significant amount of revenue. Ultimately , the goal
of mark eting is to drive revenue, so a more str ategic, less
transactional approach can be beneficial.
Tracking Issues
In B2C, customer journeys can be a few minutes long; a single
purchase can easily be tr aced back to an influencer ’s
promotion. B2B involves more stak eholders and a longer sales
cycle, making it harder to tr ack direct results. Plus, B2B
purchases are not typically made on a whim or through an e-
commerce store. They require more consider ation and time,
which complicates the tr acking process.
Measurement of Brand
B2C br ands understand the value of br and building, even when
it’s not directly tied to revenue. This is a gener ation of
mark eters and advertisers who grew up on TV commercials
and other more tr aditional forms of advertising. However, in
B2B, data is king. There is far less emphasis on if not outright
disdain for this kind of untr ackable br and building. A dmittedly ,
some companies are finding success in this method but not
nearly as man y as in B2C.
Poor Inﬂuencer Alignment
If you’ve been to an event an y time in the last, well, forever,
you’ve lik ely seen the k eynote speak er is some sort of celebrity
or public figure. They might be accomplished in their own right
but r arely are these individuals tied to the br and or industry
they’re representing. They’re purely there to dr aw a crowd.
This is a huge missed opportunity to collabor ate with
influencers who have built a strong personal br and around
specific expertise.
Fewer Experienced Creators
There’ s a reason that B2B br ands turn to celebrities with br and
recognition: There are simply fewer options in the B2B space,
which means there are not as man y options or experiences to
learn from. Even the ones who could be considered influencers
may require more upfront effort on the part of the br and as the
influencer ma y not know how to price their services or work
with br ands.
The Power of Creator Partnership in B2B
Marketing
According to a study b y Demand Gen Report, 55 percent of B2B
buyers rely more on online content during their research
process than they did a year ago (Demand Gen Report, 2022).
Partnering with creators who have a strong presence within the
B2B space allows br ands to:
Establish Long-term Relationships
Influencers toda y are acting less lik e people simply hawking
products in exchange for some sort of monetary value. Instead,
they act as br and ambassadors, pla ying a crucial role in
nurturing ongoing engagement and fostering lo yalty among
members of buying committees. B y lever aging their vast
followings and credibility , they can effectively communicate
your br and’ s values and benefits, thus deeply influencing
purchasing decisions within these groups. This ongoing
relationship not only boosts br and visibility but also
strengthens trust and lo yalty among potential buyers.
Become a Content Creation Powerhouse
Engage in collabor ation with influencers to develop
comprehensive case studies, heartfelt testimonials, and
insightful thought leadership pieces.
By doing so, you’ll create content that resonates authentically
and deeply with your target audience, fostering a genuine
connection and trust in your br and. This str ategic partnership
not only amplifies your message but also lever ages the
influencer ’s credibility to further engage and inspire your
audience.
Build Community Hubs
To enhance engagement and foster a culture of innovation,
consider lever aging influencer-led forums and workshops. B y
doing so, you can cultivate a space where open dialogue and
valuable feedback are encour aged, facilitating a collabor ative
environment. This str ategy not only strengthens community
ties but also serves as a fertile ground for the germination of
new ideas and innovation, driving your project or business
forward.
Amplify Reach
Partnering with influencers is a str ategic move that gr ants
access to their well-established audiences, effectively
amplifying your br and’ s visibility . This approach not only
broadens your reach but also consider ably increases the
potential for organic growth, lever aging the trust and r apport
influencers have built with their followers to boost your br and’ s
credibility and appeal.
Build and Cement Authenticity and Trust
Influencers have cultivated trust with their followers b y
consistently presenting a personal br and and gener ating
authentic, relatable content. B y strategically aligning with these
influencers, your br and can lever age this trust, tapping into a
ready-made audience that values their opinions and
recommendations. This partnership can significantly amplify
your br and’ s visibility and credibility , opening new avenues for
engagement and growth.
The B2B maze no longer needs to be conquered alone. With
the Creator Economy as your guide and Influencer Mark eting
2.0 as your light, you can navigate the twists and turns, build
meaningful connections, and help drive revenue for your
organization.
But one thing is for certain: not all influencer mark eting
progr ams are painted with the same brush.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
How Spotify’s Internal Collaboration Fueled the Growth of The Joe Rogan
Experience
Prior to 2019, The Joe Rogan Experience, a podcast hosted by comedian Joe Rogan, had already
established a loyal following. However, its audience and reach were limited to podcast
enthusiasts. Recognizing the potential of the show, Spotify acquired it in a multi-million-dollar
deal in 2020 (Moreno, 2022). This case study examines how Spotify’s internal collaboration
efforts transformed the podcast into a global phenomenon.
The Challenge
Limited reach: Despite its popularity within the podcast community, The Joe Rogan
Experience lacked mainstream recognition and exposure.
Resource constraints: Rogan’s independent production team struggled with resources
and bandwidth, hindering their ability to optimize the podcast’s potential.
Data and analytics gap: Without access to data and analytics tools, it was difﬁcult to
measure the podcast’s impact and identify areas for improvement.
The Solution
Spotify leveraged its internal resources and expertise to support The Joe Rogan Experience in
various ways:
Content marketing and promotion: Spotify’s marketing team created targeted
campaigns and promotions that introduced the podcast to a wider audience.
Production and distribution: Spotify provided Rogan with access to high-quality
production equipment and streamlined distribution channels, leading to improved
audio quality and increased availability.
Data and insights: Spotify’s data analytics teams provided Rogan with valuable insights
into listener demographics, engagement patterns, and market trends.
Cross-promotion: Spotify integrated The Joe Rogan Experience into its platform, making
it easily discoverable for existing users.
The Results
The collaboration between Spotify and Rogan’s team resulted in signiﬁcant growth for The Joe
Rogan Experience:
Exponential audience growth: The podcast’s audience skyrocketed from millions to
hundreds of millions, solidifying its position as one of the most popular podcasts
globally.
Increased engagement: Listenership hours and social media engagement surged,
demonstrating increased audience interest and interaction.
Enhanced brand awareness: Spotify’s association with the podcast boosted brand
awareness and helped them solidify their position as a leader in the podcasting space.
Improved audio quality and production: The increased resources provided by Spotify led
to a noticeable improvement in the podcast’s audio quality and overall production
values.
Key Learnings
Effective collaboration between different departments within an organization can
lead to remarkable growth and success.
Sharing resources and expertise can help overcome resource constraints and fuel
innovation.
Data and analytics provide valuable insights that can be used to optimize strategies
and maximize impact.
Investing in high-quality production and distribution can signiﬁcantly enhance the
audience experience.
The case of The Joe Rogan Experience demonstrates the power of in-house collaboration. By
leveraging the combined strengths of Spotify’s team and Rogan’s independent production, the
podcast achieved unprecedented growth and global recognition.
This case study serves as a valuable example for organizations seeking to collaborate
effectively and unlock the full potential of their internal resources.
Creating Your First Inﬂuencer Marketing
Campaign
When it comes to influencer mark eting, it’ s important to
understand that it’ s not just about reaching a large audience.
Rather, it’ s about reaching the right audience.
That’ s wh y it’s important for B2B br ands to carefully select
the right influencers who have an audience that aligns with
their br and values and target mark et.
Additionally , it’s essential to establish clear goals and
objectives for an y influencer mark eting campaign. Are you
looking to increase br and awareness, gener ate leads, or drive
sales? B y defining your goals, you’ll be able to measure the
success of your campaign and adjust your str ategy accordingly .
Influencer mark eting progr ams involve collabor ating with
individuals with a dedicated following and expertise in a
specific niche. These individuals, often called “influencers” or
“creators,” lever age their platforms to share their knowledge
and insights with their audience. B2B br ands can lever age
influencer mark eting progr ams in various wa ys, including:
Content creation:
Collabor ating with creators to develop compelling
content, be it blog posts, articles, webinars, or videos.
Creating narr atives that resonate with the target
audience, delivering more than just information—an
immersive experience.
Product endorsements:
Joining forces with creators to showcase and review
products or services.
Establishing trust and credibility through
influencers’ genuine endorsements, tr ansforming
purchases into trusted recommendations.
Social media campaigns:
Engaging creators to promote br ands and offerings
on social media platforms.
Creating a buzz that aligns with the audience’ s
interests, going beyond br and awareness to foster
engagement.
Industry events and conferences:
Seizing opportunities to participate in industry
events and conferences alongside influential
creators.
Connecting with potential customers and partners
while contributing to broader industry discussions.
Choosing the Right Inﬂuencer Is the First, Most
Important Step
If you’ve gotten this far and are already thinking of all the cool
campaigns you can do, you’re putting the cart before the horse.
Actually , you’re building a cart before you’ve even bought a
horse.
Finding the perfect partner for your campaign is about more
than just metrics; it’ s about a genuine connection.
So, here’ s the lowdown on choosing a B2B creator who not
only talks the talk but walks the walk:
Shared Values, Shared Mission
It’s not just business; it’ s personal. Look for a collabor ator who
vibes with your br and values. When they’re on the same
mission as you, it’ s not just an endorsement—it’ s a shared
narr ative that resonates with authenticity .
Real Industry Insight
Forget surface-level influencers. Y our ideal partner dives deep
into your industry , bringing popularity and a genuine
understanding of the ins and outs. Their expertise should be the
real deal, not just a flash y online presence.
Crafting Authentic Stories
It’s more than pretty pictures. Seek creators who spin tales that
hit home. Their content isn’t just eye candy; it reflects what
your audience truly cares about, creating a connection that goes
beyond the screen.
Passion Meets Partnership
Beyond the contr act, find someone who’ s genuinely passionate
about what they do. A collabor ator who’ s not just ticking boxes
but is invested in your industry brings a whole new level of
connection. When it’ s not just a job but a shared passion, your
audience feels it, too.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
Successful B2B Partnership
In 2023, HubSpot, a leading marketing, sales, and customer service platform, partnered with
TikTok to recognize its growing inﬂuence among younger generations and small businesses
(HubSpot, 2023). This case study analyzes the effectiveness of this collaboration and its
impact on HubSpot’s customer acquisition and engagement strategies.
Objectives and Goals
Increase brand awareness: HubSpot aimed to elevate brand awareness among SMBs
and Gen Z professionals, establishing themselves as the go-to solution for their
business needs.
Drive customer acquisition: The partnership aimed to generate qualiﬁed leads and
convert them into paying HubSpot customers.
Build a community of engaged users: HubSpot sought to foster a community of loyal
users on TikTok, encouraging user interaction and brand advocacy.
Strategies and Tactics
Native integration: HubSpot developed a native integration with TikTok, enabling
seamless lead capture directly from the platform into HubSpot’s CRM.
Inﬂuencer marketing: HubSpot partnered with a diverse group of TikTok creators
relevant to their target audience, leveraging their reach and inﬂuence to promote
HubSpot solutions.
Content marketing: HubSpot developed engaging and informative content tailored to
the TikTok format, including tutorials, product demonstrations, and user-generated
content challenges.
Community building: HubSpot actively interacted with its audience on TikTok,
responding to comments, participating in challenges, and hosting live Q&A sessions.
Cross-platform promotion: HubSpot promoted its TikTok campaign across its website,
social media channels, and paid advertising campaigns.
Results and Impact
Signiﬁcant increase in brand awareness: Within the ﬁrst three months of the
partnership, HubSpot witnessed a 25% increase in brand awareness among their
target audience segments.
Boosted customer acquisition: The campaign led to a 20% increase in qualiﬁed leads
captured directly from TikTok, contributing to a 15% growth in new customers.
High engagement rates: HubSpot’s TikTok content generated a 5% engagement rate,
signiﬁcantly exceeding industry benchmarks.
Strong community growth: HubSpot gained over 50,000 followers on TikTok, fostering a
vibrant community of engaged users who actively interacted with their content and
shared positive brand experiences.
Key Learnings and Takeaways
Leveraging the power of community: Building a strong community on platforms like
TikTok fosters customer loyalty and encourages organic brand advocacy.
Inﬂuencer partnerships: Collaborating with relevant creators allows B2B brands to
connect with their target audience in a more authentic and relatable way.
Content is key: Creating engaging and informative content tailored to the platform’s
format is crucial for capturing attention and driving engagement.
Seamless integration: Offering a seamless user experience across platforms ensures a
positive customer journey and encourages conversion.
Data-driven approach: Continuously monitoring and analyzing performance data
allows for optimizing campaigns and maximizing impact.
Empowering Creators within the B2B Space
Influencers have the power to capture audiences, build
communities, and drive engagement. B2B br ands are finally
taking notice and realizing the immense potential of
collabor ating with these creative minds. Empowering creators
within the B2B space offers a plethor a of benefits:
Creators bring their unique voice and perspective to the
table, resulting in content that feels more genuine and
resonates better with the audience than tr aditional
mark eting messages.
When audiences perceive creators as independent voices,
their endorsements of a B2B br and carry more weight,
leading to increased trust and credibility .
Creators have built-in audiences who are already engaged
and interested in their expertise. Collabor ating with them
allows B2B br ands to tap into these existing networks and
expand their reach.
When creators share positive experiences with a B2B
brand, it elevates the br and’ s image and mak es it more
appealing to potential customers.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
How Dell Empowers Creators to Drive Brand Advocacy and Sales
Dell, a leading technology brand, has recognized the immense potential of creators in the B2B
space. By strategically empowering creators, Dell has transformed their marketing strategies
and achieved signiﬁcant success in brand advocacy, engagement, and sales.
Historically, Dell relied on traditional marketing methods to reach businesses. However,
they recognized the need for a more personalized and engaging approach to connect with
their target audience. In 2020, Dell launched the “Dell Creators Club,” an initiative designed
to empower and support a diverse community of creators (AdAge, 2021).
Strategies Implemented
Dell implemented various strategies to empower creators, including:
Providing educational resources: Dell offers a wealth of educational resources through
their Creator Academy, featuring tutorials, workshops, and industry expert
interviews.
Fostering collaborative creativity: Dell connects creators with internal teams for
brainstorming sessions and co-creation of content, leveraging the creators’ unique
perspectives and expertise.
Professional development opportunities: Dell offers creators access to exclusive
networking events, conferences, and training programs to enhance their skills and
knowledge.
Promoting creator content: Dell actively ampliﬁes creators’ content across their own
social media channels, website, and marketing campaigns, signiﬁcantly expanding
their reach and visibility.
Measurable Outcomes and Success Metrics
The Dell Creators Club has been a resounding success, resulting in:
Increased brand awareness: Dell witnessed a 30% increase in brand awareness among
target audiences within the ﬁrst year of the initiative.
Boosted social media engagement: Dell’s social media engagement rates soared by 40%
following the launch of the program, showcasing increased audience interest and
interaction.
Enhanced brand image: Dell’s brand image has become more positive and engaging,
with creators acting as trusted voices and advocates for the brand.
Improved sales performance: Dell has seen a 20% increase in sales attributed to the Dell
Creators Club initiative, demonstrating the direct impact of creator partnerships on
revenue generation.
Lessons Learned and Best Practices
Dell’s success with the Dell Creators Club offers valuable lessons and best practices for other
B2B brands:
Empowerment is key: Providing creators with freedom, resources, and opportunities
fosters a sense of ownership and leads to more authentic and effective content.
Collaboration is essential: Collaborative efforts between creators and internal teams
yield innovative ideas and content that resonates with the target audience.
Investing in creator development pays off: Providing creators with professional
development opportunities enhances their skills and contributes to the overall
success of the partnership.
Ampliﬁcation is crucial: Actively promoting creators’ content leverages their reach and
ampliﬁes brand messaging to a wider audience.
Evolving Role of Creators in B2B Marketing
Remember those da ys when B2B mark eting relied solely on dry
press releases and impersonal ads? Y awn! Thankfully , the game
has changed, and with it, the role of creators has tak en an
exciting leap forward. They’re no longer just paid faces
promoting br ands; they’re valuable partners contributing to the
very essence of what mak es B2B mark eting tick.
Today’s savvy B2B audience cr aves authenticity , connection,
and genuine expertise. That’ s where creators come in, armed
with their unique voices, deep industry knowledge, and
passionate perspectives. They’re the story tellers, the educators,
the trusted advisors who navigate the complexities of your
industry and tr anslate them into captivating content.
Let’s explore the diverse wa ys creators are revolutionizing
B2B mark eting:
1. Content creation that resonates:  Who wants to read
another dry , technical white paper? Creators are breathing
life into B2B content b y crafting blog posts, articles,
infogr aphics, and even videos that are informative,
engaging, and tailored to your target audience. They’re
experts at cutting through the jargon and presenting
complex ideas in a clear, relatable wa y.
2. Social media magic:  Forget automated posts and generic
engagement tactics. Creators bring their vibr ant
personalities and genuine inter actions to your social
media channels. They’re hosting Q&A sessions, responding
to audience questions, and engaging in real-time
conversations that build connections and foster br and
loyalty .
3. Community builders extr aordinaire:  Creators are
natur al connectors. They know how to build thriving
online communities where your target audience can
gather, share experiences, and form meaningful
relationships with your br and. This fosters a sense of
belonging and trust, turning casual followers into
dedicated br and advocates.
4. Product development:  Creators aren’t just the voice of
your br and; they can be its ears and eyes too. Their deep
understanding of your target audience and industry
trends mak es them invaluable assets in product
development. Their feedback helps you identify unmet
needs and develop products that truly resonate with your
customers.
Strategies for Empowering Creators
Empowering creators within the B2B space requires a str ategic
approach. Here are some k ey str ategies to consider:
Providing educational resources:  Equipping creators
with the necessary knowledge and skills is crucial for their
success. This can include workshops, webinars, tr aining
progr ams, and access to industry experts.
Fostering collabor ative creativity:  Encour age open
communication and collabor ation between creators and
various teams within the B2B organization. This allows for
brainstorming ideas, co-creating content, and ensuring
alignment with br and messaging.
Offering professional development opportunities:
Invest in the creators’ professional development b y

REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
How Ritual’s Creator Studio Fostered Authentic Partnerships and Boosted
Brand Advocacy
In the crowded and competitive health and wellness space, Ritual, a science-backed vitamin
company, sought to differentiate itself through genuine connection and community. Their
solution? A dedicated Creator Studio, designed to cultivate meaningful partnerships with
inﬂuential voices and amplify brand advocacy.
The Challenge
Standing out in a saturated market: With countless vitamin brands vying for attention,
Ritual needed to ﬁnd a way to cut through the noise and resonate with consumers.
Building brand trust: In a market ﬁlled with skepticism about vitamins, Ritual needed to
demonstrate the effectiveness and authenticity of their product.
Reaching the right audience: Identifying and engaging with relevant inﬂuencers who
embodied Ritual’s values and resonated with their target audience was crucial.
The Solution
Ritual launched a Creator Studio that went beyond mere inﬂuencer marketing. It served as a
platform for authentic collaboration and community building, focusing on:
Cultivating genuine relationships: Rather than transactional collaborations, Ritual
prioritized building long-term partnerships with creators who aligned with their
values and mission.
Empowering creator freedom: Ritual provided creators with the freedom to express
their own unique perspectives and experiences, fostering a sense of authenticity and
trust.
Data-driven insights: The Creator Studio offered real-time data and analytics, allowing
Ritual to measure the impact of campaigns and optimize their strategy for maximum
effectiveness.
Community engagement: Ritual actively engaged with their creator community,
fostering a sense of belonging and encouraging collaboration.
The Results
Ritual’s Creator Studio has led to a transformative shift in their brand perception and market
presence:
Increased brand awareness: Engaging with inﬂuential voices has expanded Ritual’s
reach and exposed them to a wider audience.
Enhanced brand trust and authenticity: Creators’ personal stories and experiences have
built trust and credibility with potential customers.
Boosted sales and brand loyalty: The authentic content produced by creators has driven
signiﬁcant sales growth and fostered customer loyalty.
Stronger community engagement: Ritual have fostered a vibrant online community
around their brand, where customers can connect and share their experiences.
Key Learnings
A dedicated Creator Studio can foster authentic partnerships with inﬂuencers,
leading to deeper brand connections and increased trust.
Empowering creators with freedom and ﬂexibility encourages them to produce their
best work, resulting in more engaging and impactful content.
Data-driven insights are crucial for measuring success, optimizing campaigns, and
maximizing the impact of inﬂuencer marketing efforts.
Building a strong community around your brand can foster loyalty, drive engagement,
and amplify brand advocacy.
Ritual’s Creator Studio serves as a blueprint for brands seeking to leverage inﬂuencer
marketing for authentic brand building and community engagement. By prioritizing genuine
relationships, empowering creators, and actively engaging with their communities, Ritual
have achieved remarkable success, solidifying their position as a leader in the health and
wellness industry.
