Legalities and Ethical
Considerations
The influencer landscape glitters with opportunity for B2B.
There are endless opportunities for offering a captivating
avenue for creative expression and collabor ation.
But beneath the surface, a complex lab yrinth of regulations
awaits, woven from the intricate threads of consumer
protection and ethical mark eting pr actices. This lab yrinth,
guarded b y the F eder al Tr ade Commission (2019) presents a
unique challenge to influencers and the mark eters who work
with them, demanding a k een eye for tr ansparency and a
commitment to building trust with their audience.
One thing to k eep in mind. If it wasn’t clear already , I am not
a lawyer. I don’t pla y one on TV or Link edIn. My legal expertise
only extends to the episodes of Law & Order  I’ve watched. T alk
to your legal team if there’ s anything they require specifically—
you’ll save yourself a lot of headaches later.
With that out of the wa y, here’ s some things you should
consider.
Navigating the FTC Mineﬁeld
Any feder al agency with three letters worth its salt is alwa ys
going to have plenty of legalities and regulations to jump
through. The F eder al Tr ade Commission (FT C) guidelines are no
different and can feel lik e navigating a legal minefield. Let’ s
take a look at a pr actical roadmap for navigating these
complexities and fostering successful partnerships (Izea, 2023).
Clarity is Key
At the core of an y ethical influencer mark eting lies
transparency . The FT C mandates clear and prominent
disclosure of an y paid collabor ations, partnerships, or
endorsements. This means sa ying goodb ye to subtle hints and
hidden meanings. Instead, embr ace str aightforward terms lik e
sponsored , ad, or brand partnership  that are easily understood
by your audience.
Remember, placement matters. Don’t bury your disclosures
in hashtags, length y captions, or obscure locations. Aim for
prominent positions where viewers are lik ely to see them at a
glance. This applies to all forms of content, including static
images, captivating videos, engaging live streams, and fleeting
stories.
Finally , let go of ambiguity . Vague terms lik e collab  or thanks
don’t cut it an ymore. Be upfront and specific about the nature
of your relationship with the br and. F or video content, consider
incorpor ating the disclosure at the beginning to ensure
maximum visibility .
Organic vs. Paid
Building trust with your audience hinges on a clear distinction
between sponsored content and your genuine opinions and
experiences. Think of sponsored content as a designated space
for br and partnerships, while your organic posts remain your
authentic voice.
Visually differentiate sponsored content using relevant
hashtags lik e #ad or #sponsored. Remember, tr ansparency goes
beyond content. Disclose an y free products or gifts received
from br ands, even if you choose not to explicitly endorse them.
Furthermore, most social media platforms offer built-in
disclosure tools that influencers can utilize to further enhance
transparency . Familiarize yourself with these tools and
incorpor ate them into your workflow .
Compliance or Consequences
Ignoring the FT C guidelines is pla ying a high-stak es game with
severe consequences for both influencers and br ands. The FT C
holds the power to impose hefty financial penalties r anging
from thousands to millions of dollars. A dditionally , they ma y
require corrective actions, such as removing deceptive content
and issuing public apologies.
Beyond financial repercussions, non-compliance can
significantly damage the reputation and credibility of both
influencers and br ands. Consumers are increasingly sk eptical of
mark eting pr actices and are quick to lose trust in those who
engage in deceptive behaviors. This can lead to decreased
brand lo yalty , negative publicity , and ultimately a decline in
sales.
Building Trust Through Transparency
For br ands, partnering with influencers is a valuable
opportunity to reach new audiences and build trust. However,
this trust can be easily shattered if the influencer engages in
unethical or deceptive pr actices. B y collabor ating with
influencers who are tr ansparent and compliant with the FT C
guidelines, br ands can protect their reputation and maximize
the effectiveness of their influencer mark eting campaigns.
Legal Mineﬁelds
There’ s more than feder al litigation at stak e when it comes to
influencer collabor ations. Here, we’ll explore the three main
legal issues that can trip up even the savviest mark eters
(Affable.ai, 2023):
Material Connection Disclosure
Let’s say you’re scrolling through Instagr am and see your
favorite influencer r aving about a new beauty product. Y ou’re
tempted to rush out and buy it, but what if they didn’t disclose
that they were actually paid to promote it? This is where
“material connection disclosure” comes in. Think of it as a
transparency rule. The FT C requires influencers to clearly state
if they have a financial relationship with the br ands they
promote. This could involve being paid, receiving free products,
or even having a personal connection lik e a friendship.
Another good instance to k eep in mind is the FTX case.
Renowned celebrities lik e Tom Br ady and Gisele Bündchen
faced legal trouble for promoting the now-bankrupt
cryptocurrency exchange without explicitly disclosing their
financial ties (Hern, 2022). This lack of tr ansparency misled
consumers and resulted in lawsuits. Remember, when it comes
to influencer mark eting, honesty is k ey!
Misleading Endorsements
Ever seen an influencer promote a product they’ve never used?
Or share a staged photo to mak e their results appear
miraculous? This is a misleading endorsement, and it’ s a major
legal issue in the influencer world. Influencers must base their
endorsements on genuine experiences and avoid making
unsubstantiated claims about a product’ s performance.
Let’s tak e Shein, the fast fashion giant. They faced backlash
after organizing an influencer trip to their factories, where
influencers painted a rosy picture of their labor and
environmental pr actices. However, social media users saw
through the facade and criticized the influencers for promoting
misleading information without investigating further (NPR,
2023). This case serves as a reminder that influencers have a
responsibility to be truthful and tr ansparent in their
endorsements.
Copyright Infringement
Copyright infringement is a common pitfall for both br ands and
influencers. This occurs when you use someone else’ s creative
work, lik e a song or image, without obtaining proper
permission. Imagine creating amazing content for your
campaign, only to discover later that you’ve used cop yrighted
material without authorization. This could lead to legal action
and damage your reputation.
Remember the case of Bang Energy? This compan y faced
lawsuits from music giants lik e Warner Music and Son y Music
for using cop yrighted music in their influencer mark eting
campaigns without licenses (Brittain, 2022). This highlights the
importance of due diligence when using creative assets in your
campaigns.
Avoiding Legal Pitfalls
Like Uncle Ben alwa ys said, with great power comes great
responsibility . As a br and navigating this exciting space, legal
consider ations are crucial. Let’ s explore five k ey areas to ensure
your collabor ations are smooth, ethical, and compliant
(Lexology , 2023).
Research is King
Don’t let the follower count fool you! Before partnering with an
influencer, delve deep into their past content and br and
associations. A bad fit can spell disaster, so imagine a health
brand partnered with an influencer promoting unhealth y
habits. Ensure the agreement includes warr anties that the
influencer won’t engage in activities that could damage your
brand reputation.
Deﬁne the Scope
Clear communication is hugely important. Define the campaign
period, deliver ables, platforms, exclusivity , and pa yment terms.
Will the influencer create a series of Instagr am posts or a single
YouTube video? Will they be paid a fixed fee or earn an affiliate
commission? Be specific to avoid confusion and disputes down
the road.
IP Ownership Matters
Who owns the content created? While br ands ma y commission
works, influencers often incorpor ate third-party elements.
Define ownership and usage rights clearly to avoid legal
complications. Consider gr anting the br and permission to use
the content on their own platforms, not just on the influencer ’s
channels.
Control with Care
Balancing br and control with influencer freedom is essential.
Brands might want to restrict editing techniques, photo filters,
or content that contr adicts their values. However,
micromanagement can stifle creativity . Consider pre-approval
rights for specific elements while allowing creative freedom
within established par ameters.
Stay Legal
Laws and regulations around influencer mark eting are
evolving. K eep yourself informed about disclosure
requirements, product placement restrictions, and industry-
specific regulations. F or example, financial br ands must be
extra cautious about influencers dispensing unauthorized
investment advice.
Ethical Partnerships in the Inﬂuencer Economy
Ethical collabor ation is a bit different to legal consider ations.
It’s not doing things because otherwise you’ll get punished. It’ s

But wh y is ethical collabor ation so essential?
Building Trust and Loyalty
Ethical collabor ations are built on trust and honesty . When

Protecting Reputation and Credibility
Unethical pr actices, such as fak e endorsements or misleading

Promoting Positive Social Impact

REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
Microsoft and Headspace: Finding Zen in the Digital Age
Recognizing the challenges of a hyper-connected world, Microsoft partnered with
Headspace, a leading meditation app, to offer employees free access to mindfulness exercises
and guided meditations (Bacchus, 2021). This initiative went beyond a mere perk; it
demonstrated a genuine commitment to employee well-being and mental health. In an era
where productivity often outweighs employee wellness, Microsoft took a bold stand,
prioritizing the mental and emotional well-being of its workforce.
Empowerment Through Mindfulness
The collaboration provided Microsoft employees with the tools they needed to manage
stress, improve sleep quality, and enhance their overall well-being. By offering accessible
resources and fostering a culture of mindfulness, Microsoft empowered its employees to take
control of their mental health and create a more balanced and fulﬁlling work experience.
Positive Impact and Shared Values
The results of this partnership were remarkable. Employees reported signiﬁcant reductions in
stress levels, improved focus and attention, and a greater sense of overall well-being. This
case study highlights the positive impact that ethical collaborations can have on individuals
and organizations. By aligning with shared values and prioritizing employee well-being,
Microsoft created a win-win situation for both the company and its employees.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE
Ethical Collaboration in Action: The Ethical Fashion Initiative
The fashion industry is notorious for its unethical practices, including unfair labor conditions,
environmental degradation, and cultural appropriation. However, amidst the negativity, there
are glimmers of hope. The Ethical Fashion Initiative (EFI), a collaborative effort between
fashion brands, NGOs, and government agencies, is one such example (Fritz Energy, 2022).
This case study delves into the EFI’s mission and showcases how ethical collaboration can be a
powerful tool for positive change in the fashion industry.
Breaking Down the Barriers
The EFI was established in 2013 with the aim of promoting ethical and sustainable practices
within the fashion industry. This initiative recognizes that tackling complex issues like
exploitative labor and environmental pollution requires collaboration among various
stakeholders. By bringing together brands, NGOs, and government agencies, the EFI fosters
knowledge sharing, resource allocation, and joint action, creating a more impactful approach
to tackling industry-wide challenges.
A Collaborative Approach to Ethical Fashion
The EFI’s work is built upon three core pillars:
Raising awareness: The EFI conducts research and publishes reports that shed light on
the ethical and sustainability challenges within the industry. This information is crucial
for informing consumers, brands, and policymakers about the true cost of fast fashion
and the need for change.
Building capacity: The EFI provides training and resources to brands and
manufacturers, helping them implement ethical and sustainable practices within their
operations. This includes workshops, training programs, and access to expert advice.
Advocacy and policy change: The EFI works with policymakers and governments to
create regulations and incentives that promote ethical and sustainable practices
within the fashion industry. This includes advocating for fair labor standards,
environmental protection laws, and transparency initiatives.
Impact and Achievements
The EFI’s collaborative approach has led to signiﬁcant progress in the fashion industry. The
initiative has facilitated the development of industry-wide standards and certiﬁcations, such
as the Global Organic Textile Standard (GOTS) and the Fair Wear Foundation, which ensure
that textiles and garments are produced ethically and sustainably. Additionally, the EFI has
helped brands implement more responsible sourcing practices and improve working
conditions in their supply chains.
Challenges and Future Vision
Despite its achievements, the EFI still faces challenges. The fashion industry is incredibly
complex and entrenched in unethical practices. Changing this system requires a long-term
commitment and the continued collaboration of all stakeholders. Additionally, the EFI must
constantly adapt and evolve its strategies to address emerging challenges and ensure its
continued relevance in the ever-changing fashion landscape.
A Beacon of Hope for the Future of Fashion
The Ethical Fashion Initiative serves as a beacon of hope for a more ethical and sustainable
future of fashion. By demonstrating the power of collaboration, the EFI has inspired countless
brands, organizations, and individuals to join the movement for positive change. As the
initiative continues its work, it offers a blueprint for transforming the fashion industry into a
force for good, promoting fair labor practices, environmental responsibility, and responsible
consumption.
Best Practices for Ethical Collaborations
Ethical collabor ations are more than just buzzwords; they
represent a shift toward a more responsible and impactful wa y
of doing business. T o ensure the success of these partnerships,
it’s crucial to implement best pr actices that foster trust and
transparency between br ands, influencers, and the audience.
Establishing Clear Guidelines for Inﬂuencers
1. Brand values alignment : Clearly outline the br and’ s values
and mission, ensuring influencers understand and align
with them in their content creation.
2. Disclosure requirements : Provide explicit guidelines for
disclosure, specifying where and how influencers should
disclose sponsored content.
3. Content review process : Establish a clear process for
reviewing influencer content before publication to ensure
compliance with br and guidelines and ethical
consider ations.
4. Performance measurement : Define clear metrics and KPIs
to measure the effectiveness of the collabor ation, focusing
on positive impact and br and alignment over vanity
metrics.
5. Communication and feedback : Foster open communication
and regular feedback loops with influencers to address
concerns, maintain alignment, and ensure a positive
partnership experience.
Regular Training on Ethical Considerations in the
Creator Economy
1. Educating influencers : Provide ongoing tr aining for
influencers on ethical consider ations lik e avoiding
misleading claims, respecting diversity and inclusivity ,
and promoting responsible consumerism.
2. Staying updated on regulations : Regularly monitor and
update guidelines to comply with evolving regulations and
best pr actices within the Creator Economy .
3. Promoting tr ansparency : Encour age influencers to be
transparent about their editing processes, paid
partnerships, and use of affiliate links.
4. Empowering influencers to sa y no : Foster a culture where
influencers feel comfortable declining partnerships that
don’t align with their values or ethical principles.
5. Building a supportive community : Cultivate a supportive
community for influencers where they can share
concerns, learn from each other, and hold each other
accountable for ethical pr actices.
By implementing these best pr actices, br ands and influencers
can build a foundation of trust and tr ansparency that allows
ethical collabor ations to flourish. This not only enhances the
credibility and authenticity of influencer content but also paves
the wa y for a more responsible and impactful Creator Economy .
Remember, ethical collabor ations are a journey , not a
destination. B y continuously learning, adapting, and upholding
these best pr actices, we can create a more ethical and
sustainable influencer mark eting landscape that benefits all
stakeholders.

Using Social Listening for Your
B2B Influencer Campaigns
The most significant challenge in engaging with influencers and
the creator economy is the sheer volume of content and voices.
Identifying the right influencers and understanding their
impact amid this noise can be daunting. Plus, k eeping up with
rapidly changing trends and audience interests poses a
challenge for even the most dedicated mark eter.
Fortunately , there are social listening tools to help. These are
platforms or software that monitor social media channels and
online conversations to gather insights into audience
sentiments, discussions, trends, and br and mentions. They
analyze data from various social media platforms, blogs,
forums, and news sites to provide valuable information about
audience perceptions and preferences.
In the creator economy , influencers are k ey pla yers shaping
trends and consumer behavior. I’ve noticed that social listening
tools act as a compass, guiding br ands and mark eters to
navigate this landscape effectively . They help tap into the pulse
of online conversations, enabling a deeper understanding of
audience sentiments, preferences, and the content that
resonates most.
What Are Social Listening Tools?
At their core, social listening tools are powerful platforms that
monitor and analyze the vast expanse of social media and
online conversations. They cast a wide net, gathering data from
myriad sources—from the buzz of social media platforms to in-
depth discussions on industry forums, from the chatter of blogs
to the headlines of news sites. This wealth of data is then
distilled into actionable insights that paint a vivid picture of
audience sentiments, preferences, and behaviors.
In the context of the Creator Economy , social listening tools
serve as a wa y to separ ate the signal from the noise and
understand who is creating content that’ s resonating with your
audience and what their followers are sa ying. This is k ey to
identifying the voices that truly influence. Armed with this
knowledge, br ands can cr aft influencer str ategies that are not
only impactful but also authentic and aligned with their target
audience.
The Many, Many Beneﬁts of Using a Social
Listening Tool
The whole point of influencer mark eting is to sta y in
conversation with your audience. That means catering to their
preferences. Social listening tools have become indispensable
for br ands looking to optimize their influencer str ategies and
build authentic connections with their target audiences. Here’ s
why:
Audience Insights and Creator Alignment
Who your audience is and what they’re sa ying about you is the
most powerful information a br and can lever age. B y analyzing
social media conversations, br ands can gain a clearer
understanding of what resonates with their target audience.
From there, you can identify creators whose content aligns best
with the br and’ s messaging and values.
Look for tools that offer audience segmentation based on
interests, demogr aphics, and sentiments. This gr anular
segmentation allows br ands to pinpoint influencers who have a
strong connection with their desired audience, increasing the
likelihood of successful collabor ations.
Trend Identiﬁcation and Content Relevance
Capitalizing on trends is extremely difficult. Some events ma y
occur again (elections, holida ys, etc) while others ma y be a flash
in the pan. Social listening tools are instrumental in tr acking
both. B y monitoring relevant k eywords, hashtags, and topics,
brands can sta y ahead of the curve and adapt their influencer
content str ategies accordingly .
Real-time trend monitoring and analysis help ensure that
influencer-created content remains relevant and resonates with
current discussions. Brands can lever age these insights to guide
content themes, hashtags, and creative directions, maximizing
the impact of their influencer campaigns.
Engagement and Relationship Building
Authentic engagement is the foundation of successful
influencer partnerships. Social listening tools enable br ands to
monitor influencer conversations and engage meaningfully
with their content. B y actively participating in discussions,
showing genuine appreciation, and providing valuable
feedback, br ands can foster strong relationships with
influencers beyond tr ansactional collabor ations.
Performance Measurement
Every mark eter is familiar with the question that occurs the
second a campaign kicks off: “How did it do?” Measuring the
impact and success of influencer campaigns is crucial for
optimizing future str ategies. Social listening tools provide
comprehensive analytics that allow br ands to assess the
performance of their influencer collabor ations.
Tools can help you better analyze metrics such as audience
engagement (lik es, comments, shares), sentiment shifts, and
brand mentions tied to specific influencer campaigns. This data
helps br ands understand the R OI of their influencer
investments and mak e data-driven decisions for future
partnerships.
Adapting to Evolving Creator Trends
No br and wants to be attached to trends that seem dated. With
the social media landscape fluctuating, it can be hard to k eep
up. Br ands must be agile and adaptable in their approach to
influencer partnerships. Continuous monitoring of the creator
ecosystem through social listening tools is essential. B y sta ying
attuned to shifts in influencer behavior and audience
preferences, br ands can quickly adjust their str ategies and align
with the most impactful creators and content styles.
Choosing the Right Social Listening Tools
With myriad options available, selecting the right social
listening tool can be a daunting task.
At the same time, if I named specific technologies, I’m just
asking for this information to be outdated. So as a middle
ground, here are the features you should be looking for as
you’re searching for the right platform for your efforts.
Sentiment Analysis
Ever wanted to know exactly how your audience feels about
your br and? Sentiment analysis, a cornerstone of advanced
social listening tools, mak es this a reality . This feature allows
you to decode the complex emotional landscape of online
conversations, uncovering the true feelings and perceptions
surrounding your br and, industry , and influencers.
For instance, let’ s say you’re looking to understand how your
target audience perceives the latest product launch. Are users
impressed? Are they excited about the new features? Frustr ated
with compatibility issues? Do they not even know about it? B y
lever aging sentiment analysis, you can delve beneath the
surface of social media chatter and uncover the genuine
emotions driving the conversation.
When evaluating social listening tools, look for platforms that
offer robust sentiment analysis capabilities. The most effective
tools go beyond basic positive, negative, and neutr al
classifications, providing nuanced insights into the full
spectrum of emotions. This information will help you cr aft
influencer campaigns that truly strik e a chord with your target
audience.
Keyword Tracking
Keyword tr acking isn’t just for SEO. B y monitoring specific
keywords, phr ases, and hashtags, social listening tools enable
you to sta y attuned to the pulse of your industry and target
audience.
Let’s say you’re mark eting a software solution focused on
sustainability . By tracking k eywords related to “green
mark eting,” “eco-friendly initiatives,” and “sustainable br ands,”
you can quickly identify the most pressing topics and
influential voices shaping the conversation. This allows you to
craft influencer partnerships that align with the latest trends
and resonate with the environmentally conscious target
audience.
Be sure to prioritize platforms that offer flexible and
comprehensive k eyword tr acking capabilities. Look for tools
that allow you to monitor a wide r ange of k eywords, including
brand names, product mentions, industry jargon, and relevant
hashtags. The ability to tr ack k eyword variations, misspellings,
and related terms is also crucial, ensuring that you never miss a
critical conversation.
Finding the Right Inﬂuencers
If you’re going to be using this tool to work with influencers, the
ability to identify them is obviously one of the k ey features
you’ll want. A dvanced social listening tools don’t just look at an
audience and see how they feel about certain topics. These tools
help you pinpoint the voices that truly resonate with your
target audience.
By lever aging influencer identification features, you can
uncover the industry experts, thought leaders, and influential
voices driving the conversation around your br and, industry ,
software, etc. Moreover, top tools allow you to gain
comprehensive insights into an influencer ’s reach, engagement,
and audience demogr aphics, allowing startups to select the
most impactful partners for their campaigns.
The most effective platforms go beyond simple follower
counts, providing in-depth analysis of an influencer ’s content
quality , audience engagement, and industry expertise. Once
you’ve identified them, then it’ll be time to start building a
relationship (but that’ s for our next chapter).
Analytics and Reporting Capabilities
Ah, metrics. Every mark eter loves and hates metrics and
analytics. Nobody wants to be digging through spreadsheet
after spreadsheet. Ensure that an y tool you’re bringing on has a
comprehensive reporting feature. This will help you shed light
on the impact of your campaigns, allowing you to measure R OI,
refine your str ategies, and optimize for maximum results.
Insights such as these will provide a clear picture of the
campaign’ s performance, enabling the compan y to identify
areas for improvement and double down on the str ategies that
yield the greatest returns. Look for platforms that provide real-
time data, visual dashboards, and the ability to export reports
for stak eholder sharing. The most effective tools will also offer
benchmarking capabilities, allowing you to compare your
performance against industry standards and competitors.
Overcoming Challenges and Pitfalls: Navigating
the Labyrinth of Social Listening and Inﬂuencer
Marketing
There’ s no doubt that social listening tools are powerful.
However, as powerful as they are, they can become another
shin y waste of time, whether you use a paid tool or a free one.
From the overwhelming deluge of data to the complexities of
influencer vetting and R OI measurement, navigating these
obstacles requires a str ategic and informed approach.
Let’s tackle some of the common challenges and pitfalls that
B2B br ands ma y encounter when implementing social listening
for influencer mark eting. F ear not, for I will also provide
practical solutions and best pr actices to help you overcome
these hurdles and emerge victorious in your quest for
impactful, data-driven influencer campaigns.
Drowning in (More) Data
Yes, data is great. At the same time, too much data is
fundamentally useless. This is social media we’re talking about.
There are dozens upon dozens of conversations going on at an y
given time. With countless conversations, mentions, and
metrics to tr ack across multiple platforms, the sheer volume of
data can quickly become a daunting challenge.
Let’s use an example: A B2B software compan y eagerly
implementing social listening to inform their influencer
mark eting str ategy . As they begin monitoring br and mentions,
industry k eywords, and competitor conversations, they find
themselves drowning in a sea of data points. The constant
stream of information feels lik e an insurmountable obstacle,
hindering their ability to extr act meaningful insights and tak e
decisive action.
To overcome the challenge of data overload, it’ s essential to
approach social listening with a clear and focused str ategy .
Begin b y defining your k ey objectives and identifying the
specific metrics and conversations that align with your goals.
By narrowing your focus, you can create a more manageable
and relevant data set to analyze.
Next, lever age the power of automation and AI-driven tools to
streamline your data collection and analysis processes.
Advanced social listening platforms offer features lik e
sentiment analysis, topic clustering, and anomaly detection,
which can help you quickly identify patterns and insights
within the vast sea of data.
Finally , establish a regular cadence for reviewing and acting
upon your social listening insights. Set aside dedicated time to
analyze the data, share findings with relevant stak eholders, and
translate insights into actionable str ategies for your influencer
mark eting efforts.
Separating “Real Inﬂuencers” from Empty Vessels
The sheer number of influencers in the world has given the
term a bit of a negative connotation. As established earlier,
liter ally an yone can deem themselves an influencer and build a
following. However, that doesn’t mean that they’re an ideal
partner for your br and. As you’re searching through the sea of
potential influencer partners, distinguishing between authentic,
impactful voices and empty vessels with inflated metrics can be
a daunting task. The challenge of influencer vetting is a critical
one, as partnering with the wrong influencers can lead to
wasted resources, damaged br and reputation, and lackluster
campaign results.
To navigate the influencer vetting conundrum, don’t just look
at the numbers. Dig deeper into an influencer ’s true impact and
authenticity . Start b y analyzing the quality and relevance of an
influencer ’s content. Do their posts demonstr ate a genuine
understanding of your industry and target audience? Are they
consistently producing valuable, engaging content that aligns
with your br and values?
Next, evaluate the influencer ’s audience demogr aphics and
engagement patterns. Look for signs of genuine inter action and
community-building, r ather than empty lik es and comments.
Tools lik e social media audits and influencer mark eting
platforms can provide valuable insights into an influencer ’s
audience quality and authenticity .
It’s also essential to consider the influencer ’s reputation and
past collabor ations. Have they work ed with reputable br ands in
your industry? Do they have a tr ack record of delivering
impactful campaigns and driving meaningful results?
Conducting thorough back ground checks and seeking
references from past partners can help you mak e informed
decisions.
Measuring the Intangible Impact of Inﬂuencer
Marketing
In our current metrics-driven culture, mark eters are forced to
attribute an ything and everything they can. Unfortunately , this
is not alwa ys possible. Unlik e traditional mark eting channels
with clear-cut metrics and attribution models, the impact of
influencer collabor ations often extends beyond immediate sales
and conversions. From br and awareness and thought
leadership to long-term customer lo yalty , the true value of
influencer mark eting can be difficult to quantify . I’m not going
to go into too much detail here as we’ll be covering this topic in
a later chapter but in essence, avoiding this pitfall comes down
to a few k ey activities.
Begin b y defining clear objectives and k ey performance
indicators (KPIs) that align with your over all mark eting and
business goals. These ma y include metrics lik e brand sentiment,
website tr affic, lead gener ation, and customer engagement, in
addition to sales and revenue. Embr ace a test-and-learn
approach to influencer mark eting R OI measurement.
Continuously monitor and analyze your campaign performance
and be willing to adapt your str ategies based on data-driven
insights. Celebr ate the intangible victories alongside the
quantifiable results and recognize that the true impact of
influencer mark eting often unfolds over time.
The Ethical Landscape of Social Listening and
Inﬂuencer Marketing
With an y tool that’ s working with information that other people
put out into the world, br ands must tread carefully . Social
listening and influencer mark eting do indeed provide
unprecedented opportunities to connect with audiences, shape
perceptions, and drive business growth. But lik e Uncle Ben said,
with great power comes great responsibility .
As we delve into the realm of social listening and influencer
partnerships, it’ s crucial to acknowledge the ethical
consider ations that come into pla y. Don’t skip over this section,
otherwise you ma y find yourself in a situation where you’ll
need Chapter 13 on crisis management.
The Privacy Paradox: Balancing Insights and User
Trust
Big data offers unprecedented insights into the lives,
preferences, and behaviors of social media users. B y analyzing
vast amounts of publicly available data, br ands can gain
valuable insights into their target audiences, informing
everything from product development to mark eting str ategies.
But this mak es the duty to respect user privacy and handle
data ethically all the more important. One can barely turn on
the news toda y without seeing another data breach or privacy
scandal. If you don’t want your br and to be one of them, you’ve
got to be proactive in building and maintaining user trust.
Privacy law is a multi-headed beast and I don’t claim to be an
expert. But I did talk to a few and I insist you do the same for
handling all your mark eting data, not just that associated with
influencer mark eting.
For starters, br ands must first and foremost ensure
compliance with all relevant data protection regulations, such
as the Gener al Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) in the
European Union (Gener al Data Protection Regulation, 2016) or
the California Consumer Privacy A ct (CCP A) in the United States
(California Civil Code, 2018). This means being tr ansparent
about data collection pr actices, obtaining necessary consents,
and providing users with the ability to opt out or request the
deletion of their data.
But compliance is just the starting point. Br ands must also go
above and beyond to build trust with their audience. This
means being clear and upfront about how social listening data
is being used and ensuring that insights are lever aged in a wa y
that benefits users r ather than exploits them.
Shining a Light on Inﬂuencer Partnerships
Authenticity is currency these da ys. Consumers are increasingly
savvy and sk eptical of br and-influencer partnerships, and they
demand tr ansparency in these relationships. F ailing to disclose
sponsored content or misleading audiences about the nature of
a partnership can quickly erode trust and damage a br and’ s
reputation.
Don’t bring on “advisors” simply because they have a large
following that you want to tap into.
Maintain the integrity of your influencer partnerships and
prioritize tr ansparency at every stage of the collabor ation. This
means ensuring that influencers clearly disclose sponsored
content, using appropriate hashtags or labels to signal the
commercial nature of the relationship.
But tr ansparency goes beyond mere disclosure. Br ands
should also be open and honest about the selection process for
influencer partners, choosing collabor ators whose values and
expertise align genuinely with the br and. Influencer briefs
should provide clear guidelines on disclosure requirements and
content expectations, empowering influencers to create
authentic, compliant content.
Navigating Controversial Topics and Maintaining
Brand Integrity
If I could describe social media in one word and one word only
it would be this: Reactive. Every single post you see on social
media is the author reacting to something and then their
audience reacting to them. Be careful which reactions you step
into. Be that as it ma y, no matter how careful you are, be
prepared to navigate sensitive and controversial topics. From
social and political issues to industry-specific controversies, the
way a br and responds (or fails to respond) to these topics can
have a significant impact on their reputation and relationships
with stak eholders.
This means bringing a delicate balance of empath y,
transparency , and adherence to br and values to the forefront.
Your whole organization must be prepared to listen to and
acknowledge the concerns of their audience, while also taking a
clear stance that aligns with their core principles.
This is where having a well-defined br and voice and values
comes into pla y. By establishing clear guidelines on how to
approach sensitive topics, and tr aining social listening and
influencer mark eting teams on these protocols, br ands can
ensure a consistent and appropriate response in times of crisis.
For those times when it’ s not possible to avoid a crisis, check
out Chapter 13 to learn how to navigate such an event.
Closing Thoughts
Navigating the complex world of social listening and influencer
mark eting requires a str ategic, data-driven approach coupled
with a strong ethical foundation. As B2B mark eters, it is our
responsibility to lever age these powerful tools in a wa y that
respects user privacy , maintains tr ansparency , and upholds our
brand values.
To succeed in this endeavor, we must tak e concrete steps to
integr ate ethical consider ations into every aspect of our
influencer mark eting efforts. This means:
1. Developing and adhering to strict data privacy policies
and pr actices
2. Establishing clear guidelines for influencer partnerships
and disclosure
3. Fostering a culture of tr ansparency and open
communication with our audiences
4. Continuously monitoring and adapting our str ategies to
align with evolving best pr actices and regulations
By prioritizing these actions and sta ying attuned to the ever-
changing digital landscape, we can harness the full potential of
social listening and influencer collabor ations while mitigating
risks and building long-term, trusting relationships with our
stakeholders.
The path ahead ma y be challenging, but with a commitment
to ethical, data-driven str ategies, we can navigate this terr ain
with confidence and emerge as leaders in the B2B influencer
mark eting space. Let’ s embr ace this.

Crafting Your Influencer
Marketing Campaign
Before we get into the actual process of creating your campaign
there’ s one misconception I need to clear up.
Today, influencer mark eting in B2B is treated as a simple
awareness pla y—and that’ s a huge mistak e. If all you’re doing is
filling the top of the funnel, you’re missing out on making an
actual impact on a buying decision.
Consider these stats:
1. Online content significantly influences purchasing
decisions, with nine out of ten B2B buyers stating it has a
moder ate to major effect on their choices (B2B Leaders
Trust WBR Insights, n.d.).
2. A large portion of the buyer ’s journey is completed
digitally , with 67% of the journey now done online before
direct contact with a sales representative is made
(Worldwide Business Research, n.d.).
What do all three of these things have in common? They’re
based on a relationship between the buyer and the br and, and
like an y solid relationship, it tak es time to build. After all,
buyers have quite a journey to go from unaware to repeat
customers. If all you’re doing is creating awareness, you’re
talking at your audience, not with them.
Instead, consider this wa y of thinking about the relationship
between influencer mark eting and stage of awareness:
Awareness:  Sure, this is where our influencer pals shine,
introducing your br and to the world. But as we’ve already
covered, that’ s just the basics.
Consider ation:  As we go deeper, influencers can share
their genuine experiences, making your product relatable
and a must-have.
Decision:  When push comes to shove, a trusted
influencer ’s endorsement could be the gentle nudge
needed to tr ansform consider ation into purchase.
Loyalty and advocacy:  Post-purchase, influencers can
keep the love alive, encour aging repeat business and
turning customers into br and advocates.
Sure, in exchange for dollars or software use, an influencer
with a lot of followers will post something nice about your
brand. Their followers might listen and become aware of the
product or ma ybe buy right awa y. But are you actually building
a relationship with your audience? Nope. And that’ s exactly the
problem, as we said. Instead, br ands need to treat influencer
mark eting lik e the full-funnel activity that it is.
Businesses should adopt a series of tactical approaches
designed to engage, convert, and retain customers to lever age
influencer mark eting as a full-funnel activity effectively .
Tactical Appr oaches for Leveraging Inﬂuencer
Marketing
Step One: Set Clear Campaign Goals
Start b y determining what you aim to achieve through your
influencer mark eting campaign. Common goals include:
Increasing br and awareness: If you’re looking to r aise
visibility and reach new audiences, your primary focus
will be on metrics such as impressions, reach, and social
media mentions.
Driving website tr affic: If your goal is to direct more
people to your website, you’ll want to tr ack click-through
rates and monitor the influx of visitors from your
influencer ’s content.
Gener ating leads: If lead gener ation is your priority , you’ll
need to set up tr acking mechanisms to measure how man y
leads are being captured through influencer-promoted
landing pages or sign-up forms.
Boosting sales: If your ultimate objective is to drive sales,
you’ll need to tr ack conversions and revenue attributable
to your influencer campaign, using unique discount codes
or affiliate links.
By setting specific, measur able goals, you can better
evaluate the success of your campaign and mak e data-
driven decisions for future initiatives.
Step Two: Identify Your Target Audience
Once you’ve established your campaign goals, it’ s time to define
your target audience. Understanding who you’re trying to reach
is essential for identifying the right influencers and cr afting
content that resonates.
To create a detailed picture of your ideal audience, consider
the following factors:
Demogr aphics: A ge, gender, location, income level, and
education.
Psychogr aphics: Interests, values, attitudes, and lifestyle
preferences.
Pain points and challenges: The problems or obstacles
your target audience face that your product or service can
help solve.
Online behavior: The social media platforms they
frequent, the content they engage with, and the
influencers they follow .
Creating buyer personas, or fictional representations of
your ideal customers, can help you better understand and
target your audience. Give each persona a name, a
backstory , and specific char acteristics that reflect your
target audience’ s demogr aphics, psychogr aphics, and
behaviors.
Step Three: Identify and Reach Out to Inﬂuencers
With your goals and target audience clearly defined, you can
now begin the process of identifying and reaching out to
potential influencer partners.
Here’ s how you can find influencers:
Identify relevant influencers:  Use social media listening
tools, hashtag searches, and manual explor ation to find
influencers who align with your br and values, have an
engaged following that matches your target audience, and
produce high-quality content that resonates with your
campaign goals.
Evaluate influencer fit:  Once you’ve identified a list of
potential partners, dig deeper into their content,
engagement r ates, and audience demogr aphics to ensure
they’re a good fit for your campaign. Look for influencers
who have a genuine connection to your industry or niche
and whose content style and tone align with your br and
voice.
Craft your outreach str ategy:  Before reaching out to
influencers, develop a clear and compelling pitch that
communicates the value of partnering with your br and.
Highlight what sets your campaign apart, the creative
freedom and resources you’re offering, and the mutual
benefits of the collabor ation.
Personalize your outreach:  When contacting influencers,
take the time to personalize your messages and
demonstr ate that you’ve genuinely engaged with their
content. Mention specific posts or videos that resonated
with you and explain wh y you believe they’d be an
excellent fit for your campaign.
Be open to collabor ation:  Remember that influencer
partnerships are a two-wa y street. Be open to the
influencer ’s ideas and feedback, and work together to
create content that aligns with both your br and goals and
their unique style and audience preferences.
By following these steps and la ying a solid foundation for your
influencer mark eting campaign, you’ll be well-equipped to
create engaging, impactful content that drives results and
resonates with your target audience.
Step Four: Identify the Type of Content You’ll Create
Now that the groundwork has been laid, it’ s time to start to
identify what exactly you’ll be creating with your influencer
partners. The best wa y to accomplish this step is identifying
which stage of the funnel you’ll be looking to target as this will
inform content type.
ToFu: Generating Awareness and Cultivating
Interest
Before we dive into specifics, let’ s start with a story . I call it
“How not to do a T op-of-the-Funnel campaign.”
One time, a B2B SaaS platform approached me about an
influencer campaign they hoped we’d participate in. Their ask
wasn’t unreasonable—three posts for a fair exchange in value.
I said no. Wh y? Three posts weren’t going to accomplish their
goal of aligning their br and with the top revenue-gener ating
leaders in the industry .
So, we countered with a far more ambitious idea, including
joint presentations b y TACK and this organization, creating a co-
branded asset, and there were a few Link edIn posts as well.
Our plan was still about driving that awareness. Still, instead
of being a few posts within an ocean of content on Link edIn, it
was centered around this event series that would provide value
without too much of an ask on the audience.
And that’ s exactly what T oFu (T op of the Funnel) content
should do. It’s time to go beyond “sponcon.”
Yes, sponsored content (sponcon) has its place. However, the
early stages of broadening your br and’ s awareness demand a
more nuanced approach. At the T oFu, we have the opportunity
to redefine what influencer mark eting can be—moving beyond
mere tr ansactions to foster authentic engagements.
Influencer mark eting isn’t just a new kind of paid ad. It’ s time
we shift our focus from short-term gains to long-term
relationships.
This means finding influencers who align with your br and’ s
values and are genuinely interested in your products or
services. These influencers will natur ally create quality content
and foster meaningful discussions with their followers about
your br and. Here are some campaign ideas for T oFu.
Takeovers That Tell a Story
We’ve all seen social media tak eovers, and they’re popular for a
reason: They work.
As with an y tactic, though, the more br ands lean on it, the
noisier it becomes. Over time, it’ s become a barr age of
influencers shuffling between br ands, and k eeping tr ack of who
represents what is hard.
Instead of having a shared narr ative that resonates with your
audience, you have a long-lasting story to tell. Let’ s use a for
instance.
A short-term rental platform wants to dr aw more attention to
how it can help people rent out their property on VRBO or
Airbnb.
Instead of having influencers in the space tak e over social
media, companies can focus on telling memor able industry
stories lik e the worst guests they’ve ever had. This approach is
relatable, speaks to the ICP , and gives your audience a reason to
engage and follow along.
Things to consider:
Choose the right influencers:  They’re representing your
brand and liter ally posting under your account.
Have a clear call to action:  Too man y social media
takeovers will have just the right combo of everything
above… but people aren’t sure what to do next. Mak e sure
every aspect of this effort is clear.
Encour age real-time inter action:  Don’t just post it and
forget it. Have an y influencer(s) involved stick around and
engage. Not only does the algorithm love it, it’ll also mak e
the whole process more effective.
Interactive Content Collaborations
We’ve also seen far too often in the mark et content/campaigns
that simply speak at your audience r ather than to them. This is
completely contr ary to everything people-first.
Community is built through engagement. So, engage your
audience (and future customers) b y involving them in the
content creation process. Instead of giving your influencers the
exact messaging you want them to use, collabor ate with them
and host contests, polls, or challenges related to your br and.
This will do everything you expect (not only create
excitement and buzz around your br and) but also allow for
direct inter action with potential customers.
Maybe you work with the influencer to invite their followers
to create along with you or share their stories. Y our audience
will feel included and valued, and most importantly , they’ll
remember the experience because of the stronger connection
with your br and.
Things to consider:
Keep your goals firmly in mind:  The type of inter activity
you decide upon needs to be aligned with your goals.
Encour age UGC:  Perhaps your influencer is the tip of the
iceberg for a whole bunch more content created b y their
followers. UGC is a great wa y to create a flywheel effect
where content creates even more content.
Use the strength of your platform:  Not all platforms are
created equal. Influencer mark eting in B2B doesn’t live or
die b y Link edIn. Driving users to platforms that allow for
better engagement can be the wa y to go if you feel
constr ained.
Webinars that Educate AND Entertain
Repeat after me: webinars aren’t dead. Boring content is dead.
Now , say it 10 more times until you start to believe it.
Yes, there are far, far too man y events we’ve been to that
have amounted to a bunch of talking heads on a Zoom screen
and, if you’re lucky , a 10-minute Q&A at the end.
No matter how great the content ma y be, lacking
engagement, inter  action, and fun will lead to low performance.
It’s easy to hide behind a slide deck and sail through bullet
points. Plus, your audience knows that webinars are recorded
and slide decks are typically shared after the fact, so they can
become disengaged.
From the content perspective, one wa y to avoid this is a
litmus test: If you do the dry run and you find yourself a little
bored, your audience would have check ed out far before you.
Whether it’ s taking a look at industry trends or a workshop
on using your product, the right influencer can tr ansform
educational webinar content into something both informative
and enjo yable:
Lead with your best content:  Don’t leave your best for
last. Put your best up first otherwise you’ll lose attendees’
attention real quick.
Avoid the disguised sales pitch:  You might think you’re
doing a soft sell, but people are so allergic to being sold to
that if your webinar has even a hint of selling in it, people
will have a negative reaction and it will mak e it that much
harder for you to create real engagement with them. So,
don’t do that.
Drive inter action:  inter action doesn’t happen b y
accident. Ensure you’ve got people and questions and polls
seeded throughout to k eep your audience engaged.
Blogs That Offer Value and Vision
When we sa y influencer mark eting, we often think about other
media lik e video, podcasting, and presenting. But remember
that some of your audience ma y prefer to learn and engage via
text.
Likewise, I’m sure there’ s a segment of your audience cr aving
depth, seeking insights that go beyond a post, tweet, or fleeting
Instagr am story . This is where the true power of blogs comes
into pla y.
Why not work with an influencer on a guest post that doesn’t
just skim the surface but delves deep into relevant topics? That
way, you’re offering your audience information and a vision. Or
consider the impact of an interview with an influencer, where
they share their experiences with your product and their
journey , challenges, and triumphs. This isn’t merely content—
it’s a narr ative woven with credibility and authenticity .
But wh y stop at imagining? The question isn’t whether this
approach can add value to your br and—it’ s whether you can
afford to overlook its potential.
A well-researched, thoughtfully written blog post stands as a
beacon of trust and authority in a sea of content that comes and
goes with the weather.
Things to consider:
Use storytelling to connect:  Avoid the listicles and top
tips and instead think on incorpor ating the influencer ’s
expertise and experience throughout.
Encour age sharing and feedback:  Mak e it as easy as
possible to share the content from its original format to
wherever it needs to go next. After all, the best piece of
content doesn’t win. The best-promoted piece of content
wins.
Play with format:  Just because the core of the piece is
written doesn’t mean you can’t use other media tools at
your disposal. Use videos, infogr aphics, and everything
throughout.
As you’re br ainstorming your T oFu content, k eep in mind that
fun should also tr anslate to meaningful engagement.
All content should be entertaining to some extent and
especially so at T oFu but it’ s crucial to aim higher. The goal is to
create content that entertains, informs, and inspires.
By working with influencers who align with your br and
values and resonate with your target audience, you can cr aft
messages that genuinely engage and leave a lasting impression.
MoFu: Nurturing Relationships and Reinforcing
Brand Connection
Let’s pivot our focus a little further down towards the buying
decision—the Middle of the Funnel (MoFu), where nurturing
relationships and reinforcing br and connection becomes
pivotal.
What sets this stage apart is that, at MoFu, your audience is
no longer at the fringes of awareness. They know your br and,
and they’ve perhaps even nibbled at what you have to offer.
Now , it’s all about deepening those initial connections.
You’re evolving a new friendship; you’ve moved past the
introductions and are now discovering the la yers that will
either cement this relationship or see it fizzle out.
Your goal? T o become synon ymous with the solution they
seek, in the wa y our friends at ZoomInfo have become
intertwined with accur ate customer data.
Here are some middle-of-the-funnel campaign ideas that can
do just that.
Exclusive Events and Q&As
Imagine cr afting exclusive opportunities for your audience to
connect firsthand with the influencers they admire, all through
a meticulously cur ated platform. Y our br and acts as the
gatewa y to exceptional experiences, spanning from private
face-to-face meetups to high-profile industry summits.
These unique encounters must go beyond ordinary events.
For instance, hosting a VIP dinner with a renowned expert in
the field or organizing a virtual Q&A session with a well-known
expert in a field can elevate engagement and foster a sense of
community among your followers.
Things to consider:
Exclusive doesn’t necessarily mean expensive:  It could
be as simple as a Zoom roundtable limited to 20 k ey
guests.
Keep the headcount lower:  The further you go down the
funnel, the more personal and connected it should feel to
the person, going from one-to-man y down to one-to-few .
Mak e sure the event matches the br and:  If your br and
has absolutely nothing to do with bowling, even at a
stretch, don’t invite people to a bowling alley . Mak e the
event and location match your br and’ s personality . It’s
stickier that wa y.
Innovative Workshops
As we proceed down the funnel, we leave behind webinars
pack ed with hundreds of attendees and welcome workshops
that are directly designed to teach and engage.
These would be things lik e an influencer walking a
participant through solving a specific problem with them (using
your product) in real-time, solving problems, offering tips, and
showcasing features in an intimate and impactful wa y.
Crafting an effective workshop is a lot more of an investment
than a webinar (though both tak e hard work).
For a good workshop, you’ll want to consider a few things:
Have a clear problem you’re solving:  Otherwise, you’re
not going to attr act the right people to join.
Plan appropriately:  Allow for enough work time during
the session. Lik ewise, actionable tak eawa ys and follow-up
resources should be provided to ensure continued
learning and implementation after the workshop.
Use break out rooms:  You can better foster a collabor ative
environment b y using break out rooms to k eep groups
small.
Authentic Testimonies
One of these da ys, I’d love to see a case study that sa ys the
compan y wasn’t really in the ICP and couldn’t justify renewal,
so it churned. But obviously , that’ s never going to happen. Case
studies are extremely powerful tools that can often get overly
polished b y zealous PR, comms, or mark eters. What people are
really looking for in case studies and testimonials is to hear the
truth, good and bad.
If there’ s a bit of a learning curve with the UX, people want to
know . If a product really is that good, nothing speaks louder
than genuine enthusiasm.
The unsolicited “I used this, and it changed how I work, live,
think!” moments ripple through audiences with persuasive
power. These narr atives are not just testimonials; they’re
validations from trusted voices.
An example of this is me speaking on behalf of my friends at
Navattic, where I am an advisor and have rolled them out four
times now at companies.
Key things to consider:
Build long-term relationships:  Identifying these
opportunities is not lik ely to involve quick, one-and-done
campaigns. Long-term, mutually beneficial relationships
with influencers mak e this type of content easier to
produce.
Transparency is extremely vital:  Obviously , authenticity
is important for every type of influencer mark eting. It’ s
triply important here. Ensure that your case studies and
testimonials from influencers are as tr ansparent as
possible. Highlight not just the successes but also the
learning curves and challenges. A uthenticity breeds trust.
You can’t fak e true enthusiasm:  Actively seek out those
users who have had tr ansformational experiences with
your product. Their actual enthusiasm is your most
powerful endorsement.
Next up, we hit the bottom.
BoFu: Where Engagement Becomes Revenue
Now , we tr ansition to the mak e-or-break junction of the buyer ’s
journey: The Bottom of the Funnel (BoFu).
Here, there’ s a singular focus: Converting nurtured leads into
paying customers. It’ s where the rubber meets the road, wheat
is separ ated from the chaff, and other similar cliches.
By this point, every bit of trust and value cultivated through
your MoFu efforts must tr anslate into decisive action from the
prospect. They’ve got a clear understanding of their problem
and your solution. They’ve been engaged, educated, and even
entertained.
Now it’ s decision-making time and as such, you should expect
to spend more of your own time and resources to mak e
influencer content for this stage.
Here are some bottom-of-the-funnel campaign ideas designed
to clinch the deal.
Tailored demos
Let’s be real.
Offering demos that are tailored to the prospect’ s unique
requirements is table stak es. If you’re giving the same, generic
presentation to all your prospects and not focusing on their
unique problem, well, you’re not going to have a great
conversion r ate.
What we’re talking about here is more along the lines of a
live, inter active demonstr ation with your prospect’ s influencer
along for the ride.
They can show off how they use your product, how it fits into
their workflows, and give real, honest feedback to questions.
These sorts of demonstr ations ma y not be a fit for every
product but if it works, it can greatly strengthen the connection
between your offering and the prospect, increasing the
likelihood of conversion.
Key consider ations:
Be highly personalized:  Use data gathered during the
MoFu stage to customize the demo to the prospect’ s
specific challenges and goals.
Inter active:  Allow for real-time feedback and questions.
This mak es the demo a dialogue, not a monologue.
Focus on specific value:  Collabor ate with influencers to
mak e sure the whole group is prepared to speak to specific
ROI, time, or cost savings, not speaking in gener alities.
Time-Sensitive or Exclusive Offers
Creating urgency or scarcity is hardly new . Done well, it can
motivate on-the-fence prospects to act.
Offer limited-time discounts, free premium upgr ades, VIP
access, trials, or exclusive bundles. These should feel lik e a
natur al culmination of the interest they’ve already shown and a
reward for their engagement both with your br and and the
influencer, further driving the prospect toward action.
Things to consider:
Genuine value:  Ensure the offer provides real,
unmistakable value. Empty discounts won’t cut it.
Clear deadline:  The timefr ame should be short enough to
prompt action but long enough to not feel pressure-filled.
Exclusivity:  Frame it as a special offer for those who have
shown a consistent interest.
Customer Success Stories
Your efforts at the bottom of the funnel must converge on
demonstr ating unmistakable value and relevance, ensuring
prospects can’t envision a solution better suited to their needs.
Your aim is to mak e your offering the go-to solution for your
audience.
Whereas MoFu might lever age broader testimonials, BoFu is
the stage to showcase detailed customer success stories. If
you’ve established a long-term relationship with an influencer,
collabor ating with them on a success story can be a powerful
testament to the efficacy of your solution.
These narr atives must resonate deeply with the prospect’ s
situation, showcasing not just the success but the
transformation experienced b y using your software, service, or
solution.
Key insights:
Detail the journey:  Cover the full story—the challenges,
the decision-making process, the implementation, and the
final outcomes.
Quantifiable results:  Data wins every time. Whenever
possible, include data and metrics that provide concrete
evidence of success.
Relatable protagonists:  If the influencer you’re working
with reflects your ICP , the stories can be even more
impactful.
Other Considerations for Crafting Your
Campaign
Segment and Personalize Inﬂuencer Campaigns
Tailor influencer campaigns to address different stages of the
buyer ’s journey . For instance, influencers can be utilized for
thought leadership content at the awareness stage, detailed
product reviews or comparisons during consider ation, and
customer testimonials or case studies to aid decision-making.
Diversify Content Formats
Depending on the funnel stage, vary the content formats to
keep the audience engaged. Start with eye-catching
infogr aphics or short videos for top-of-the-funnel awareness,
move to webinars or live Q&A sessions for deeper engagement
in the consider ation phase, and offer exclusive discounts or
trials to nudge conversions at the decision stage.
Use Inﬂuencer Campaign Insights into Your Product
Roadmap
Encour age influencers to provide feedback on your products or
services. This feedback can be invaluable for improving or
developing new offerings. It not only enhances the product-
mark et fit but also strengthens the influencer ’s genuine
advocacy for your br and.
Integrate Inﬂuencer Marketing with Other Channels
Influencer mark eting is a powerful tool, but it works best when
integr ated with other mark eting channels. B y creating a
cohesive, cross-channel campaign, you can amplify your
message, reinforce your br and narr ative, and guide your
audience through the mark eting funnel more effectively .
To ensure a seamless and impactful integr ation across
channels, it’ s essential to maintain a consistent br and voice and
visual identity throughout your campaign.
Provide your influencer partners with clear guidelines and
assets, such as logos, color palettes, and messaging fr ameworks,
to ensure that their content aligns with your br and standards.
By presenting a united front across all touchpoints, you can
create a more memor able and persuasive campaign.

Measuring ROI from Inﬂuencer Marketing
According to a 2024 report b y Influencer Mark eting Hub, the
aver age R OI from influencer mark eting is around $5.20 for
every $1 spent. On the other hand, B2B R OI varies widely based
on industries, with some reporting an aver age return of $3 for
every $1 spent, while others show significantly higher returns.
B2B R OI centers on lead quality and long-term value from
CRM data, while influencer mark eting focuses on immediate
actions but struggles with long-term impact tr acking. B2B
incurs diverse expenses, while influencers primarily involve
fees.
B2B yields enduring results; influencers provide immediate
impact. B2B analytics offer deeper insights than influencer
metrics. Lead quality , audience relevance, attribution
challenges, and long-term impacts factor into accur ate R OI
assessment in both str ategies.
Here are some k ey differences between B2B and influencer
ROI:
Target Audience Reach
In B2B, the audience is often more niche and specific. R OI here
depends on engaging with decision-mak ers and stak eholders
within other businesses. This might involve longer sales cycles
and relationship-building, impacting R OI calculations.
Influencer mark eting tends to have a broader reach, tapping
into the influencer ’s followers. While the reach might be wider,
gauging the alignment of the influencer ’s audience with your
B2B product/service is crucial for R OI accur acy.
Conversion Rates
The sales funnel in B2B mark eting can be complex, involving
multiple touchpoints. R OI calculation often considers lead
quality , conversion r ates, and the lifetime value of acquired
clients.
Influencer-driven R OI here heavily depends on immediate
actions (lik e clicks, purchases) driven b y the influencer ’s
endorsement. However, tr acking long-term impact beyond
immediate conversions is challenging.
Measurability
B2B metrics lik e customer acquisition cost (CA C), customer
lifetime value (CL V), and lead-to-customer conversion r ate are
commonly used to measure success. Businesses analyze CRM
data, pipeline, and do customer surveys to gauge the impact of
their efforts.
Influencer R OI metrics include engagement r ates, click-
through r ates (CTR), and direct purchases attributed to the
influencer ’s promotion. Businesses use advanced tools to tr ack
traffic sources and coupon code usage link ed to influencers.
Cost
B2B mark eting costs revolve around sales teams, mark eting
campaigns, content creation, and relationship-building efforts.
Calculating R OI requires factoring in these diverse expenses.
Influencer mark eting costs primarily encompass the
influencer ’s fee or partnership terms, sometimes supplemented
by content creation costs. Compar atively , influencers might
seem less expensive upfront but assessing their impact against
spend is essential.
Longevity and Impact
B2B mark eting str ategies tak e time to yield results, but often
these relationships and br and associations have enduring
effects, leading to sustained R OI over time.
Influencer R OI is immediate and impactful, but sustaining the
influence and measuring lasting effects beyond the campaign’ s
duration can be challenging.
Data
B2B organizations can evaluate robust data analytics and CRM
systems often to get in-depth insights into customer behavior,
which allows for precise R OI measurements.
While influencer mark eting platforms provide some data, the
depth and accur acy might not match B2B analytics tools.

Marketing Strategies
Creator-first B2B influencer mark eting str ategies have

through a blend of quantitative and qualitative metrics.

Qualitatively , there are more nuanced measurements:

Review, Adapt, Scale
In creator-first B2B influencer mark eting, measuring R OI
involves a precise blend of k ey performance indicators (KPIs)
tailored to your campaign goals.
Here are more specific metrics:
Attribution Models
Utilize multi-touch attribution models to tr ace the entire
customer journey . This could involve first-touch attribution
(crediting the influencer for the initial touchpoint), last-touch
(attributing the conversion to the final inter action), or a more
comprehensive approach considering all touchpoints.
Implement UTM par ameters or unique tr acking codes for
each influencer link to precisely attribute conversions. T ools
like Google Analytics help in creating and analyzing these
codes, offering insights into which influencers drive actual
conversions.
Customer Lifetime Value (CLV)
Assess the long-term value gained from acquired customers due
to influencer mark eting efforts. This helps in understanding the
actual impact on revenue over the customer ’s lifespan.
Combine CRM data with campaign-specific identifiers to tr ack
CLV. Compare CL V between customers acquired through
influencer campaigns and other channels to assess the long-
term impact of influencers on customer value.
Content Engagement Metrics
Go beyond surface-level metrics. Dive into metrics lik e time
spent on page, content completion r ates, or even sentiment
analysis on comments to gauge audience involvement and
resonance with the influencer ’s content.
Utilize heatmaps and user behavior analytics tools to
understand how audiences inter act with influencer-gener ated
content. Optimize content formats, length, and structure based
on these insights to enhance engagement.
Analyze comments and inter actions on an influencer ’s post
promoting your product. Look for detailed comments
discussing product features, asking questions, or sharing
personal experiences related to your offering.
Actionable steps:
Create a comment analysis template categorizing
comments b y depth, inquiries, testimonials, or discussions.
Track shares and resharing of the influencer ’s content and
identify if it leads to meaningful discussions or further
engagements.
Inﬂuencer Performance Metrics
Evaluate individual influencer performance beyond just reach
and engagement. Look at conversion r ates specific to each
influencer to understand their actual impact on driving actions.
Develop unique referr al codes or affiliate links for each
influencer. This allows precise tr acking of conversions
attributed to individual influencers, providing data to identify
top-performing influencers for future collabor ations.
Brand Sentiment
Monitor shifts in br and perception or sentiment through
sentiment analysis tools or surveys.
Conduct sentiment analysis using social listening tools to
gauge how audiences perceive your br and after exposure to
influencer content. Look for shifts in sentiment, identifying
positive or negative shifts and their correlation with the
campaign.
Use sentiment analysis tools lik e Brandwatch or T alkwalk er
to tr ack changes in sentiment. Suppose there’ s a shift from
neutr al or negative sentiment to positive sentiments lik e
excitement or trust post-campaign.
Actionable steps:
Set up sentiment tr acking for relevant k eywords or
campaign-specific hashtags.
Compare sentiment levels before, during, and after the
influencer campaign.
Identify specific comments or discussions that contribute
to sentiment changes and analyze their content for
insights.
Content Impact
Evaluate the impact of influencer-gener ated content in terms of
resonance, uniqueness, and relevance to your br and’ s
messaging.
Assess how an influencer integr ates your product/service into
their content. Look for storytelling, tutorials, or authentic
endorsements that resonate with the influencer ’s audience.
Actionable steps:
Develop content guidelines or briefs to guide influencers
on integr ating your product/service authentically .
Evaluate influencer content against these guidelines,
noting instances where the content aligns well with your
brand’ s messaging and values.

Social media platforms evolve r apidly . Keep adapting

Feedback integr ation
Act on immediate audience feedback b y tweaking content

Post-campaign, conduct interviews or surveys asking
about the influencer ’s authenticity in promoting your

usual content.
Actionable steps:
Create survey questions probing audience perception of
the influencer ’s authenticity and br and alignment.
Analyze the responses to identify common themes or
sentiments related to the influencer ’s authenticity .
Encour age two-wa y communication between influencers and

How to Tap into Inﬂuencer-Led B2B Community
Marketing
Hiring influencers can be a str ategic move for br ands aiming to

Micro-influencer partnerships:  Collabor ate with micro-

Influencers with 10,000 to 100,000 followers have a lik e

This fosters a sense of community and involvement.
Inter active content gener ates 2x more conversions than

Community-centric giveawa ys or contests:  Collabor ate
with influencers to host contests or giveawa ys that require

Tailwind, Instagr am contests gener ate 3.5 times more lik es
and 64 times more comments per post (Christopher, 2020).
Co-creation of exclusive products or services:  Involve

products/services. This not only adds value but also mak es
the community feel included. 80% of consumers are more
likely to purchase a product or service if it’ s associated
with a personalized experience.
Utilize niche platforms and emerging trends : Explore
emerging platforms or trends where influencers are
active. F or instance, TikT ok has seen exponential growth,
and influencers on this platform have shown remarkable
engagement r ates due to its algorithm-driven content
distribution.
Collabor ative campaigns:  Collabor ate with influencers
on campaigns that encour age community involvement,
such as contests, challenges, or user-gener ated content
initiatives.
Consistent inter action:  Encour age influencers to engage
regularly with the community , responding to comments,
queries, and feedback, fostering a sense of inclusion.
Advocacy progr ams:  Develop progr ams recognizing and
empowering community advocates identified among the
audience, further amplifying the influencer ’s impact.
Community-led growth through B2B influencer mark eting
hinges on fostering a sense of community ownership and
belonging, where influencers act as more than just endorsers—
they become pivotal figures in cultivating genuine engagement
and fostering relationships within the br and’ s ecosystem.
B2B Community Marketing KPIs
Content Performance Metrics
Track the percentage of viewers who followed through on the
influencer ’s call-to-action (CT A), such as signing up for a
webinar or downloading gated content.
Measure the aver age time spent engaging with the
influencer ’s content. Longer engagement times often indicate
deeper interest and potential conversion intent.
To-do:
Use unique tr acking links or UTM par ameters for each
influencer ’s CTA.
Monitor the number of clicks on these CT As using
analytics tools.
Calculate the conversion r ate (number of conversions
from CT A clicks/total CT A clicks) × 100.
Community Building Metrics
Measure the increase in the B2B community size after the
influencer campaign. This includes new sign-ups, forum
members, or social media followers.
Assess the frequency and depth of inter actions within the
community—comments, discussions, or user-gener ated content
inspired b y the influencer.
To-do:
Establish a baseline for community size before the
campaign begins.
Regularly tr ack new sign-ups, forum registr ations, or
social media followers during and after the campaign.
Calculate growth r ate ((new community size – baseline
community size)/baseline community size) × 100.
Inﬂuence on Thought Leadership
Track how often the influencer ’s content is shared on Link edIn
or industry-specific platforms. This demonstr ates thought
leadership and reach within professional circles.
Measure the perceived educational value b y evaluating
comments or feedback indicating insights gained from the
influencer ’s content.
To-do:
Encour age influencers to share content on professional
platforms.
Monitor shares or reposts of influencer content on
platforms lik e Link edIn.
Track the number of shares directly from the influencer ’s
posts.
Relationship Development Metrics
Quantify new partnerships or collabor ations established within
the B2B industry as a result of the influencer ’s introduction or
involvement.
Track the number of positive testimonials or
recommendations received from B2B clients or industry peers
due to the influencer ’s impact.
To-do:
Identify and tr ack new partnerships or collabor ations
initiated post-campaign.
Measure the frequency of inter action or joint initiatives
with these new partners.
Assess the qualitative impact of these partnerships on
business growth or knowledge exchange.
Conversion and Pipeline Metrics
Measure the lead-to-sale acceler ation r ate for a funnel post-
exposure to influencer content.
Quantify the revenue directly attributable to leads influenced
or engaged b y the influencer campaign.
To-do:
Track the movement of leads through the sales funnel
using CRM data.
Compare the aver age time tak en for leads exposed to
influencer content to progress through the pipeline
against those not exposed.
Calculate acceler ation r ate: ((aver age time for influenced
leads) – (aver age time for non-influenced leads)) ÷
(aver age time for non-influenced leads) ×100.
Employee Advocacy and Engagement
Measure the increase in emplo yees sharing br and- or
influencer-related content within their professional networks.
Track cross-departmental collabor ations spurred b y the
influencer campaign, fostering internal engagement and
knowledge sharing.
To-do:
Implement an internal sharing progr am for influencer-
related content.
Monitor emplo yee participation and content sharing
within their professional networks.
Track the increase in engagement metrics from emplo yee-
shared content.
These KPIs help br ands gain a deeper understanding of the
influencer campaign’ s impact on community building, thought
leadership, relationship development, and br and perception
within the B2B space. This data-driven approach allows for a
more nuanced evaluation of the campaign’ s effectiveness and
its real contribution to business growth.
