Forging Long-Term B2B
Influencer Partnerships
Finding the right creators to partner with can be a daunting
task. It’ s like searching for a needle in a ha ystack, except the
haystack is an infinite network of creators with varying
audience sizes, engagement r ates, and content styles.
However, with the right approach and a k een eye for what
truly matters, you can navigate this landscape and discover the
perfect partners to elevate your br and.
Partnering with creators is akin to tapping into the power of
word-of-mouth mark eting. It’ s not just about promoting a
product; it’ s about aligning your br and with a creator whose
style and audience match your own. When done right, this
approach can lead to higher-intent customers and prospects, as
the creator ’s endorsement carries weight and credibility .
Inﬂuencers Are People Too. Identifying the Right
Ones is Crucial
When selecting creators to partner with, it’ s crucial to look
beyond the numbers and consider the qualitative aspects. Ask
yourself: Does this creator align with our br and’ s style and
values? Does their audience mak eup match our target mark et?
A creator who shares your br and’ s vision and speaks to your
ideal customer is far more valuable than one with a massive
but unengaged following. T ake the time to research potential
partners, analyze their content, and gauge the quality of their
audience inter actions.
Think about it this wa y. Would you hire an emplo yee who
didn’t align with your compan y’s values? I’m sure the answer
would be a resounding “nope.”
So wh y should it be an y different when choosing an
influencer to represent your br and?
When you partner with a creator, they become an extension
of your br and. Their actions, statements, and behavior can
significantly impact your br and image. Therefore, it is crucial to
treat influencer partnerships as carefully as adding headcount
to your team.
Here are some of the qualitative things to consider when
selecting an influencer.
Alignment With Your Brand’s Values
An influencer who doesn’t share your br and’ s ethos and values
can do more harm than good. Their followers might see
through the lack of authenticity , damaging the credibility of
both the influencer and your br and. It’ s essential to ensure that
the influencer ’s values align with yours before proceeding with
any collabor ation.
Empowerment to Share Their Perspective
Your chosen influencer should feel empowered to share their
honest opinions about your product or service. This not only
maintains their authenticity but also builds trust among their
followers. Micro-managing their content could lead to a lack of
genuine engagement and poor campaign results.
Mutual Respect with Their Audience
The influencer ’s relationship with their followers is another
critical aspect to consider. Do they have a respectful, two-wa y
communication with their audience? Trust and respect are the
foundations of an y successful influencer mark eting campaign.
Metrics That Matter
We’ve covered plenty of qualitative factors (and these are
essential) but there are still quantifiable metrics to consider
when evaluating creators. Here are a few k ey ones to k eep in
mind:
Audience size:  While not the be-all and end-all, audience
size does pla y a role. Look for creators with a following
that’ s large enough to provide significant reach but not so
large that their engagement suffers.
Ramp:  Analyze a creator ’s engagement over time. Are
they experiencing steady growth? A creator whose
engagement is consistently increasing is lik ely to yield
better results and potentially more R OI in the long run.
Engagement r ate: Don’t just look at the number of lik es
and comments; consider their quality . A creator with a
smaller but highly engaged audience ma y be more
valuable than one with a large but unengaged following.
Revenue:  Ultimately , the success of your influencer
mark eting efforts will be measured b y their impact on
your bottom line. Use referr al links or UTM tr acking to see
which creators are driving the most tr affic and
conversions.
Professionalism
Lastly , professionalism is k ey. While follower count and
engagement r ates are important, it’ s equally vital to work with
someone who respects deadlines, communicates effectively , and
isn’t, well, a complete jerk. Viewing influencer partnerships in
the same light as hiring a new team member can mak e all the
difference. It ma y seem lik e a lot of work upfront, but trust me,
it’ll save you a PR headache later.
Some Industries Have It Easier than Others
The ease of identifying and partnering with influencers can
vary greatly depending on the industry . In sectors lik e
mark eting and sales, Link edIn has emerged as a go-to platform

However, mapping out these k ey figures can present

It’s crucial to find someone who is not only respected within

type of content that resonates with them. The collabor ation

the influencer ’s expertise and authenticity to shine through.
In niche industries, the struggles can be more apparent.
Finding an influencer with a significant following who also has

However, this challenge presents an opportunity to explore
alternative collabor ation formats that can help bridge the gap.
Appr oaching Potential Inﬂuencer Partners
If you’ve followed through this far, you’ve identified relevant
influencers in your industry . Start b y researching individuals
who have a strong presence on platforms where your target

specific forums. Look for thought leaders, experts, and content

Once you’ve identified potential partners, it’ s time to reach

message, focus on building a genuine connection r ather than
simply pitching your product or service. Show that you’ve tak en
the time to familiarize yourself with their content and
expertise. Highlight specific aspects of their work that resonate
with your br and and explain wh y you believe a partnership
would be mutually beneficial.
Avoid generic, cop y-pasted messages that feel impersonal and
transactional. Instead, tailor your outreach to each individual
influencer, demonstr ating your appreciation for their unique
voice and perspective. Be clear about your intentions and the
type of partnership you envision, whether it’ s a one-time
collabor ation, an ongoing campaign, or a long-term advisory
role.
When initiating contact, it’ s essential to be respectful of the
influencer ’s time and attention. K eep your message concise and
to the point, while still providing enough information to pique
their interest. If they don’t respond right awa y, follow up
politely after a reasonable amount of time has passed.
Remember, building a successful influencer partnership is a
gradual process that requires patience, persistence, and
genuine effort.
Crafting Compelling Pitches That Showcase the
Value of a Partnership
Once you’ve established initial contact with a potential
influencer partner, it’ s time to cr aft a compelling pitch that
showcases the value of a collabor ation. Y our pitch should be
tailored to the specific influencer and demonstr ate a clear
understanding of their audience, content style, and goals.
Start b y outlining the objectives of the partnership and how
they align with the influencer ’s own mission and values. Be
specific about what you hope to achieve together, whether it’ s
increasing br and awareness, gener ating leads, or driving
conversions. Clearly articulate how the influencer ’s unique

value for their audience.
Next, highlight the benefits of the partnership for the
influencer themselves. This could include access to exclusive
resources, products, or insights that can help them create more
compelling content for their followers. If you’re offering
monetary compensation, be tr ansparent about the terms and
ensure that the amount is fair and commensur ate with the
influencer ’s reach and engagement.
In addition to tangible benefits, emphasize the opportunity
for the influencer to grow their personal br and and expand

reputable B2B compan y can lend credibility to their expertise
and help them attr act new followers and opportunities.
When cr afting your pitch, be sure to include specific

could include proposed content formats, topics, and
distribution channels. However, be open to the influencer ’s
input and ideas as well. Remember, a successful partnership is

Close your pitch with a clear call to action and next steps.
Invite the influencer to schedule a call or meeting to discuss the
partnership further and address an y questions or concerns they

Aligning Inﬂuencer Partnerships with Your
Marketing Strategy
To maximize the impact of your B2B influencer mark eting

over all mark eting str ategy . Start b y defining clear goals and

For example, if your compan y is launching a new product,

When developing your influencer mark eting plan, consider

Coordinate your influencer-created content with your own

To ensure that your influencer partnerships are truly

Busting Inﬂuencer Marketing Myths
Influencer mark eting world is full of certain myths but not all
of them are true. Let’ s see how .
Myth: Size (of Their Audience) Matters
False. One of the most common pitfalls in B2B influencer
mark eting is the fixation on audience size. It’ s easy to get caught
up in the allure of partnering with creators who have tens or
hundreds of thousands of followers. However, this approach
can be a mistak e.
Let’s tak e a step back and remember the ultimate goal of
mark eting: Driving revenue. A creator with a massive following
doesn’t necessarily equate to a significant impact on your
bottom line. In fact, some of the most successful campaigns
have been run with micro-creators, those with an audience size
of around 1K to 5K.
These micro-creators often have a deeper, more personal
connection with their audience. They can speak to specific pain
points and create content that truly resonates. Plus, working
with them usually comes at a lower cost compared to their
larger counterparts.
By partnering with a carefully selected group of mid-level
influencers, companies can achieve significant results without
needing an enormous number of impressions. This approach
allows for a more targeted, authentic campaign that resonates
with the right people, r ather than casting a wide net and hoping
for the best.
Myth: You Only Need One Inﬂuencer
False. One often-overlook ed benefit of influencer mark eting?
You can work with more than one. B y partnering with sever al
creators who all target the same audience, your product or
service will appear frequently in your target mark et’s feed. This
repetition, known as the bubble effect, can be a powerful driver
of br and awareness and engagement.
Imagine your ideal customer scrolling through their social
media feed and seeing your br and mentioned b y multiple
creators they trust and follow . This consistent exposure can
pique their curiosity and increase the lik elihood of them
checking out your offering.
Myth: Inﬂuencers Can’t Work for Your Company
False. Building influencers internally can be a hugely effective
strategy . Man y experts predict that companies will start
developing their own influencers internally over the next five
years. This could involve identifying emplo yees with strong
personal br ands and helping them build their influence within
the industry , or even having founders become influencers
themselves.
The benefits of having a subject matter expert who is active
within the community and inter acts with buyers daily are
immense. B y cultivating internal influencers, companies can
create authentic, trusted voices that can speak to the unique
value proposition of their products or services. These internal
influencers can also provide valuable insights into customer
needs and preferences, helping to shape the direction of the
compan y’s offerings.
Myth: It’s okay if we treat this like a one-off
False. Approach your influencer mark eting efforts lik e you
would an y other mark eting campaign. Spread your investments
across multiple creators, then optimize over time based on
performance.
Start b y sourcing a diverse set of 10 to 20 creators to
potentially work with. Not every partnership will be a perfect
fit, so it’ s important to cast a wide net. As you begin
collabor ating, tr ack each creator ’s performance using a CRM
tool. This will help you identify the top performers and mak e
data-driven decisions about who to continue working with.
Building Long-Term Relationships With
Inﬂuencers
Building a meaningful B2B influencer partnership isn’t just
about tr ansactions; it’ s about forging a connection (Srivastava,
2023). Here’ s your recipe for success.
Open Communication and Transparency
Picture this partnership as a journey , and the map for this
expedition is open communication. Clearly defining
expectations, goals, and deliver ables right from the start sets
the tone for a shared adventure. It’ s not just about what you
want; it’ s about understanding each other ’s aspir ations and
ensuring you’re on the same exciting path.
Creative Freedom and Collaboration
Like an y great duo, you and your influencer are a team. A dash
of creative freedom allows the influencer to bring their unique
expertise and flair to the table. Let them weave their magic.
After all, their authentic touch tr ansforms content from
ordinary to extr aordinary . Embr ace collabor ation as a dance of
ideas, and let the creativity flow .
Mutual Respect and Trust
Every strong partnership is built on trust. It’ s the invisible
thread that weaves through every inter action. Respect is the
foundation, and trust is the structure. Understand and
appreciate the influencer ’s perspective and let them bring their
authenticity to the forefront. The more trust you invest in this
relationship, the richer the dividends in terms of authenticity
and long-term success.
Measurement and Analysis
Every journey needs its checkpoints, and your influencer
partnership is no different. Regularly checking the map, or in
this case, tr acking campaign results, is your North Star. Analyze
the data, understand the twists and turns, and be ready to
adjust your sails. It’ s not just about the destination; it’ s about
enjo ying the journey and making it as rewarding as possible for
both you and your influencer collabor ator.
Establishing Guidelines
While the B2B influencer mark eting space ma y lack the
formalized structure of its B2C counterpart, that doesn’t mean
you should approach it haphazardly . Establish guidelines for
your creator partnerships to ensure a consistent br and message
and voice.
Create a document outlining your product’ s key features,
benefits, and use cases. Include examples of successful posts
and phr ases to avoid. Share this with your creators to give them
a solid foundation to work from. Remember, the goal is to
provide guidance, not to dictate what they should post. Allow
them the creative freedom to cr aft content that authentically
resonates with their audience.
Compensation Considerations
Compensating creators for their work is a crucial aspect of
building strong, long-lasting partnerships. However, this
compensation doesn’t alwa ys have to be monetary . Consider
alternative forms of compensation, such as providing software
or assistance in building their personal br and.
The k ey is to approach these partnerships as mutually
beneficial relationships. B y supporting your creators and
helping them grow , you’ll foster a sense of lo yalty and
encour age them to go the extr a mile for your br and.
Embracing Experimentation
Finally , don’t be afr aid to experiment. Influencer mark eting,
especially in the B2B space, is still a relatively new frontier.
What works for one br and ma y not work for another. Be willing
to try new approaches, test different creators, and iter ate based
on your results.
Keep a close eye on your metrics, but also listen to your gut. If
a partnership feels off-br and or inauthentic, don’t be afr aid to
pivot. The beauty of working with a diverse set of creators is
that you have the flexibility to adjust your str ategy as you go.

Other Considerations for Finding the Right

As more companies recognize the value of B2B influencer

Think Outside the Box with Alternative
Collaboration Formats
One effective approach for working with influencers in niche
industries is to host webinars or podcast series with them.
These formats allow for a Q&A-style engagement that not only
caters to the influencer ’s comfort level but also helps to

By providing a platform for the influencer to share their
knowledge and insights, you can tap into their expertise while
also building trust and credibility with your target audience.
Podcasts, in particular, have emerged as a powerful tool in
B2B influencer mark eting. They allow companies to tap into an
influencer ’s audience without necessarily having to pa y that
individual, making them a cost-effective wa y to expand your
reach. B y featuring influencers as guests on your podcast or
sponsoring their own shows, you can align your br and with
their credibility and thought leadership, reaching a highly
engaged audience that trusts their opinions and
recommendations.
Don’t Leave Out Qualitative Metrics When
Measuring Success
When it comes to measuring the success of your influencer
partnerships, it’ s essential to look beyond immediate sales and
focus on qualitative metrics that provide a more
comprehensive picture of your campaign’ s impact.
One k ey metric to consider is whether the influencer has
encour aged your target audience to inter act with your content
in a wa y they wouldn’t have without their involvement. This
can be assessed through various means, such as “How did you
hear about us?” submissions, sales call recordings that mention
the influencer, and engagement from the right companies and
people on the content itself.
While bottom-funnel metrics lik e sales and conversions are
important, they don’t alwa ys tell the whole story . Engagement
from k ey decision-mak ers and target accounts can be just as
valuable, indicating that your message is reaching the right
people and making an impact. B y tracking these qualitative
measures of success, you can gain a clearer picture of your
campaign’ s effectiveness and mak e data-driven decisions for
future partnerships.
The Rise of the Advisor or Content Creator Role
One of the most exciting trends in B2B influencer mark eting is
the rise of the advisor or content creator role. Companies are
moving beyond tr aditional influencer partnerships and offering
individuals a stak e in their business, money , or a referr al
progr am to become an integr al part of their organization as an
advisor.
This innovative approach allows businesses to tap into the
influencer ’s expertise and credibility in a more substantive wa y,
creating a deeper, more authentic partnership. B y bringing the
influencer into the fold as an advisor, companies can lever age
their insights and thought leadership to shape their products,
services, and over all str ategy .
A key advantage of this approach is its cost-effectiveness.
Rather than investing in a single, high-profile influencer,
companies can collabor ate with sever al advisors or content
creators, resulting in a surge of impressions and a more diverse
range of voices advocating for their br and. This str ategy has
proven successful for companies lik e Lavender, which has
hired individuals with strong personal br ands and lever aged
their influence effectively .
Embracing the Future of B2B Inﬂuencer Marketing
As the B2B influencer mark eting landscape continues to evolve,
companies that sta y attuned to emerging trends and adapt their
strategies accordingly will be well-positioned for success. B y
exploring alternative collabor ation formats, focusing on
qualitative metrics, and embr acing new roles lik e advisors and
internal influencers, businesses can build authentic, impactful
partnerships that drive real results.
The k ey is to approach influencer mark eting as a long-term
strategy r ather than a one-off campaign. B y investing in
relationships with trusted voices in your industry and
providing value to their audiences, you can create a powerful
network of advocates who can help elevate your br and and
drive growth for years to come.
As we’ve seen, the world of B2B influencer mark eting is full
of exciting possibilities. B y sta ying agile, innovative, and
focused on authenticity , companies can navigate the challenges
and opportunities of this dynamic landscape and build
partnerships that truly move the needle. So don’t be afr aid to

What Makes Glo bal Different?
Flexibility . Global influencer mark eting means applying a

PopSock ets nailed this approach. While celebs lik e Kendall

Local vs. Global Inﬂuencers
Think of global influencers lik e those jet-setting celebrities you
see on red carpets or social media profiles with millions of
followers from all corners of the world. They’re lik e the A-
listers who everyone knows about, tr anscending borders and
cultures with their massive reach.
Global influencers are the pop stars—big, bold, and known to
almost everyone—while local influencers are more lik e the
cherished community leaders who have a powerful impact
within their specific area.
Now , local influencers? Picture your friendly neighborhood
heroes, the ones who know everyone in town and can
recommend the best local spots to hang out. They might not
have millions of followers, but they’ve got a devoted group of
locals who hang onto their every word.
The k ey difference? Global influencers cast a wide net, aiming
to capture the attention of diverse audiences worldwide.
Meanwhile, local influencers focus on a specific region, offering
tailored content that deeply resonates with their community .
Both have their perks, so it depends on whether you want the
world’ s spotlight or to build a strong bond with a particular
group.
Reach
Global influencers have a massive reach, spanning across
different countries and continents. They appeal to a broad,
diverse audience.
On the other hand, local influencers have a more
concentr ated reach, focusing on a specific region or community .
Audience Demographics
Global influencers attr act a wide r ange of demogr aphics,
cultures, and interests due to their extensive reach. They cater
to a diverse audience with varying preferences.
Local influencers, however, target a specific demogr aphic
within their region, often sharing experiences and interests that
resonate with their local audience.
Impact and Engagement
Global influencers can create widespread br and awareness and
recognition due to their large following.
They might not alwa ys have the same level of engagement as
local influencers, who tend to foster deeper connections and
engagement within their community . Local influencers often
have higher engagement r ates because of their close-knit
audience.
Content Focus
Global influencers ma y create content that appeals to a broad,
international audience, often in multiple languages.
In contr ast, local influencers concentr ate on producing
content that speaks directly to the culture, language, and
preferences of their local audience.
How to Make the Switch?
Shifting from a local to a global influencer involved a big

while sta ying true to my roots.
I didn’t want to become a walking, talking cultur al faux pas!

What really click ed was the ‘adapt without compromise’

I didn’t do it alone! I collabor ated with local influencers who

territories of different mark ets. Their insights were gold—
helping me avoid embarr assing blunders and shaping content
that click ed with specific regions.
The k ey? It’ s been a gr adual expansion. I didn’t go global
overnight. I started b y dipping my toes in a few regions, testing
the waters, and learning. Slowly , I’ve been broadening my
horizons as I gain confidence and knowledge about different
global audiences.

The famous adage applies to B2B influencer mark eting.

Cultural Sensitivity
B2B audiences are cultur ally sensitive—but just lik e locals,

Cultur al sensitivity is the cornerstone of successful global

You might recall the controversy created b y Pepsi’ s Kendall

So, wh y does cultur al sensitivity matter? W ell, imagine trying

Your cultur al understanding matters more than your words
when penetr ating global mark ets. A campaign that hits home in

Localization
Influencer localization is str ategically adapting your mark eting
campaigns to resonate with specific regional or local audiences.
It involves tailoring content, messaging, and collabor ations to
fit the cultur al nuances, preferences, and behaviors of a
particular geogr aphic location.
Why Is It Important?
Different regions have unique cultur al norms, values, and
preferences. Localization ensures that the content aligns with
these cultur al nuances, making it more relatable and engaging
for the audience.
Localized content feels more authentic and genuine. When
influencers understand and reflect the local culture, it fosters
trust among the audience, leading to stronger connections and
better reception of the br and’ s message.
Content that resonates cultur ally tends to gener ate higher
engagement. It can evok e emotions and sentiments that are
specific to the local audience, prompting more inter actions and
shares.
Key Elements of Inﬂuencer Localization
Localize your language:  Using the local language or
dialect helps in breaking language barriers and
connecting more intimately with the audience.
Cultur al sensitivity:  Respect local tr aditions, customs,
and sensitivities. A voiding cultur al taboos or
misunderstandings is vital for a successful localized
campaign.
Geogr aphic relevance:  Tailoring content to suit specific
geogr aphic references or regional trends can enhance
relatability .
Collabor ating with local influencers:  Working with
influencers who are already established and trusted
within the community can amplify the campaign’ s impact.
Localized content creation:  Adapt content formats,
visuals, and references to align with local tastes and
preferences.
In essence, influencer localization is about going beyond
language and adapting mark eting efforts to truly connect with a
local audience. It’ s a powerful wa y to ensure that influencer
campaigns feel more personal, resonant, and impactful in
diverse regions or mark ets.

The Shiny Platform Syndrome
Shin y Platform S yndrome refers to the tendency of content
creators or influencers to constantly shift their focus from one
platform to another, chasing the latest trend or popular social
media platform (Clouse, 2023). It often leads to a lack of
consistency , dilution of efforts, and an inability to build a
strong, engaged audience.
When expanding globally or even at a local level, succumbing
to Shin y Platform S yndrome can be detrimental for sever al
reasons:
Divided efforts
Constantly jumping between platforms means spreading
your time and resources thinly , making it harder to
cultivate a dedicated following on an y one platform.
Inconsistent presence
Followers appreciate consistency . If you’re continually
switching platforms, your audience might struggle to k eep
up, leading to reduced engagement and potential loss of
interest.
Learning curve
Every platform has its unique algorithms, features, and
audience behaviors. Constantly switching platforms
means a perpetual learning curve, making it difficult to
master an y one platform’ s best pr actices.
Lost opportunities
By perpetually chasing the latest platform, you ma y miss
out on fully lever aging the potential of a particular
platform where your audience is already engaged.
Creators often fall victim to Shin y Platform S yndrome because
of the fear of missing out (FOMO). It’ s tempting to think that
success lies in being present everywhere, on every trending
platform. There’ s this belief that if you’re not on a certain
platform, you’re missing out on a massive audience or
opportunity .
Plus, there’ s the pressure of sta ying ahead of the curve. Every
new platform promises innovation, wider reach, and potential
success, which mak es it hard to resist diving in headfirst.
It’s easy to get caught up in the h ype, thinking that the next
big thing will skyrock et your career. But in reality , trying to
maintain a presence on every platform spreads you too thin. It
divides your focus, time, and energy across multiple spaces,
often diluting the impact you could have on platforms where
your audience actually engages with your content. It’ s a classic
case of quantity over quality , where the effort gets scattered,
and the returns are minimal.
To avoid this syndrome, focus on a few k ey platforms where
your audience is most active. Prioritize building a strong
presence and community on these platforms r ather than
continuously shifting focus.
Consistency and quality engagement are k ey to successful
global expansion or local growth for influencers. Once you’ve
established a strong foothold, then consider expanding
strategically to other platforms, maintaining a balanced
approach without losing your primary focus.
How to Go Glo bal?
First off, you’ve got to pla y cultur al cards right. Understand
your audience inside out—what they lik e, what bugs them, and
what speaks to their hearts. T ailor your content accordingly .
One smart move is to go local. I’m talking about tr anslations.
When I went global, I hired local talent who understood the
local mark ets. They made sure my content felt lik e it belonged.
Collabor ation is the rock et fuel. Partnering up with local
creators opens doors to new followers and priceless insights
into what mak es the locals tick.
Your social media game needs a regional twist. While Insta
and F acebook are global stars, platforms lik e WeChat or
KakaoT alk dominate other parts of the world. Include them in
your str ategy .
Networking is a must-have. Get involved in local groups or
industry hangouts. Build those relationships, share ideas, and
earn trust.
Global success tak es time, effort, and a genuine interest in the
folks you’re reaching out to. Stick with it, and you’ll see those
global horizons get closer and closer.
Adapting Strategies for Global Markets
When I first expanded my content to a global audience, I was
thrilled but quickly hit some unexpected roadblocks. F or
instance, what seemed lik e a universally amusing jok e in my
home country didn’t quite land the same wa y in another. That
was a wak e-up call—humor doesn’t alwa ys tr anslate!
Then came the logistical puzzle of time zones. Trying to
synchronize live sessions or collabor ations across continents
felt lik e conducting an orchestr a. It involved early mornings,
late nights, and sometimes just going with the flow of
unpredictable time differences.
Legalities threw me for a loop too. Each country had its own
set of rules, from data compliance to content regulations.
Understanding these was lik e deciphering a complex code.
But each stumbling block was a lesson. It pushed me to adapt
my content str ategy , not just b y translating words but also b y
understanding cultur al subtleties. It taught me to respect and
embr ace the diverse perspectives worldwide, shaping my
approach to create more inclusive and relatable content for my
global audience.
Here is how you can avoid making the same mistak es I did:
Platform understanding
Recognize the popularity of different platforms in various
regions. T ailor your content format and style according to
the platforms most favored b y your global audience.
Localized engagement
Go beyond content creation b y actively engaging with
your audience. Participate in discussions, comment
sections, and local forums to build genuine connections
and understand their perspectives.
Collabor ative learning
Engage with local creators, not just as partners but as
learners. Understand their str ategies, content styles, and
audience engagement methods, which can provide
invaluable insights for your global approach.
Diverse content formats
Explore diverse content formats that cater to different
preferences across regions. Some audiences might prefer
short-form videos, while others engage more with long-
form written content or podcasts.
Adaptable br anding
Ensure your br and messaging and identity are flexible
enough to resonate universally while maintaining
consistency . Create a br and that adapts to diverse cultures
without losing its core values.
Data-driven decisions
Lever age analytics and data insights to understand how
your content performs in various regions. Use this
information to refine your str ategies and optimize content
for better engagement.
Community building
Foster a sense of community among your global audience.
Encour age inter actions between audience members from
different regions, creating a unified space around your
content.
Adaptive scheduling
Embr ace flexible scheduling for content releases or live
sessions, considering time zones. Utilize scheduling tools
to optimize post timings and engage with audiences
worldwide.
Legal compliance
Get familiar with global legalities and regulations
concerning data, content, and advertising. Engage legal
counsel if needed to ensure compliance with each region’ s
laws.
Testing and iter ating
Start small when entering new mark ets. T est your content,
strategies, and campaigns in pilot phases to gather
feedback and adapt before scaling up.
Expanding globally as a creator involves a blend of cultur al
intelligence, adaptability , and a deep understanding of the
audiences you’re targeting. Integr ating these str ategies can help
tailor your creator-first approach to resonate strongly across
diverse global mark ets.

LinkedIn’s Algorithm
Link edIn’ s algorithm is a complex system designed to
determine the visibility and distribution of content on the
platform. It prioritizes specific content types and engagement
factors to enhance user experience. Here’ s a break down.
The algorithm focuses on relevance, aiming to displa y content
that aligns with users’ interests, connections, and engagement
history .
It analyzes various signals to determine content visibility ,
including relevance to the audience, engagement metrics, post
recency , and the poster ’s activity .
LinkedIn Algorithm Signals Checklist
Relevance signals:
Audience alignment:  Is the content aligned with the
interests and industry affiliations of the target
audience?
Profile matching:  Is the content tailored to resonate
with the professional back grounds of the intended
audience?
Engagement signals:
Inter actions:  Will the content lik ely prompt
meaningful engagement such as lik es, comments,
and shares?
Engagement dur ation:  Is the content engaging
enough to hold users’ attention?
Recency:  Is the content recent and timely to remain
relevant in users’ feeds?
Poster ’s activity signals:
Consistency:  Has there been consistent engagement
with the audience and a regular posting schedule?
Network engagement:  Do the connections engage
with the content, indicating its relevance?
Content format and type signals:
Native videos:  Have engaging native videos been
included to increase visibility?
Comprehensive content:  Has in-depth content been
shared, showcasing thought leadership?
Hashtag usage signals:
Relevance:  Are the hashtags used relevant and
aiding content discovery?
Optimized hashtags:  Have suitable hashtags been
used without overwhelming the content?
User behavior signals:
Click-through potential:  Is the content lik ely to
gener ate clicks and interest?
Negative signals:  Has content lik ely to be hidden or
flagged b y users been avoided?
Profile credibility signals:
Profile completeness:  Is the profile complete with
endorsements and expertise?
Expertise displa y: Does the content showcase
expertise and thought leadership?
External engagement signals:
External referr als: Will the content attr act
engagement or tr affic from external sources?
Cross-platform sharing:  Can the content encour age
sharing across different platforms?
LinkedIn Favored Content Types
Native videos:  Link edIn favors native videos that are
engaging, informative, and directly uploaded to the
platform.
Long-form content:  Articles with comprehensive insights,
industry analyses, or thought leadership pieces tend to
perform well.
Engaging multimedia:  Visual content lik e infogr aphics,
slideshows, and images that captivate and inform the
audience.
Live videos and webinars:  Real-time engagement
through live sessions and webinars attr acts visibility .
Engagement Factors That Inﬂuence the Algorithm
Relevance to audience:  Content aligned with users’
interests and industry niches tends to get more visibility .
Engagement metrics:  High-quality engagement—
meaningful comments, shares, and longer dwell times—
boosts visibility .
Consistency:  Regular posting and engagement contribute
positively to visibility .
Personal connections:  Content shared or engaged with b y
connections tends to appear more prominently in feeds.
Elements That Do Not Impact the Algorithm
Hashtags:  While they can increase discover ability ,
Link edIn’ s algorithm focuses less on hashtags compared to
other platforms.
Post length:  Unlik e other platforms, Link edIn doesn’t
prioritize specific post lengths. Quality and relevance
matter more than length.

Amplifying Your Strategy
Video production—the art of compelling visual content creation
—is at the forefront of B2B influencer mark eting. Nothing
mak es viewers stick to their screens more than a swipeable
short-reels continuum.
Video production’ s core elements are storytelling, visual
artistry , and audio expertise to deliver a powerful message.
I, as a B2B influencer, have come to recognize the par amount
importance of video in capturing attention, building viewers’
trust, and driving engagement. But wh y is there a sudden surge
in video’ s popularity within the B2B mark eting landscape?
Ninety-one percent of video mark eters sa y that using videos
has directly increased dwell time and tr affic on their websites
(Wyzowl, 2023). Videos captivate your audience and increase
their attention span in a world flooded with information.
Let’s talk about attention. The aver age user attention span is
around eight seconds (McSpadden, 2015).
Yep, you read that right—eight seconds. But here’ s where
things get interesting: Videos extend the viewer ’s attention
window up to 10 seconds as compared to static content!
What mak es videos an attention magnet for online visitors?
Visuals paint the story , while sound adds depth to create an
immersive story for the viewers. In fact, some videos tend to
disconnect the viewers from the outside world and k eep them
glued to their screen.
By 2022, online videos will constitute more than 82 percent of
all consumer internet tr affic (Cisco, n.d.). The video production
demand surge is upward for a solid reason—videos connect
better than other content mediums.
A HubSpot survey reports that a whopping 79 percent of
people have reported buying a software or app after learning
about it through video mark eting (Marinelli, 2023).
Video is King
A decade ago, I was knee-deep in the creators’ economy and
regularly shared the typical landscape-oriented videos for my
B2B campaigns. It was the usual routine—cr aft, edit, post, and
hope for the best.
Then came this seismic shift: The rise of vertical video
platforms.
Initially , I scoffed at the notion, dismissing it as a passing
trend. Wh y would an yone opt for a vertical video? It defied
conventional wisdom and, to be honest, my comfort zone. But
soon, the numbers began speaking a different language—one
that demanded attention.
I stumbled upon a report revealing the sheer dominance of
mobile platforms lik e Instagr am and TikT ok—both
championing the vertical video format. It hit me hard—more
than 75 percent of US adults were dedicating up to two hours
daily to short-form vertical content on their smartphones (Open
Influence, 2022a). TikT oks, IG Reels, YT Shorts—that’ s where the
audience was, soaking up content in a whole new dimension.
Flipping my camer a’s orientation flipped my perspective. I
realized that to resonate with a B2B audience, I needed to meet
them where they were—right on their smartphone screens.
Like having a heart-to-heart video chat with your audience.
For me, the switch was inevitable. I dived headfirst into
vertical videos and reimagined my entire content str ategy .
Rather than sifting through long-form topics my focus was now
to look for bite-sized vertical video content ideas. I
experimented with a few videos and the impact was profound
—vertical videos were more captivating, dr awing in viewers on
content where tr aditional videos failed to engage.
Vertical videos create a more immersive experience, tailor-
made for the short attention spans of toda y’s audience.
Moreover, for B2B influencers, these videos are a golden tick et
—a chance to create deeper connections, tell compelling stories,
and establish authenticity in a format perfectly tailored for
mobile consumption. Videos gave us a new , more intimate and
engaging wa y of storytelling without much effort from the
audience’ s end!
The lesson was clear: evolve or be left behind.
Embr acing vertical video is a tactical and tr ansformative shift
which can redefine your entire influencer content str ategy and
mark eting engine. Videos are no longer just a piece of the

dominated lives.

Long-Form Comeback
Now , let’s fast-forward to toda y. Long-form content is making a
comeback! Y ouTube’ s audiences are leaning into longer videos,
almost lik e traditional TV viewing.
Over time, shorter content formats dominated social media
due to attention spans and the need for quick information.
However, there’ s been a noticeable shift. A udiences are cr aving
depth, authenticity , and substance. This shift is driven b y a
hunger for comprehensive insights and genuine expertise from
trusted influencers.
In recent years, short-form content lik e TikT oks and Reels
took over social media. But it seems this trend might be
changing. Platforms are finding it tough to mak e money from
short videos and the quality is dropping due to too much
content.
Facebook’ s pausing of its creator fund, which gives money to
creators who hit certain goals, shows the struggles of short
content. A ds in short videos don’t bring in enough money
because viewers don’t lik e watching ads between short videos.
Also, there’ s so much low-quality stuff that it’ s hard to mak e
good content that stands out.
Short videos mak e less money compared to longer ones per
minute of watching. This means creators need other wa ys to
earn, lik e selling things, sponsorships, or memberships. T o fix
the problem of too much low-quality stuff, platforms are using
quality measures lik e how long people watch a video or how
much they inter act with it. Creators need to focus on making
high-quality content to get noticed more.
But Y ouTube is going a different wa y. They’re not fighting in
the short video space. Instead, they’re all about long videos and
getting into podcasts. And it’ s working—Y ouTube has wa y more
creators than active podcasts.
Long videos are better for building a connection with your
audience. Short videos get attention, but it’ s hard to build a
relationship with them. Long videos lik e podcasts let you
connect more and give your audience more value. Using long
videos can help you build a strong relationship with your
audience.
Being smart about how you use k eywords, titles, and
descriptions can mak e your long videos more visible on
platforms lik e YouTube. Also, sharing your videos on social
media can help more people find them.
In my journey , I’ve seen some k ey mistak es. Br ands often fall
short in maintaining authenticity , pushing sales pitches r ather
than fostering genuine connections. Influencers sometimes
miss the mark b y neglecting to align their content with the
brand’ s core message or failing to deliver value-driven insights

What TikTok Doesn’t Favor
TikT ok’s algorithm has its preferences, and some metrics don’t
directly influence what you see on your F or You page. Here are
a few that don’t pla y a significant role in shaping TikT ok’s
recommendations:
1. Follower count:  Unlik e some platforms, TikT ok doesn’t

followers a user has. Having a large following doesn’t

2. Previous video performance:  The algorithm isn’t solely
driven b y the history of your videos’ performance. Even if
you haven’t had vir al videos before, great content can still
land on users’ F or You pages.
3. Duplicated content:  Repeated or identical content you’ve
already seen won’t be recommended frequently b y the
algorithm.
4. Spammy content:  TikT ok’s algorithm filters out spam,
seeking to prevent content designed to artificially increase
views or engagement.
The platform is open to diverse content and doesn’t solely favor
established accounts or previous high-performing videos. It
means that an y of your videos can go vir al!
TikTok Metrics
Monitoring analytics provides insights into what content

Regularly review your analytics, test different content

content str ategy:

video. Gr adually , strive for 10,000 to 50,000 views as your
content gains tr action.
Engagement r ate: Aim for an engagement r ate between
3% and 5%. As your audience grows, maintaining a 2% to
3% engagement r ate is a good achievement.
Follower growth:  Starting out, aim for 100 to 500 new
followers per week. With consistent content, growth can
rise to 300 to 1,000 followers weekly .
Watch time:  Initially , target a watch time of 30%–40%.
Gradually push toward 50% or more as your content
improves.
Video completion r ate: Aim for a completion r ate
between 20% and 30% in the beginning. Progressively
work toward 30% to 40% or higher.
Click-through r ate (CTR):  A CTR of 1%–2% is a
reasonable starting point. As your content becomes more
engaging, aim for 2%–3%.
Shares and saves:  Initially , expect a share r ate of around
1% and a save r ate of 5% or less. As your content resonates
better, aim for 1.5%–2% shares and a save r ate of 8% or
more.
These are gener al benchmarks, and your success depends on
various factors lik e content quality , niche, consistency , and
audience engagement. A djust these goals based on your specific
content, audience, and growth r ate over time.

IG Reels Algorithm
The Instagr am Reels algorithm oper ates on sever al key signals
to determine the content a viewer is lik ely to engage with:
User inter action history:  It considers which accounts a
viewer frequently engages with—liking, commenting, or
sharing content from specific creators.
Content preferences:  The algorithm analyzes the type of
content a user engages with the most. F or instance, if
someone enjo ys beauty content, the algorithm ma y
prioritize showing more beauty-related Reels.
Post timing:  When a Reel is posted matters. The algorithm
considers when content is shared to ascertain its
relevance to a user.
Originality and quality:  The algorithm favors original,
high-quality content. It tends to deprioritize content that
appears to be recycled from other platforms or is of low
quality .
Engagement metrics:  The level of engagement (lik es,
comments, shares) a Reel receives influences its visibility .
Higher engagement often leads to more prominent
placement in users’ feeds.
Best Times to Post Instagram Reels:
4 am local time:  This early slot benefits from less
competition, catching users during their initial scroll of
the da y.
Monda y: Start the week strong as Monda ys tend to see
increased user engagement.

IG Subscriptions for Exclusive Content
Use your Reels to advertise exclusive content available to your
subscribers. Instagr am’s subscription feature allows creators to
monetize exclusive access.
Pricing for subscription content starts at $0.99 and goes up to
$99.99 per month (F ourthwall, 2023). Earnings depend on the
number of subscribers you attr act.
Instagr am Subscriptions offer creators a wa y to earn
recurring monthly income b y providing exclusive content and
experiences to their most dedicated followers. Subscribers pa y
a monthly fee to access content highlighted with a purple ring,
standing out in comments and DMs with a subscriber badge.
The progr am includes subscriber badges, exclusive lives,
stories, chats, posts, reels, and a dedicated “Subscriber Home”
on your profile.
Types of Subscription Content
On Instagr am, various types of content can be offered as part of
a subscription to entice and retain dedicated followers. Here
are the primary types:
Exclusive lives:  Live sessions that are only accessible to
subscribers, allowing for intimate inter actions, Q&A
sessions, or behind-the-scenes glimpses.
Exclusive stories:  Stories containing exclusive content,
such as personal insights, sneak peeks, or special
announcements, visible only to subscribers.
Subscriber chats:  A direct chat feature that allows
creators to engage with a limited number of subscribers in
exclusive discussions, providing a more intimate space for
conversation.
Exclusive posts and reels:  Permanent posts and short-
form video content (Reels) shared exclusively with
subscribers, offering authentic and personalized content.
These subscription-exclusive content formats are designed to
create a sense of belonging and exclusivity for followers who
are willing to pa y for more personalized and in-depth
inter actions with their favorite creators.
How to Set it up
Setting up Instagr am Subscriptions involves sever al steps:
Eligibility check:  You must be aged 18+, residing in an
eligible country , and have at least 10,000 followers. Y ou
should also comply with Instagr am’s Partner Monetization
and Content Monetization Policies.
Invitation or availability:  Subscriptions might not be
available to everyone; if you’re eligible, you might receive
an invitation to use the feature. In some regions, it’ s open
to all eligible creators.
Accessing professional dashboard:  Once eligible, access
your Professional Dashboard on Instagr am.
Subscription setup:  In the Professional Dashboard, locate
the “Subscriptions” section. T ap on it to set up your
subscription offering. Here, you can set the subscription
price and see your subscriber list.
Content creation:  Develop exclusive content tailored for
subscribers. This can include exclusive Lives, Stories,
Chats, Posts, or Reels.
Engagement and management:  Inter act with your
subscribers through exclusive content and discussions.
Manage your subscriber list b y blocking, restricting, or
removing subscribers if necessary .
Monitoring earnings and engagement:  Use the
dashboard to tr ack your subscription earnings, new
subscribers, cancellations, and over all engagement.
Setting price points:  Creators set their own subscription
fees. Instagr am allows you to set your own price points for
subscriptions, r anging from $0.99 to $99.99 per month.
When someone subscribes, they are charged the set
amount monthly to access your exclusive content.
Subscriber retention str ategies:  Offers and promotions
to grow and k eep subscribers.
Revenue:  Creators receive 100% of the subscription
revenue gener ated after the taxes are deducted. Apple and
Google k eep 30% of the amount for in-app purchases.
Subscriptions allow followers to pa y a monthly fee to access
exclusive content and experiences offered b y creators.
Subscribers get a unique purple badge to stand out in
comments and DMs, while creators offer exclusive content
within the app’ s environment, building a closer connection with
their most dedicated audience.
Tips to Create Subscription Content
Stay unique:  Focus on what sets you apart to offer
exclusive, can’t-find-an ywhere-else content.
Engage and recognize subscribers:  Reply to comments,
give shoutouts, or host welcome sessions for new
subscribers.

Transparency and communication:  Be clear about your

process.
Surprise and delight:  Offer surprises lik e guest

subscribers.
Creators aged 18+ with 10K+ followers in eligible countries can
use Subscriptions (Instagr am, n.d.).
Access subscriptions  through the “Professional dashboard”
once invited. Manage subscribers, earnings, and content there.
Subscriptions are a wa y for creators to offer additional,
exclusive content to their most dedicated followers while
gener ating revenue directly from their audience’ s support.
Accept Virtual Gifts
For creator accounts, viewers can send virtual gifts during live
Reels. A ccumulate these gifts and exchange them for real
currency .
Virtual gifts on Instagr am are a wa y for viewers to support
creators b y sending them digital gifts during a live stream or
through Instagr am Reels. Here’ s how they work:
1. Availability:  Virtual gifts are currently available only for
creator accounts.
2. Sending gifts:  Viewers can purchase stars (the virtual
currency) within the Instagr am app. These stars come in
packages that r ange from 45 stars for $0.99 to 300 stars for
$5.99 (Perez, 2023).
3. Giving gifts:  During a live stream or on a Reel, viewers
can click on the gift box icon near the comment box. This
opens the gift interface, displa ying various virtual gifts
that can be sent.
4. Star packages:  Once a viewer selects a gift to send, they
can choose how man y stars (associated with real money)
they want to spend on that gift.
5. Earnings for creators:  Creators receive stars as gifts from
their audience during live streams or Reels. These stars
accumulate in the creator ’s account as a virtual currency .
6. Monetization:  Creators can exchange stars for real
money . Instagr am’s policy sets an exchange r ate of $0.01
per star. Creators can cash out their accumulated stars
once their gift balance reaches $25 or more (Ndtvprofit,
2023). It’ s a wa y for audiences to show support and
appreciation for their favorite creators, and for creators to
monetize their content directly through the support of
their audience.
Drive Trafﬁc to External Platforms
Use Reels to direct followers to your website, Y ouTube channel,

How to Get Veriﬁed on Snapchat
Verification on Snapchat isn’t just for A-listers an ymore. It’ s
about letting people know you’re the real deal, not an imposter.
Here’ s how you can get that blue checkmark.
First off, what’ s verification? It’ s that blue badge that shows
you’re the legit star, not a cop ycat. Y ou can even pick your own
cool emoji to go with it.
Now , here’ s the deal: Y ou don’t need to be a big-time celeb. If
you’re rocking tons of views and followers on Snapchat, you’re
eligible. But there’ s a process.
Head to your settings, find “Help” and hit up “Contact Us.”
Tell them you’re being impersonated, causing confusion among
your fans.
Fill out the form, spill the beans about the fak es, and attach
your government ID. This wa y, Snapchat knows you’re the real
deal.
After you’ve hit submit, sit tight for a response. If they sa y no,
don’t sweat it. Try the process one more time.
But hey , what about those cool emojis? They’re unique for
each verified user. So, if you’re in, pick something that screams
“you.”
And there you have it! A little patience, a government ID, and
a sprinkle of persistence could get you that blue checkmark.

Twitch Inﬂuencers
Twitch is a live streaming platform primarily known for
gaming content, where creators broadcast live gamepla y,
inter act with viewers via chat, and build communities around
shared interests. But it’ s not just for gamers; it’ s becoming
increasingly relevant for B2B influencers, br ands, and diverse
users.
Twitch has over 140 million monthly active users (Dean,
2024) and over 6.89 million active streamers in 2023 (Statista,
2024), illustr ating its massive reach and potential for diverse
content creation and engagement. Its potential lies not just in
gaming but in providing a platform for authentic connections,
innovative mark eting, and inter active experiences that cater to
a wide arr ay of interests.
Here’ s wh y it matters.
For B2B Inﬂuencers
Twitch offers a direct and real-time connection with audiences,
allowing B2B influencers to engage deeply and personally with
their followers. It presents an opportunity to diversify content
beyond tr aditional platforms, catering to a more engaged and
inter active audience.
B2B influencers can create communities around specific
industry niches, fostering engagement and discussion among
professionals.
For Brands
Twitch hosts diverse communities, allowing br ands to reach
specific demogr aphics or niche mark ets aligned with their
products or services. Br ands can engage users through
sponsored streams, collabor ations with influencers, or by
hosting their own br anded channels, creating unique mark eting
opportunities. Twitch provides a platform for br ands to show
their human side, engage authentically with audiences, and
build br and trust.
For Users
Twitch offers a r ange of content beyond gaming, including live
talk shows, art creation, music performances, and educational
streams.
Users can participate actively through chat, connect with
creators, and be part of engaging communities sharing common
interests.
It provides a unique experience of real-time inter action,
where users can directly influence content or conversations
during live broadcasts.
For B2B influencers, br ands, and users, Twitch opens doors for
authentic connections, targeted engagement, and novel
mark eting approaches that go beyond tr aditional platforms,
making it a potent tool for community building, content
diversification, and fostering genuine connections in the digital
space.
Twitch Key Features
Twitch offers a suite of features designed to mak e live
streaming and community engagement seamless and
inter active:
Live streaming:  Creators can broadcast live content,
including gaming, talk shows, music, art, and educational
content, fostering real-time engagement with their
audience.
Chat inter action:  Viewers can engage in live chat, inter act
with the streamer, ask questions, and connect with other
community members while the stream is ongoing.
Channel customization:  Creators can personalize their
channels with custom br anding, la youts, and panels to
reflect their unique style and offerings.
Emotes and Bits:  Twitch uses emotes (emoticons) and Bits
(virtual currency) for viewers to express reactions and
support streamers monetarily during live streams.
Subscriptions and donations:  Viewers can subscribe to
channels, unlocking benefits and supporting creators
financially . They can also donate money directly to
support their favorite streamers.
Moder ation tools:  Creators have access to moder ation
tools to manage chat, ban or timeout users, and ensure a
positive and safe environment for their community .
Categories and tags:  Content can be categorized under
specific genres or tags, making it easier for viewers to find
streams related to their interests.
Clips and highlights:  Viewers and creators can create
short clips or highlights from live streams, making it
easier to share and revisit the best moments.
Community engagement:  Twitch fosters a sense of
community through followings, notifications, and
integr ated Discord connections, allowing creators to build
loyal and engaged fanbases.
These features collectively create an immersive and inter active
experience for both creators and viewers, fostering
engagement, community building, and entertainment in real-
time.
Popular Twitch Content Categories
On Twitch, certain content categories tend to attr act larger
audiences and followership due to their popularity and
engagement levels.
Gaming
Gaming content remains the cornerstone of Twitch. Categories
like “Just Chatting,” “Gr and Theft A uto,” “F ortnite,” “League of
Legends,” “W orld of W arcr aft,” and “V alorant” consistently
attract high viewership due to their dedicated fan bases
(Twitchmetrics, n.d.).
Example:  “League of Legends”—streamers engage viewers
with live gamepla y, strategies, and commentary on this widely
popular multipla yer online battle arena (MOB A) game.
IRL (In Real Life)
This category covers a wide r ange of non-gaming content,
including vlogs, cooking, art, music, and other creative
endeavors. It allows streamers to showcase diverse interests
beyond gaming.
Example:  “ASMR ”—streamers showcase their ASMR skills
and inter act with the audience in real-time.
Talk Shows and Podcasts
Twitch shows discussing various topics, including politics,
current events, or interviews, have gained popularity .
Categories lik e “Talk Shows & Podcasts” and “Science &
Technology” often dr aw engaged audiences.
Example:  “The Joe Rogan Experience” podcast on Spotify—
although not exclusively on Twitch, podcasts lik e Joe Rogan’ s
draw huge viewership with discussions on various topics, often
inviting guests for interviews.
Music and Performing Arts
Streams featuring music performances, DJ sessions, or creative
performances fall under this category , attr acting music
enthusiasts and fans.
Example:  “Music—Live Channels”—musicians perform live
concerts, DJ sets, or music production sessions, engaging
audiences with their performances and inter actions.
Just Chatting
This category encompasses casual conversations, discussions,
or even advice sessions. Streamers engage with viewers on
various topics, contributing to its broad appeal.
Example:  “Advice Sessions”—streamers offer advice, discuss
life experiences, or engage in casual conversations, fostering
community inter action and sharing thoughts on diverse topics.
Art and Creativity
Streams dedicated to digital art, painting, gr aphic design, and
creative processes cater to art lovers and those interested in
creative workflows.
Example:  “Digital Art Creation”—artists create digital
illustr ations, designs, or animations, showcasing their creative
process and inter acting with viewers.
Retro and Classic Games
Nostalgia-driven content featuring older games or retro gaming
experiences often garners dedicated viewership among gaming
enthusiasts.
Example:  “Super Mario Bros. Speedruns”—streamers pla y
classic games lik e Super Mario Bros., attempting to complete
them as quickly as possible, attr acting nostalgia-driven viewers.
These categories boast high reach and followership due to their
diverse appeal and engagement potential. Creators focusing on
these categories can tap into existing viewer bases, engage
diverse audiences, and build dedicated communities around
their content.
How to Monetize Twitch Content?
Ninja, a renowned streamer, reportedly earns millions yearly
from subscriptions, ads, and sponsorships.
Streamers lik e Pokimane or xQc gener ate substantial revenue
through subscriptions, donations, and exclusive content.
Twitch Partner Program
Win Twitch partnership b y meeting Twitch’ s criteria (aver age
concurrent viewers, broadcast frequency , content adherence).
Partners can earn from ads, subscriptions, and Bit
contributions.
Twitch Partner Progr am qualification criteria (Elja yem, 2023):
Average concurrent viewers (A CV):  Aim for a consistent
high number of concurrent viewers, often estimated
between 100 to 300 viewers or more during streams.
Sustained high viewership over time is crucial.
Streaming schedule:  Maintain a consistent streaming
schedule, ideally sever al times a week, for a few hours
each session, showcasing dedication and engagement.
Content quality:  Produce high-quality content with
engaging inter actions, fostering an active and supportive
community . Inter action metrics lik e chat activity , remote
usage, and subscriber engagement are vital.
Channel growth metrics:  Aim for steady growth in
followership, channel views, and subscribers. While
specific numbers aren’t disclosed, a consistent upward
trend signifies an engaged and expanding audience.
Content adherence:  Strictly adhere to Twitch’ s terms of
service, community guidelines, and cop yright regulations
to maintain a clean and supportive channel environment.
Potential:  Partners receive 50 percent of subscription revenue
(Tier 1 subscription is $4.99/month), Bits revenue varies (1 Bit =
$0.01 to the streamer).
Twitch Afﬁliate Program
Qualify for the Affiliate Progr am (minimum viewership and
streaming requirements). Affiliates earn from subscriptions,
Bits, and game sales.
To qualify , you must (Twitch Help Portal, n.d.):
Meet minimum stream requirements:  Stream for a
minimum of eight hours within a 30-da y period.
Complete seven da ys streamed:  Stream on at least seven
different da ys within the 30-da y period.
Have minimum aver age concurrent viewers:  Maintain
an aver age of three concurrent viewers or more during
streams.
Fifty followers:  Reach a minimum of 50 followers on your
channel.
Adhere to platform T&Cs:  Similar to the Partner
Progr am, ensure compliance with Twitch’ s terms and
guidelines.
Potential:  Affiliates get a 50 percent share from subscriptions
(Tier 1 subscription is $4.99/month), a portion of Bits revenue,
and a cut from games sold through their channel.
Ad Revenue
Run pre-roll, mid-roll, or displa y ads during streams (available
for Partners).
Potential:  Ad revenue varies based on viewer count, ad
frequency , and audience engagement but can be
significant for high-viewer streams. A dditionally , it’s
important to understand the revenue-sharing model, with
ad revenue earned at a 55 percent net ad share for both
Affiliates, who gener ate revenue from running three
minutes of ads or more per hour, and Partners, who
participate in the A ds Incentive Progr am. The 55 percent
net ad share refers to the portion of the gross ad revenue
that creators receive, with the actual gross amount subject
to variation based on factors such as taxable location,
withholding r ates, or fees (Twitch Help Portal, n.d.).
Donations and Bits
Encour age donations from viewers or accept Bits (Twitch’ s
virtual currency).
Potential:  Donations vary widely; Bits revenue depends
on viewer contributions (1 Bit = $0.01 to the streamer).
Additionally , when your viewers perform and confirm an
action that requires Bits within the extension on your
channel page, you’ll earn 80% of 1 US cent per Bit used,
with the remaining 20% shared with the extension
developer. It’ s important to note that the Bits in Extensions
progr am, including revenue share, ma y be adjusted from
time to time or depreciated b y Twitch at its sole discretion
(Twitch Help Portal, n.d.).
Merchandising and Sponsorships
Sell br anded merchandise or collabor ate with sponsors for
brand promotions.
Potential:  Earnings depend on sales and the nature of
sponsorship deals but can offer additional revenue
streams.
Exclusive Content or Subscriptions
Offer exclusive content to subscribers or provide perks for
higher-tier subscriptions. Exclusive content drives subscription
growth and provides additional revenue.
The revenue potential on Twitch is vast, but success often
requires consistent streaming, engaging content, and building a
loyal audience. B y diversifying income streams and engaging
with viewers, you can gr adually increase your revenue
potential on the platform.

Discord Inﬂuencers
Discord is a robust, community-based platform initially
designed for gamers to communicate via voice, video, and text
channels. However, it has evolved into a versatile space for
various communities, including influencers, to engage with
their audiences.
For influencers, Discord offers a unique, dedicated space to
connect intimately with followers. Unlik e other social media
platforms, Discord enables real-time inter actions and fosters a
sense of belonging within the community . This direct
engagement builds stronger relationships and cultivates a lo yal
fan base.
Discord oper ates as a versatile platform catering to users,
brands, and creators in distinctive yet interconnected wa ys.
Here’ s a break down of its functionality and significance.
For Users
Discord serves as a communication hub offering text, voice, and
video channels. It allows users to engage in real-time
conversations, fostering a sense of community and connection.
Users can join diverse communities aligned with their
interests, hobbies, or fandoms, allowing them to inter act with
like-minded individuals.
Discord provides a space for users to access exclusive content,
engage with creators, and be part of private communities.
For Brands
Brands lever age Discord to engage directly with their audience,
fostering br and lo yalty . It’s a platform for br ands to build
dedicated communities around their products, services, or
content, encour aging customer lo yalty and advocacy .
Discord offers mark eting opportunities through sponsored
events, collabor ations, or exclusive promotions to engage with
their target audience.
For Creators
Discord allows creators to engage deeply with their audience,
providing direct support, exclusive content, and fostering a
sense of belonging.
It serves as a space for creators to monetize their content
through memberships, donations, merchandise sales, and
exclusive perks.
Discord facilitates content sharing, collabor ation, and
networking among creators, enabling them to expand their
reach and create diverse content.
As of 2024, Discord has over 196 million active users,
signaling its growing influence and potential for deeper
explor ation and utilization (Smith, 2024).
However, despite its substantial user base, Discord is yet to be
fully discovered and lever aged b y man y. Its expansive
capabilities, particularly for creators and br ands, remain
relatively untapped.
Key Features of Discord
Discord offers sever al key features that mak e it a popular
platform for communication, community-building, and
collabor ation:
Text, voice, and video communication:  Users can engage
in real-time text chats, voice calls, or video calls either
privately or within a group.
Server organization:  Discord is structured around
servers, which can be created for specific interests,
communities, or topics. Servers are further divided into
channels for better organization.
Channel variety:  Within servers, users can access
different types of channels lik e text channels for
discussions, voice channels for live conversations, and
announcement channels for important updates.
Roles and permissions:  Discord allows server owners to
assign roles with specific permissions to users, controlling
their access to various channels and functionalities.
Emojis and reactions:  Users can express themselves
using emojis, reactions, and custom emojis within
messages to enhance engagement and communication.
Bots and integr ations:  Discord supports bots and
integr ations that offer various functionalities, from
moder ation and music pla yback to automated
notifications and games.
File sharing:  Users can easily share images, videos, links,
and other files within Discord, making it a versatile
platform for content sharing and collabor ation.
Community inter action:  It fosters a sense of community
through features lik e public and private servers, member
statuses, and customizable server invitations.
Security and moder ation:  Discord provides moder ation
tools, allowing server admins to manage and moder ate
conversations, ensuring a safe and positive environment.
These features collectively mak e Discord a flexible and
inter active platform suitable for various purposes, from casual
conversations and gaming communities to professional
collabor ations and content creation.
Content Formats Available on Discord
Text channels:  Ideal for discussions, sharing updates, and
exchanging information. These channels can be
categorized into different topics or themes for organized

Voice channels:  Enable live voice conversations, podcasts,

Video channels:  Some servers have integr ated video
channels, allowing creators to host live streams, conduct

File sharing:  Discord allows the sharing of various media

Discord’ s unique community-oriented design has attr acted

How to Grow Your Following on Discord
Engage on Text Channels
Develop diverse text channels focusing on different topics or
interests relevant to your audience. Create segmented text

regularly .
Encour age discussions, share exclusive content, and prompt

Interactive Voice Sessions
Regularly schedule voice sessions lik e Q&As, casual chats, or

Example:  YouTuber Jacksepticeye hosts monthly voice
chats on Discord, providing a more intimate experience
for his Discord community .
Exclusive Video Channels
Introduce video channels to share exclusive content, behind-

Example:  Musician T-Pain’ s Discord server features

footage, live studio sessions, and Q&A sessions.
Encourage Collaboration and File Sharing
Create a space where members can share their creations,
whether it’ s artwork, music, or videos. Encour age collabor ation
among members, nurturing a sense of community ownership
within the server. Encour age members to share their creations,
collabor ate, and provide feedback within the server.
Example:  Artist RossDr aws invites members to share their
artwork, offers critique sessions, and occasionally features

Consistent Engagement
Actively participate in discussions, respond to messages, and
acknowledge member contributions. Consistency in your
engagement showcases your commitment and encour ages
others to participate. A cknowledge member contributions and
create a welcoming atmosphere.
Example:  YouTuber Markiplier actively engages with his
Discord community , responding to messages, joining voice
chats, and regularly sharing updates.
Promotion and Integration
Integr ate your Discord server across your social media
platforms, Y ouTube channel, or website. Invite your existing
audience and highlight the value of joining the community to
create curiosity and interest.
Example:  Streamer V alkyr ae integr ates Discord
promotion on her Reddit channel and streams, inviting

inter actions.
By utilizing these channels effectively and consistently
engaging with your audience, you’ll create an environment that
not only attr acts but retains and nurtures a growing following
on Discord.
