Crisis Management in Influencer
Marketing
Imagine overseeing a star influencer, basking in the success of a
lucrative br and collabor ation, only to wak e to a storm of
negative comments and a sinking feeling in your gut. This isn’t
an uncommon thing, especially with just about the entire planet
on one social media platform or another.
Crises don’t knock politely in the creator world—they barge
in uninvited. While you ma y have carefully cur ated your
influencer ’s creative adventures, nothing can truly prepare you
for the unexpected setbacks that arise, save for experience.
The success narr ative is not the same for all, and while your
influencer ma y be riding a smooth wave compared to some of
their peers, the chances are their competitors are more battle-
tested, having weathered their own setbacks. This puts them
one step ahead, and when the moment of crisis arrives, it ma y
threaten to devour your influencer and give wa y to their more
prepared competitors.
About two years ago, I went through this myself. I shared a
post intended to resonate with a specific audience, but it took
an unexpected detour, landing in the eye of a controversy
tornado. The fallout exposed the gaps in the influencer ’s—and
by extension, the manager ’s—preparedness for the
unpredictable nature of the digital world.
Crisis management is the safety net every influencer manager
must have in their toolkit. It’ s the lifeboat that can k eep your
influencer afloat when reputation damage, partnership
quagmires, or unexpected data storms threaten to capsize their
efforts. In the Creator Economy , where the tides of success and
failure can shift r apidly , being equipped to navigate these
treacherous waters is not just a luxury , but a necessity .
The Anatomy of an Inﬂuencer Crisis
Potential crises are uninvited plot twists, r anging from your
influencer accidentally stepping on the wrong side of their
audience’ s values, to legal contr actual shutdowns. A misstep
could lead to a cliffhanger—will their audience stick around for
the next chapter, or will they perish in the face of setbacks?
The Audience Backlash
Your influencer cr afts a story , expecting thunderous applause,
only to be met with a sudden, adverse reaction from their
listeners. Sometimes, an innocent comment or piece of content
can rub the audience the wrong wa y, leading to a barr age of
negative comments, unfollows, or a dent in the influencer ’s
credibility . This often occurs due to a creator-audience
mismatch, catching the influencer off guard as the waves of
discontent cr ash against their carefully cur ated digital shores.
Brand Partnership Nightmares
Imagine overseeing an influencer who has partnered with a
million-dollar br and, only to realize they’re headed in
completely different directions. Although creators are mostly
flexible, going against their values can put a dent in their
authenticity and credibility . When that happens, the influencer
remains of no use to their viewers or the br and. Similarly , the
influencer ma y clash with the br and over content, pa yment
issues, or misaligned expectations, turning a promising
collabor ation into a dispute nightmare.
Legal Labyrinths
Your influencer is on a quest, following a path they thought was
clear, until suddenly , they find themselves ensnared in a legal
tangle. From unintentional cop yright infringements to privacy
violations or even facing defamation allegations, legal woes can
quickly turn an influencer ’s journey into a maze of
complexities.
Data Breach Dilemmas
The influencer has gathered precious artifacts on their quest,
only to have them stolen b y digital thieves. Similarly , a data
breach in the influencer ’s world can compromise personal or
audience data, eroding trust and leaving them gr appling with
the fallout.
Community Discord
Imagine the influencer ’s supporting char acters—their lo yal
followers—turning against them. A single insensitive remark or
action can alienate the community , leading to a rift that affects
engagement, lo yalty , and ultimately , the influencer ’s influence.
As you’re working with influencers, it’ s vital that you’re adept
at crisis management due to ever-changing platform rules,
variable user behavior, and diverse br and needs. Creating and
following a well-thought-out crisis management str ategy ,
connecting on more communication channels, and helping your
influencers build a resilient relationship with their audience
are essential to weathering an y storm that might arise.
Identifying and Reporting a Creator Crisis
Your br and’ s reputation is par amount to your success. Crisis
identification and reporting safeguard your credibility , as a
crisis left uncheck ed can significantly damage your online
identity . Nearly 94 percent of consumers are lik ely to be lo yal to
a brand that offers complete tr ansparency , particularly in times
of crisis (Emarsys, 2021).
Timely crisis identification and assessment allows for
proactive measures to reduce the long-term repercussions.
Positive relationships with partners, clients, and collabor ators
are vital for B2B influencers’ success. Crisis management
demonstr ates responsibility and reliability , preserving these
valuable connections.
Swift crisis identification also helps influencers sta y
compliant with legal and regulatory requirements.
Approximately 55 percent of consumers believe that companies
should tak e a stand on social, environmental, and political
issues, emphasizing the importance of ethical and compliant
behavior (Harvard Business School, 2021).
The Crisis Management Playbook
Here’ s how you can fulfill your responsibility as a crisis-ready
influencer:
Step 1: Identify the Issue
Collect all available information about the crisis, including
social media posts, messages, or emails related to the incident.
Document the date, time, specifics of the incident, and an y
initial reactions or comments from your audience or
stakeholders.
Ask yourself:  What exactly happened? Who is involved or
affected? When did it occur? Is it an ongoing issue?
Step 2: Assess Impact and Scope
Evaluate potential repercussions on audience trust, br and
reputation, partnerships, and legal implications. Collect
information on potential reach downtime, severity of impact,
and an y historical precedents, if applicable.
Ask yourself:  How severe is the issue? Who might be
affected, and to what extent? What are the worst-case
scenarios?
Step 3: Recognize Stakeholders Involved
Identify all parties affected—your audience, collabor ators,
partners—and assess their perspectives. Create a list of
stakeholders, their relationship to the issue, and their potential
concerns.
Ask yourself:  Who might be impacted b y this issue? What
might their reactions be? What are their priorities or
expectations?
Step 4: Evaluate Response Options
Brainstorm response str ategies and assess their potential
outcomes and feasibility . Analyze different response options,
their pros and cons, and their potential effects on stak eholders.
Ask yourself:  What immediate actions can be tak en?
What are the potential outcomes of each action? What
aligns best with our values and goals?
Step 5: Develop a Detailed Action Plan
Create a step-b y-step plan with assigned responsibilities and a
clear timeline. Define k ey tasks, responsibilities,
communication guidelines, and a timeline for each action.
Ask yourself:  Who will do what, and b y when? How will
we communicate internally and externally?
Step 6: Communicate Clearly and Timely
Share the crisis report and management plan with relevant
stakeholders clearly and promptly . Use all communication
channels, determine the k ey messages, and choose the right
platforms to address the situation.
Ask yourself:  How can we communicate this effectively?
Who needs to be informed and when?
Step 7: Monitor and Adapt
Continuously monitor the situation, adapt the plan as needed,
and reassess the effectiveness of actions tak en. Collect feedback,
reactions, and an y new developments related to the crisis.
Ask yourself:  Is our plan working? Do we need to adjust
anything based on new information?
As creators, influencers are responsible for crisis identification,
reporting, and management. It matters because it defines your
commitment to your audience, partners, and the industry . It
shows integrity and a dedication to maintaining a trustworth y
and reliable presence in the B2B space. Crisis management
protects your identity and helps you uphold the trust of your
audience and business stak eholders for long-term success.
Rebuilding from the Ashes: Six Strategies for

When a crisis strik es, the immediate focus is often on

the true test of resilience lies in the aftermath—in the ability to
rebuild, restore trust, and emerge from the storm even stronger
than before.
As an influencer manager, your role in the post-crisis

Reclaim the Narrative: Shift the Focus Back to Your
Inﬂuencer’s Core
In the wak e of a crisis, the narr ative can quickly spir al out of
control, with external voices and critics dominating the
conversation. Y our first task in the rebuilding process is to

influencer ’s core values, accomplishments, and commitment to

Encour age your influencer to tak e full accountability for their
missteps, expressing genuine remorse and a commitment to
making amends. This displa y of humility and vulner ability can
go a long wa y in rebuilding trust and humanizing your
influencer in the eyes of their audience.
Lever age various content formats, from heartfelt video
messages to thoughtful blog posts, to share your influencer ’s

they’re taking to rectify the situation, such as collabor ating with
industry experts, revising their content guidelines, or
implementing new safeguards to prevent future incidents.
By actively shaping the narr ative and shifting the focus back
to your influencer ’s core values and renewed dedication to
their cr aft, you can begin to counter act the negative press and

Reconnect with the Audience: Cultivate Empathy
and Transparency
In the aftermath of a crisis, the most critical task is to reconnect
with your influencer ’s audience and rebuild the shattered trust.
This process requires a delicate balance of empath y,
transparency , and a genuine commitment to addressing the

Encour age your influencer to engage in direct, personal

Moreover, consider inviting your audience to participate in

By fostering this empathetic, audience-centric approach, you

Strengthen Internal Systems and Processes
While reconnecting with your audience is crucial, the true long-
term resilience of your influencer ’s brand lies in the strength of

Importantly , be tr ansparent about these internal

Diversify Revenue Streams and Partnerships
A crisis can often have a devastating impact on an influencer ’s

Encour age your influencer to explore new revenue-

Leverage Evergreen Content and Thought

Getting Identified as an
Influencer Yourself
We’ve spent a lot of this book discussing how to work with
influencers but what if you want to become one yourself? If
you’re curious about how to get started in this journey , read on.
For me, starting out as an influencer felt lik e entering a whole
new world—lots of excitement and a chance to “hit it big” but
there were also tons of unknowns too. I quickly learned that
being an influencer isn’t as easy as it seems.
Becoming a pro influencer is more than just about posting
content; you are constantly switching gears mentally . You go
from being an amateur and creating stuff for fun to having a
clear game plan and being super intentional about what you
share.
I fell into the tr ap of thinking that success would hit me lik e a
lightning bolt. But truth be told, it requires blood, sweat, long
nights, and undying dedication. Y ou need to be very patient and
keep true to your path, even when it feels lik e nothing’ s
happening.
When I started, I thought I had to be an instant hit or cop y
what the big influencers were doing. But that didn’t work. It
only made me feel stressed and kind of fak e. And before I knew
it, I was under the influence of “Imposter S yndrome.” My
previous work that had made me feel proud of myself was
triggering my insecurities. I started to feel lik e a fr aud and was
down the r abbit hole of questioning my abilities, skills, and self-
worth.
The real trick was to tak e it slow , celebr ate small wins, and
not stress over becoming an overnight sensation. Being my true
self and not comparing my journey with others was really
helpful for me.
I had to be super careful not to get lost in the noise of creating
content without a real plan. Setting goals, sta ying real, and
being myself—those were the things that really helped me
navigate this new world.
Success in this game isn’t about luck. It’ s a mix of steady
effort, learning from slip-ups, and not giving up. It’ s all about
finding your thing, knowing your audience, and k eeping it real.
Transitioning from an amateur to a pro influencer isn’t just
about what you create; it’ s about sticking to your passion,
putting in the hours, and building real connections.
Amateurs vs. Professionals
The common understanding is that amateurs don’t mak e real
money online. They are usually in it for fun or as a hobb y. They
might not have a clear str ategy , and their content creation
might be spor adic. They do what feels right in the moment and
lack a structured plan.
On the other hand, a professional influencer treats their
creation lik e a business. They’re intentional about what they
share, have a clear str ategy , and are consistent. They create and
share content FOR their audience, not for themselves.
Their long-term focus is building a br and and delivering
value consistently . Most professional influencers are perceived
to be committed, hard-working, and people who tak e the time
to learn and grow—and obviously mak e more money than an y
new entr ant.
Let’s talk a bit more about the word “amateur.” It’ s not a
critique; it’ s a phase in your journey . It means you’re not yet
doing this as a full-time gig—in other words, you’re not r aking
in the cash just yet.
But trust me, there’ s a world of difference when you start
earning from what you love.
Picture this: W orking from home, calling the shots on your
schedule, and owning your life. That’ s the kind of freedom
being a professional influencer offers.
Here’ s the hard truth: Getting there isn’t a strok e of luck. It
takes a lot of intent, grind, and time. If someone’ s pitching you a
get-rich-quick scheme in this field, they’re not telling you the
whole story .
The shift from being an amateur to a professional concerns
your mindset more than an ything else. Y ou tak e what you love
and turn it into something phenomenal, well-directed, and
valuable.
How Does Money “Happen” Online?
Let’s demystify the money side of things. W e’ve already chatted

But who’ s footing the bill for these pros?
Money doesn’t just pop out of thin air. People shell out cash
for things they find valuable. So, as a creator, your gig is to
create that value for others.
Here’ s the rundown:
Your Squad
Your audience is your ace in the hole. These folks are gold.
They’ve got problems, desires, dreams. Y our mission? Be their
fixer, guide, or genie.
Take my pal Alex, for instance. He is into homemade tech
innovations, but not just an y gadgets—exclusively for DIY

The Third-Party Players
Brands and other parties have their own game going. They are

Think of it lik e this book. My book caters to aspiring

Bottom line? Y ou solve problems or mak e dreams come true,

Brands? They’re on the look out for audiences lik e yours to

Now that you know the difference between amateurs and

Goal-Setting
I was navigating the influencer space when a major br and

That’ s when it click ed—this is not about promotion; it’ s about

Here’ s the deal: B2B goals usually revolve around two main

Let’s put it under the microscope.
Influencers possess a powerful asset—their followers,

Brands want more than sales—they want to win customers’

Influencers bring authenticity to the table. When they

So, b y creating genuine, relatable content that connects with

It’s a powerful synergy—the business meets its br and growth

Now let’ s talk about setting goals—a game-changing pr actice

The Aha Moment
When I began, I was all about the content, focusing solely on

I will be honest. The idea of goal-setting was overwhelming

Beyond the surface goals lik e increased visibility or

Niche vs. Premise
“Find your niche” used to be the golden rule for creators, but
here’ s the thing—it’ s confusing and outdated.
A niche is essentially a small, specialized segment of the
mark et that often focuses on a specific audience or topic. Think
of it as a corner of the vast creative world where you fit snugly .
However, this concept can sometimes feel limiting and elusive.
Now , let’s talk about something more accur ate and genuinely
helpful: Your premise.
Your premise is the heartbeat of your content or br and. It’ s
that concise, crystal-clear statement that encapsulates what
you’re all about. It goes beyond “what” you’re doing to “wh y”
you’re doing it.
This shift from the niche to a premise moves you, as an
influencer, from a tin y box to a wide-open field where your
creativity can truly flourish.
When I was starting out, the idea of a niche felt confining. I
was trying to fit into this predetermined box, desper ately
attempting to carve out a space in an already crowded mark et.
It was when I stumbled upon the idea of a premise that
everything changed. I realized I wasn’t just creating content for
the sak e of it—I had a unique perspective, a purpose that set me
apart.
To find your premise, ask yourself some k ey questions:
Who are your audience?
What problems or dreams do you address for them?
How does your approach differ from what’ s already out
there?
For me, it wasn’t an instantaneous revelation. It was a process
of self-reflection, trial, and error. I found my premise b y delving
into wh y I’m passionate about helping creators. T oday, I don’t
just post r andom content; I provide evidence-back ed insights
that truly mak e a difference in my viewers’ journey .
Your premise is your North Star in the creative universe. It’ s
what guides you, resonates with your audience, and sets you
apart in a crowded space.
So, hold on to your niche but hold your premise closer—it’ s
where your authentic, impactful storytelling begins.
Premise, Values, and SDGs
Personal values and Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) can
beautifully align with your premise as a creator. Lik e I said,
your premise is rooted in wh y you do it and the impact you
wish to mak e. This is where personal values and SDGs pla y a
pivotal role.
Your personal values are the cornerstone of your premise.
They reflect your beliefs, ethics, and the principles you stand
for. When you infuse these values into your creativity , it wins
more authenticity and deep resonation with your audience.
For instance, if your core values revolve around
environmental conservation, your premise might focus on
spreading awareness about sustainable living pr actices or
advocating for eco-friendly products. This alignment ensures
that your content is a genuine reflection of your beliefs,
creating an authentic connection with your audience who share
similar values.
Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)
These global targets aim to address various social, economic,
and environmental challenges b y 2030 (United Nations, n.d.).
Aligning your premise with SDGs means integr ating these goals
into your content str ategy , actively contributing to causes that
support the SDGs.
Let’s say one of the SDGs is gender equality . If this resonates
with your values, your premise might revolve around
empowering women through financial liter acy or advocating
for equality in tr aditionally male-dominated industries.
Here are some questions to guide you in aligning your
personal values with your premise and finding connections to
SDGs.
Personal values:
–What values drive my decisions and actions in life?
–How do I want to impact the world positively?
–What causes or issues am I deeply passionate about?
–What are my long-term aspir ations, and how do they
align with my values?
–What unique perspectives or experiences do I bring
that can contribute to positive change?
Defining your premise:
–What am I passionate about creating?
–Who are my target audience, and what are their
needs?
–How can I create content that resonates with both my
audience and my values?
–What sets me apart from others in my field or niche?
Connecting with SDGs:
–Which SDGs align closely with my values and
premise?
–How can my content contribute to r aising awareness
or actively supporting specific SDGs?
–In what wa ys can I integr ate SDGs into my content
while maintaining authenticity?
–Are there specific SDGs that resonate with both my
audience and me?
Reflecting on these questions can help you identify the
intersections between your personal values, the core of your
content premise, and how they can align with broader global
objectives outlined in the SDGs.
Aligning personal values and SDGs with your premise reflects
your authenticity in your content. It shows how you live and
breathe your “cause” in every piece of content you create, in
every inter action with your audience, and in every decision you
mak e as a creator.
This alignment adds depth, purpose, and authenticity to your
work to create a stronger connection with your audience while
contributing positively to the world around you.
How To Get Identiﬁed as an Inﬂuencer
Lever age creator-first platforms for effective influencer

Why Are You Not Getting Noticed?
About five years into my journey as a creator, I felt a bit stuck.
No matter how much effort I poured into my work, it felt lik e I
was struggling to break through. When people discussed top
creators or recommended podcasts, my name r arely popped up.
I was lost in the noise. People barely noticed me as a creator .
It was disheartening.
So, I decided to dig deeper. I ask ed around and found out how
people perceived my work. Their responses were interesting.
They mentioned words lik e “authentic,” “innovative,” and
“community-oriented,” but only a handful associated my work
with the term “creator.”
That was a wak e-up call.
Let me tell you about a psychological concept called “cued
recall.” When people seek recommendations, they use specific
words as cues to recall suggestions. My work wasn’t connected
to the term “creator,” so I was often overlook ed in these
conversations.
That missing association was holding me back.
Conversations about creators were happening everywhere,
all the time. And when those conversations start working in
your favor, when people are cued to recommend Y OU, that’ s
when things turn magical.
But how do you mak e that happen?
The Power of Association
Creating valuable content is crucial, but in toda y’s world, it’ s
just the starting line. What matters equally , if not more, is your
brand. Not just your br and name, but what your work stands
for. Y our content needs to resonate with a specific idea.
Consider some fresh examples:
Sarah Johnson: Mindful parenting
Alex Chen: Sustainable living
Michelle W aters: Creative problem-solving
When your work is intrinsically link ed to an idea, it doesn’t just
spread; it creates a strong, engaged audience.
Building Association
There are three essential steps to establish association:
Step 1: Selection
This initial phase involves choosing what you want to be
associated with. It could be a word, phr ase, idea, or a
combination that encapsulates the essence of your content or
brand:
Be specific but not limiting: Strive for a focused
association that’ s neither overly broad nor excessively
niche. Find a balance that resonates with your audience
while being distinct enough to stand out.
Intersection of ideas: Consider positioning yourself at the
crossroads of two concepts. It can help carve out a unique
space that’ s appealing yet less crowded, allowing you to
create a blue ocean str ategy .
When I realized my work wasn’t associated with “creators,” I
rebr anded my content to be more aligned with that term,
though it’ s a competitive field. I focused on a broader term to
appeal to a larger audience while acknowledging the challenge
of competing in a crowded space.
Step 2: Expression
Once you’ve chosen your association, the next crucial step is to
express your ideas or content in a wa y that aligns with this
association while setting you apart from others:
Differentiation is k ey: Strive to articulate your
perspectives uniquely . Don’t echo what others in your field
are already communicating. Originality and a distinct
point of view are crucial for standing out.
Authenticity matters: Lever age your personal experiences,
perspectives, or skills to provide a fresh tak e. Authentic
expression enhances your credibility and mak es your
content more relatable.
In my attempt to compete in the crowded space of “creator ”
content, I focused on different perspectives within the Creator
Economy , such as the balance between creator-educators and
creator-entertainers. This allowed me to offer a new angle
within a familiar domain.
Step 3: Repetition
Building association isn’t a one-time event; it requires
consistent reinforcement. Repetition solidifies the connection
between your br and or content and the chosen association in
the minds of your audience:
Consistent messaging: Regularly reinforce your
association through your content, ensuring that your
chosen ideas or themes are consistently communicated.
Familiarity breeds connection: People tend to feel more
connected to familiar concepts or br ands. Repetition helps
create this familiarity , making your association more
memor able.
Much lik e neuroscientist Andrew Huberman emphasizes
insights on neuroplasticity and repetition, I recognized the
power of repetition. I didn’t stop at expressing unique
perspectives once; I embr aced repeating these perspectives to
strengthen the association with my br and.
When people see your work, they should react lik e, “Didn’t he
post this before?”
Creating an association isn’t just about being visible; it’ s about
being synon ymous with a particular cue. It’ s about being the
first name that pops up in people’ s minds when triggered.
Here’s a Little To-Do
Ask yourself, What word, idea, or movement do you want to be
linked with? Is it distinct, memor able, and does it pique
interest?
Who am I serving?
Who is my intended audience or community?
What are their needs, desires, or pain points?
How can my content address these specific aspects?
What sets me apart?
What unique perspectives, experiences, or skills do I
bring to the table?
How does my approach differ from others in my
field?
What distinct value do I offer that stands out?
Why should people remember me?
What impression do I want to leave on my audience?
What emotions or reactions do I aim to evok e
through my content?
What memor able aspect about my work do I want
people to recall?
What can I be consistently associated with?
What word, phr ase, or idea represents the core
essence of my content or br and?
Is this association both unique and appealing?
How can I express this association consistently across
my content?
How does my association resonate with my audience?
Have I tested this association with my audience or
community?
Does this association align with their interests,
preferences, or expectations?
What feedback have I received regarding this
association?
What do I want my legacy to be?
How does this association contribute to my long-term
goals?
How do I envision my br and or content being
remembered in the future?
What impact do I aim to create through this
association?
These questions can serve as guideposts to help you navigate
and define the association you want to establish with your
audience or community .
Two Key Indicators of an Inﬂuencer’s Success
Trust and attention are the bedrock of influence in toda y’s
world. However, earning them isn’t a stroll in the park. It
demands creating and distributing top-notch content that
resonates with your audience. When I embark ed on my
influencer journey , I realized I needed not only to become the
center of attention among my audience but also to win their
trust.
But it’ s a tough nut to cr ack. It’ s human nature to be cautious
and wary of the unknown. Breaking the ice and looking
beneath the surface is the trick behind successfully winning
anyone’ s trust. Once you convince someone that you mean well
and can solve their problems, most people tend to trust you
from that point onwards.
Choose Your Medium
One of the first-ever steps in this pursuit is str ategically
choosing the right medium and format. This is a pivotal
decision. Think of it as the canvas for your creativity . Each
medium—writing, audio, or video—brings its own strengths
and challenges:
Writing:  If you’re dr awn to the written word, writing
offers the power to articulate thoughts with precision. Y et,
it can be quite daunting, often requiring profound thought
before the pen hits the paper. It’ s a skill that cultivates
clear thinking and efficient information tr ansfer.
Audio:  Audio, on the other hand, provides a platform for
those who excel in speaking. Podcasting or professional
speaking might be your forte. Speaking often correlates
with quick, efficient thought processes—ideal for engaging
conversations.
Video:  Then there’ s video—the current powerhouse in
audience growth. Platforms favoring video-centric content
are phenomenal for audience building. However, creating
great videos involves multiple skills—scripting, editing,
performing—demanding a learning curve.
Choose Your Format
Once you’ve settled on your medium, the next step is format:
Short-form  content reigns supreme in toda y’s social
media landscape, offering swift audience growth. Y et, it’ s
fleeting. Its ephemer al nature means you’re often on a
content creation treadmill.
Long-form content , in contr ast, ensures lasting value. It’ s
not just about the length; it’ s about creating content that’ s
enduring, easily shareable, and remains relevant long
after it’ s published. This could be Y ouTube videos, essa ys,
newsletters, or podcast episodes.
Multi-Format Approach to Inﬂuencer Content
Marketing
I leaned toward a multi-format approach r ather than hitching
onto one medium. This diversified str ategy allowed me to cater
to diverse audience preferences. I dabbled in writing, ventured
into podcasts, and experimented with videos. The goal was to
create content that endured, resonated, and brought long-term
value to my audience.
A multi-format approach involves creating content in various
mediums or formats to engage with diverse audience
preferences. Implementing this str ategy requires
understanding your strengths, audience behavior, and the
unique value each format offers.
Let’s break it down:
Understanding strengths
Identify your strengths and preferences. Are you a
compelling writer? Do you excel at speaking or hosting
conversations? Are you comfortable facing the camer a?
Knowing where you shine allows you to lever age those
strengths across different formats.
Audience behavior
Analyze your audience. Do they prefer consuming content
via podcasts during commutes? Are they dr awn to
engaging visuals on social media? Understanding how
your audience consumes content helps tailor your multi-
format str ategy to meet their needs.
Medium selection
Choose the mediums that align with your strengths and
audience behavior. This could include writing blogs or
articles, producing podcasts or audio content, creating
videos for Y ouTube or social media platforms, or even
hosting live sessions.
Content adaptation
Repurpose your content across different formats. F or
instance, a blog article could be tr ansformed into a
podcast episode b y narr ating it or discussing its k ey points.
The same content might be distilled into a short video or
infogr aphic for social media platforms.
Consistency and cohesion
Ensure a cohesive br and voice and message across
formats. Even though the medium varies, maintaining
consistency in your content style, values, and the core
message is crucial for audience familiarity and trust. F or
example, let’ s say you’re an influencer focusing on
personal finance. Y ou might adopt a multi-format
approach b y:
writing in-depth articles about investment str ategies
on your blog
creating podcasts where you discuss financial tips
and interview experts in the field
making short educational videos explaining
budgeting techniques or mark et trends on social
media platforms
conducting live Q&A sessions on Instagr am or
YouTube to inter act directly with your audience and
address their financial queries
However, this path is not without challenges. The lure of short-
form content for immediate growth is potent. Balancing short-
form with the enduring value of long-form content was tricky .
How to Strike a Balance Between Long-Form and
Short-Form Content
Micro to Macro Storytelling
Craft a short-form snippet teasing a compelling story or idea
and then gr adually unfold the narr ative across long-form
content, building anticipation and depth.
This engages audience curiosity , driving sustained interest
and anticipation for the full narr ative.
Short-Burst Info Nuggets
Share quick, informational bursts (lik e tips, quotes, or stats) in
short-form content, and expand on each point in detail through
long-form articles or videos.
This offers quick, digestible insights that encour age further
explor ation in comprehensive content.
Podcast Teasers
Create short teaser segments from your longer podcast
episodes. These bite-sized audio snippets can be shared across
socials, enticing your audience to engage with the full episodes.
Teasers amplify podcast reach b y drawing in audiences
through intriguing audio snippets.
Reveal and Explore Challenges
Launch short-form challenges revealing a snippet of a larger
theme, then dive deeper into the subject in long-form content,
like blog posts or inter-active videos.
These challenges create inter active, sequential content that
builds community engagement and learning.
Vlog-to-Blog Conversion
Share brief highlights or teasers of your vlogs on social media
and convert these into comprehensive blog posts that elabor ate
on the experiences showcased.
You can repurpose visual content for a textual audience,
catering to diverse preferences.
Content Feedback Loops
Engage your audience b y asking questions or gathering
opinions in short-form content, then compile their responses
into long-form, data-driven insights or analysis.
Feedback fosters community involvement and showcases
audience insights in detailed analysis.
Visualize-Then-Dive
Share eye-catching infogr aphics, visuals, or meme-lik e content
as short-form snippets. Use these as springboards to delve
deeper into the subject in long-form explanatory posts.
This attr acts attention through visually appealing content and
educates through in-depth explanations.
Snippet Series into Masterclass
Roll out a series of short-form educational snippets on a topic,
culminating in a comprehensive masterclass or workshop that
delves extensively into the subject matter.
This provides tiered learning experiences, gr adually leading
to comprehensive expertise.
Mini to Full Story Series
Introduce a short story series or anecdotes across social
platforms and develop them into a comprehensive narr ative or
blog series exploring the char acters or situations in depth.
Use this to capture audience attention with engaging
narr atives, driving interest in the complete story .
Real-time Challenges and In-depth Guides:
Present quick daily challenges or tasks on socials and compile
them into a comprehensive guide or e-book exploring the
strategies and outcomes in detail.
These guides encour age active audience participation and
offer detailed guidance for deeper learning and
implementation.
The crux is that finding the right medium is going to be your
creative evolution—you will encounter a mix of personal
inclination, experimentation, and audience observation useful
in finding the right medium and format. When you better
understand your skills and where you shine brightest, you will
start to attr act the right audience. The journey to this
understanding is a continuous loop of trial, error, and
recalibr ation.
Choose Your Platform
When I set out to find the perfect platform for my influencer
journey , I felt lik e a kid in a candy store with too man y choices.
Each platform seemed lik e a different flavor, and I had to figure
out which one my audience preferred.
The challenge was understanding my audience’ s digital
playground. W ere they more into scrolling through vivid
Instagr am feeds, diving deep into Y ouTube videos, or ma ybe
indulging in quick TikT ok moments? Deciphering their
hangouts felt lik e trying to read a map in a foreign language.
Adapting to the ever-changing algorithms was lik e chasing a
moving target. What work ed brilliantly one da y might tumble

There’ s no one-size-fits-all solution; it’ s more of a quest, a tr ail
of trial and error sprinkled with audience feedback and a good

every content piece, audience preference, and platform must

Two Types of Inﬂuencer Platforms
1. Discovery Platforms
Discovery Platforms are digital spaces where creators showcase
their content to reach a broad audience. These platforms,
including social media sites lik e Instagr am, Y ouTube, TikT ok,
and Twitter, facilitate content visibility and enable creators to
attract new followers and engagement.
I like to call them the stage for our digital performances.
They’re where we showcase our content to the vast sea of
online audiences.
So, imagine the big names lik e Facebook, Instagr am, Y ouTube,
and even search engines lik e Google as bustling mark etplaces.
They’re hungry for one thing—your attention.
Why? Because the longer they k eep us scrolling and engaging,
the more ads they can show us, the more they earn. I remember
when I first realized this—it was a lightbulb moment. These
platforms are designed to match the right content with the right
people.
That’ s where the algorithms come in. They’re lik e
matchmak ers, connecting users with the most engaging content
possible.
Now , this is where the magic happens for creators lik e us. If
we cr aft content that captivates and holds attention, these
platforms reward us b y sharing our content far and wide.
That’ s the dream, right? Going vir al!
But here’ s the thing—when we do go vir al, it’ s like a sneak
peek, an audition in front of a new audience. They might lik e
what they see, but it’ s not an instant deep connection. It tak es
time to build trust.
Even when our content gets a lot of love, these platforms still
have their own rules. Not every piece we post reaches all our
followers. They tend to prioritize what k eeps people glued to
their screens.
So, while these platforms offer us a stage and a shot at the
spotlight, it’ s important to remember that the distribution
power sta ys in their hands. W e’re just borrowing it to share our
content.
But hey , don’t let that discour age you. These platforms open
doors to incredible opportunities and help us reach diverse
audiences we wouldn’t otherwise.
They are most ideal for:
Expanding reach:  Discovery Platforms are perfect for
expanding one’ s audience base and gaining exposure to a
wider demogr aphic. They allow content to be seen b y a
large number of users, increasing the lik elihood of
reaching potential followers.
Quick exposure:  These platforms offer quick exposure
and the potential for content to go vir al. Due to their broad
audience reach, they are ideal for creating buzz around a
new piece of content, a product launch, or an event.
Engagement testing:  Creators often use these platforms to
test content engagement, analyze audience preferences,
and understand what resonates best with their followers.
It’s a space to experiment with various content formats
and styles.
However, while they offer visibility and initial engagement,
they might not guar antee consistent or long-term audience
connection. The challenge lies in tr ansitioning followers from
these platforms to more relationship-focused mediums lik e
email newsletters, podcasts, or private communities for deeper
engagement and lasting connections.
They’re a launchpad for our creativity , allowing us to connect
with people who genuinely appreciate what we do. And that’ s
pretty amazing, isn’t it?
2. Relationship Platforms
Let’s switch gears to Relationship Platforms—the spaces where I
get to build more meaningful connections with those who
genuinely want to hear from me. These platforms aren’t about
“owning an audience,” but r ather about having a direct line of
communication with individuals who’ve willingly opted in to
engage.
Relationship Platforms are mediums where influencers or
creators directly communicate and engage with their audience.
Examples include email newsletters, podcasts, SMS (text
messages), or private communities (lik e Discord or Patreon).
Think of it this wa y—I might not “own” each person in my
audience, but I do have the privilege to connect and share with
them as long as they choose to sta y connected.
Now , onto the four Relationship Platforms I swear b y:
1. Email
2. Podcasts
3. SMS (text messages)
4. Private communities (lik e Discord, Circle, Uscreen, and
others)
These platforms are my backstage passes, gr anting me the
chance to directly reach out to my audience without algorithms
or filters. When someone signs up for my email list or
subscribes to my podcast, it’ s like they’re giving me a VIP pass
to their inbox or podcast app.
But, let me tell you, it’ s not as easy as hitting a “follow” button
on social media. Sharing personal contact details—lik e an email
address or joining a private community—is a leap of faith. It’ s a
trust fall between us.
Yet, that’ s where the real magic happens—the conversations
are deeper, the engagement is more genuine, and the
relationships are stronger.
These platforms are best utilized when influencers aim to:
Establish deeper connections:  Relationship Platforms
allow influencers to foster more intimate connections with
their audience. They’re ideal for engaging with dedicated
followers who seek more personalized and exclusive
content.
Own and control engagement:  Unlik e Discovery
Platforms, where algorithms control content visibility ,
relationship platforms provide more control over content
distribution. Creators can directly communicate with their
audience without algorithmic restrictions.
Create long-term engagement:  They are perfect for
nurturing long-term relationships with dedicated
followers. These platforms offer a reliable means of
communication, ensuring that content reaches subscribers
without being affected b y platform algorithms or changes.
The primary benefit is the ownership and control over
audience engagement, ensuring that the influencer ’s messages
reach the audience reliably and directly . However, they require
a higher level of commitment and trust from the audience, as
followers willingly provide contact information or opt into
these platforms to receive content.
The Rule of Thumb
Think of your influencer platforms as the place for building a
strong social circle. Y ou want the buzzing hotspots where
everyone hangs out (Discovery Platforms) and the cozy spots
where you chat comfortably (Relationship Platforms).
My personal str ategy? K eep it simple:
focus on one Discovery Platform, lik e TikT ok or Instagr am,
to showcase your content to a broad audience
then, choose one Relationship Platform, such as an
engaging newsletter or a podcast, where you can connect
more intimately with your followers
Imagine it lik e throwing an awesome party in the city center to
get noticed, and then hosting an exclusive gathering at your
favorite café to bond with your closest friends.
This two-pronged approach helps cast a wide net to attr act
new followers while building meaningful relationships with
your core audience.

New Attention vs. Retained Attention
Attention is won in two steps: Capturing it and retaining it.
Man y creators excel at gr abbing attention but struggle to k eep
it. This realization struck me after observing the typical focus
on capturing attention while neglecting retention.
I found this understanding crucial to share because it’ s a
pivotal efficiency factor. Man y invest energy and resources in
gaining visibility without securing a lasting connection with
their audience. It’ s akin to pouring water into a leaky buck et—
the effort and resources go in, but the retention is minimal.
When creators fail to tr ansition their audience from
Discovery Platforms to Relationship Platforms, it signifies an
attention retention problem. Building a robust, long-term
relationship with your audience is vital. This is what eventually
creates a sustainable distribution system that you control.
It dawned on me after noticing the struggle man y creators
face in shifting from capturing attention to retaining it: It’ s
important to develop str ategies that focus on both aspects.
Rather than fixating solely on amassing a large following, the
goal should be nurturing a committed audience base over time.
New attention refers to the initial notice or interest people
have when discovering your content or br and. It’ s the first
impression, the spark that ignites curiosity . On the other hand,
retained attention focuses on maintaining and deepening that
initial interest, building a lasting connection, and fostering
ongoing engagement with your audience.
The difference between these types of attention matters for
the following reasons:
Long-term engagement:  New attention is fleeting; it’ s the
entry point. Retained attention, however, is what sustains
your relationship with your audience over time.
Trust and lo yalty:  While new attention indicates initial
interest, retained attention allows you to nurture trust and
loyalty . It’s about delivering consistent value and quality to
keep your audience engaged.
Conversion and advocacy:  Retained attention often leads
to conversions (lik e purchases or subscriptions) and turns
audience members into advocates for your br and or
content.
Your str ategy should be a balanced blend:
Capture attention—Discovery Platforms:  Lever age
Discovery Platforms to attr act new attention. Engage with
eye-catching content, trends, or vir al topics to bring people
in.
Retain attention—Relationship Platforms:  Transition
the new attention to a Relationship Platform. F ocus on
providing continuous value and building trust through
high-quality , personalized content.
Measure and adapt:  Track metrics lik e engagement, click-
through r ates, and retention to understand what works.
Adapt your str ategy to better cater to your audience’ s
needs and preferences.
Here are some questions to consider:
How can I mak e my content stand out to gr ab new
attention?
What value can I offer to retain the attention of my
audience?
How can I tr ansition new attention into a more engaged
relationship?
What platforms or formats align best with my content and
audience for sustained engagement?
How can I measure and improve retention metrics over
time?
So, consider your content medium, format, and platform wisely .
Choose avenues that align with your strengths and audience
preferences. Balancing between capturing and retaining
attention is the cornerstone of sustained success in the creator
space.

Campaign Ideation Strategies

Building connections:  These campaigns build a

Experiential campaigns  take the audience from digital to

This immersive approach creates lasting impressions. It’ s an

Trend Following vs. Trend Setting
Following trends is lik e riding a wave—you catch it, ride it out,
and enjo y the momentum. But being a trendsetter? That’ s like
creating the wave—setting the tone, direction, and pace.
Why follow trends? W ell, they offer immediate visibility .
When you hop on a trend, you align with what’ s hot, tapping
into a ready-made audience and boosting your visibility . It’s an
express tick et to getting noticed, engaging your audience, and
staying relevant.
However, setting trends?  It’s a game-changer. Y ou become the
one everyone’ s watching. It’ s about innovation, originality , and
creating the next big thing. But it’ s not an easy feat.
It starts with knowing your audience inside out. Know their
needs, desires, pain points. Then, blend that insight with your
authentic voice, creativity , and expertise. Y our goal is to
anticipate what they’ll love before they know they’ll love it.
The “how” is a mix of experimentation, risk-taking, and
staying true to your br and. Be bold, test new ideas, push
boundaries. Don’t fear failure—it’ s often the stepping stone to
success. And timing? W ell, that’ s the magic trick! K eep your
finger on the pulse of cultur al shifts, emerging tech, and societal
changes. Strik e when the iron’ s hot.
There’ s value in both—riding trends k eeps you relevant, but
setting trends mak es you a game-changer. Balance is k ey. So,
hop on trends while innovating on the sidelines, and who
knows? Y ou might just create the next big wave everyone wants
to catch.
I’ve found that being a trendsetter creates your unique
identity . When you lead with original ideas, you’re not just part
of the conversation—you’re shaping it. Y ou’re not a follower,
you’re the one setting the tone. That distinction is incredibly
empowering. It’ s like having your br and’ s unique stamp on the
industry , and that’ s priceless.
Of course, it’ s not all sunshine and r ainbows. Being
innovative comes with risks. Sometimes your fresh ideas might
not resonate immediately , or they might even receive some
skepticism. There’ s an inherent uncertainty in pioneering new
trends. It requires patience, persistence, and the readiness to
embr ace occasional setbacks.
Despite the risks, setting trends is a long-term investment. It
builds a lo yal audience who sees you as a visionary in your
niche. Y ou’re not just adapting to what’ s popular, you’re
defining what’ s next. And that’ s a powerful position to be in.
Plus, the satisfaction of seeing your unique ideas gain tr action—
there’ s nothing quite lik e it.
You get to shape the industry landscape and leave your mark
on it. That, to me, mak es it entirely worth the effort and risk.

Lastly , check metrics . Track, tweak, pivot. One campaign I

A Step-by-Step Guide for Implementing Audience-Driven Trends
in Your Strategy
1. Trend spotting:  Start b y observing creators in your niche.

5. Campaign innovation:  Integr ate trends into your

6. Adapt and sta y consistent:  Trends evolve swiftly . Remain

7. The authenticity factor:  Ensure that partnerships
resonate with your br and values. A uthenticity builds trust
and connects with your audience.
8. Data-driven insights:  Measure campaign metrics.
Understand how trends affect engagement and
conversions. A dapt str ategies based on these insights.
Lever aging creator-driven trends in influencer campaigns
demands a blend of flexibility and astute observation. It’ s about
marrying the trend’ s appeal with your br and’ s distinct identity .

Achieving Long-term Success as
a Creator
There’ s really only one wa y to ensure that you can sustain a
career or side-hustle as a successful creator and it’ s simple but
not easy: Y ou’ve got to niche down str ategically . Focus on a
specific area where you excel or have in-depth knowledge.
Niche-specific micro-influencers get 60 percent more
engagement (Schneider, 2024) as compared to mega-
influencers.
Nic he Down
Identify Your Distinct Expertise or Passion
It could be something unconventional, lik e infusing psychology
into B2B sales str ategies or exploring AI’ s impact on HR.
Ask
What specific area in B2B excites me the most?
What unique skills or knowledge do I have within this
area?
To-Do
Use a table or chart with columns for each section, allowing you
to easily compare and analyze your passions and expertise.
Strengths:  List your top skills and strengths related to
B2B.
Interests:  Document specific areas within B2B that
genuinely fascinate you.
Curiosity sparks:  Record what aspects of B2B mak e you
curious or eager to learn more.
Dive Deeper Beyond Broad Categories
For instance, within mark eting, focus on something specific,
like conversational mark eting for SaaS companies. Micro-niches
can set you apart and attr act highly engaged audiences.
Ask
How can I narrow down this niche even further?
What subtopics or specific segments within my expertise
have the potential to captivate a dedicated audience?
To-Do
Use a spreadsheet or mind map, arr anging these sections for
each potential niche, making it easy to compare and prioritize.
List niche ideas:  List potential micro-niches or subtopics
within your B2B expertise.
Mark audience relevance:  Note wh y each niche might
resonate with your audience or how it aligns with mark et
demands.
Personal interest:  Highlight wh y each niche excites you
personally .
Zone In on One or Two Major Pain Points
Delve into nuanced issues—perhaps addressing remote team
collabor ation challenges in global B2B companies or navigating
compliance in fintech.
Ask
What precise challenges do businesses face within this
narrowed niche?
Which pain points are most critical or underserved?
Document
Create a document or list, categorizing each pain point with its
impact and potential solutions/content angles for reference.
Pain points:  Describe specific challenges or pain points
faced b y businesses in your niche.
Impact analysis:  Explain the significance of each pain
point—how it affects businesses and wh y it needs
addressing.
Solutions/content angles:  Brainstorm potential solutions
or content angles to address these pain points.
Combine Seemingly Unrelated Niches
Blend B2B mark eting with elements from, sa y, sustainable

Develop Your Unique Methodology or Framework
Whether it’ s a proprietary str ategy for content mark eting in
niche industries or a step-b y-step process for effective B2B

Creators often develop unique methodologies or fr ameworks
that reflect their expertise and differentiate their content. Here
are a few examples across different domains:
Content creation
Gary V aynerchuk’ s “Jab, Jab, Jab, Right Hook”: This
methodology emphasizes providing value (jabs) before
making an ask or promotion (right hook) (Aster, 2021). It’ s
about delivering content that serves the audience before
seeking returns.
Fitness and wellness
Kayla Itsines’ “BBG” (Bikini Body Guide): Ka yla’s work out
progr am focuses on 28-minute high-intensity work outs
and meal plans. It’ s a structured, easy-to-follow
framework for fitness enthusiasts (Goodreads, n.d.).
Business and entrepreneurship
The Lean Startup b y Eric Ries: It’ s about developing
businesses and products through short cycles of
experimentation and learning. It emphasizes customer
feedback, iter ation, and validated learning (Reis, 2011).
Personal development
Tim F erriss’ The 4-Hour W orkweek: Tim F erriss
introduced str ategies for increased productivity , efficiency ,
and lifestyle design. It focuses on optimizing time and
resources for a better work-life balance (F erris, 2007).
Finance and investment
Warren Buffett’ s Value Investing Principles: Buffett’ s
approach involves identifying undervalued stocks based
on fundamental analysis and a long-term investment
horizon (Shvartsman, 2024).
Education and learning
Khan A cademy’ s Mastery Learning: Providing free,
personalized learning experiences to master subjects at
one’ s own pace using a structured curriculum and
assessment (Khan A cademy , n.d.).

brands to embr ace the richness of diversity and inclusion. W e

life, weaving a tapestry of perspectives and experiences into
our mark eting campaigns. This not only ensures that your
brand resonates with a wider audience but also fosters a sense
of belonging and inclusivity within your community .
The Rise of Specialized Inﬂuencers
Gone are the da ys of one-size-fits-all influencers. T oday, we see
the rise of specialized influencers who possess in-depth
knowledge and expertise in specific niches and industries.
These “micro-influencers” ma y have smaller follower bases
compared to mainstream figures, but they offer unpar alleled
reach and engagement within their targeted audience. B y
partnering with specialists, br ands can ensure their message
resonates deeply with the right individuals, maximizing the
effectiveness of their campaigns.
Chief Inﬂuence Ofﬁcers
Recognizing the critical role of influencer mark eting, man y B2B
brands are appointing dedicated Chief Influence Officers (CIOs).
These individuals spearhead the development and execution of
influencer mark eting str ategies, ensuring alignment with
over all mark eting goals and maximizing the potential of this
powerful tool.
Employee Inﬂuencer Advantage
Your most valuable assets are right under your nose. B y
empowering your emplo yees to become br and advocates, you
can tap into a powerful and authentic voice. Imagine your
passionate emplo yees sharing their genuine experiences and
expertise, building trust and credibility with potential
customers, and showcasing your compan y culture from the
inside out.
The Importance of First-Party Data
In a world satur ated with information, owning first-party data
is a valuable asset. B2B br ands need to prioritize collecting and
lever aging data from their websites, social media platforms,
and customer inter actions. This allows for a deeper
understanding of their audience, enabling them to tailor their
influencer mark eting campaigns and optimize their reach and
engagement.
Performance-Based Deals
In toda y’s data-driven world, results speak volumes. B2B br ands
are increasingly embr acing performance-based deals, where
influencers are rewarded based on their ability to achieve
specific results, such as lead gener ation, website tr affic, or sales
conversions. This approach ensures a clear alignment of
incentives, maximizing return on investment and ensuring that
every collabor ation delivers tangible value.
The Future is Collaborative
The future of B2B influencer mark eting is bright, and it’ s built
on collabor ation. B y embr acing emerging trends, utilizing
innovative technologies, and working closely with talented
creators, br ands can unlock the immense potential of this
powerful mark eting channel. So, let’ s join forces, roll up our
sleeves, and together, shape the future of B2B influencer
mark eting into something truly remarkable.

Creator-First Future Trends
As someone who navigates the B2B influencer mark eting
landscape every da y, I’ve witnessed the evolution firsthand.
From the tr ansactional, one-off collabor ations of the past to the
collabor ative, integr ated partnerships of toda y, the shift
towards creator-first str ategies has been remarkable. But it’ s
more than just a shift in pr actice; it’ s a change in mindset that
recognizes the immense value creators bring to the table. It’ s
about moving beyond simply lever aging them to actively
partnering with them, empowering them to become co-creators
of our br and stories.
Why Creator-First Matters
Remember those campaigns that felt forced and inauthentic?
Yeah, those da ys are fading awa y. Creator-first partnerships are
built on trust and shared vision. It’ s not about dictating every
aspect of the campaign but giving creators the freedom to
express themselves and interpret our message in a wa y that
resonates with their audience. This results in content that feels
genuine, relatable, and ultimately , more impactful.
Unlocking the Power of Authenticity
One of the biggest benefits of creator-first is the authenticity it
fosters. Creators connect with their communities on a personal
level, building trust and lo yalty . When they share a br and
message, it doesn’t feel lik e an advertisement; it feels lik e a
recommendation from a friend. This authenticity cuts through
the noise and connects with audiences on a deeper level,
driving engagement and br and affinity .
The Flexibility and Adaptability Advantage
The B2B mark eting landscape is constantly evolving, and
brands need to be agile to adapt. Creator-first partnerships
provide the flexibility we need to sta y ahead of the curve.
Creators are often at the forefront of emerging trends, and they
can help us tailor our message and content to resonate with
ever-changing audiences. This allows us to be more responsive
and adaptable in a dynamic mark etplace.
Building Bridges and Fostering Collaboration
Of course, tr ansitioning to a creator-first approach requires
collabor ation, both internally and externally . We need to break
down silos within our own organizations and foster open
communication between mark eting teams, leadership, and
creators. This ensures everyone is on the same page and
working toward shared goals. A dditionally , we need to build
strong relationships with creators, understanding their needs
and aspir ations. This collabor ative spirit is the foundation of
successful creator-first partnerships.
Learning from the Leaders
The power of creator-first str ategies is undeniable. It’ s a shift
toward collabor ation, empowering creators to become active
partners in br and storytelling and driving impactful results. But
beyond the theoretical benefits, let’ s delve into the world of
brands who have successfully adopted this approach and
witnessed remarkable outcomes.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE 1
Glossier and the Inﬂuencer Collective
Glossier, the beauty brand known for its Millennial-focused products and transparent
marketing, has successfully nurtured a community of “Glossier girls” through its strong
emphasis on creator-ﬁrst partnerships (Oswald, 2022). They do this by:
Partnering with micro-inﬂuencers: Focusing on smaller, niche inﬂuencers who align with
their brand values and connect with a loyal audience.
Sharing creative control: Empowering creators to produce authentic content that
resonates with their unique style and voice.
Building long-term relationships: Investing in ongoing collaborations with creators,
fostering trust and mutual understanding.
This creator-ﬁrst approach has resulted in:
Signiﬁcant brand awareness: Glossier has built a dedicated community of loyal
customers who trust the brand recommendations of their favorite creators.
Increased product sales: Inﬂuencer-generated content has been instrumental in driving
product trials and conversions.
Enhanced brand sentiment: Glossier is consistently praised for its authenticity and
commitment to diversity and inclusion.
REAL-WORLD EXAMPLE 2
Patagonia and the Environmental Activist Collaborations
Patagonia, the outdoor apparel brand known for its environmental activism, has seamlessly
integrated creator-ﬁrst strategies into its mission-driven marketing (Net Inﬂuencer, 2022).
They do this by:
Partnering with environmental activists: Collaborating with individuals who share their
passion for environmentalism and can amplify their message.
Supporting creators’ initiatives: Patagonia provides creators with resources and support
to implement their own environmental projects.
Leveraging social media for impact: Using creators’ platforms to raise awareness about
environmental issues and inspire action.
This creator-ﬁrst approach has resulted in:
Increased brand afﬁnity among environmentally conscious consumers: Patagonia’s
commitment to sustainability resonates with a growing audience who align with their
values.
Enhanced brand loyalty: Patagonia fosters a loyal customer base who are passionate
about the brand and its mission.
Positive social impact: Patagonia’s creator-ﬁrst partnerships have contributed to
raising awareness about environmental issues and driving positive change.
Beyond the Numbers: Measuring the Impact of
Creator-First
The success of these campaigns extends beyond tr aditional
metrics lik e clicks and impressions. Creator-first str ategies
focus on deeper engagement, br and affinity , and ultimately ,
driving business impact. Here are some k ey KPIs to consider:
Social media engagement:  Likes, comments, shares, and
mentions are indicators of audience interest and
inter action with creator-gener ated content.
Website tr affic and conversions:  Analyzing the impact of
influencer campaigns on website tr affic and conversions
helps measure effectiveness in driving leads and sales.
Brand awareness and sentiment:  Tracking br and
mentions and sentiment analysis provides insights into
how audiences perceive the br and and its message.
Sales and revenue growth:  Ultimately , the success of
creator-first partnerships is measured b y their ability to
contribute to the br and’ s bottom line.
By focusing on these KPIs, br ands can gain valuable insights
into the effectiveness of their creator-first campaigns and
demonstr ate the tangible impact they have on their business
objectives.
Should You Advocate for Standardization?
As we witness the success of creator-first partnerships, the need
for standardization becomes increasingly evident. Establishing
industry-wide best pr actices and guidelines ensures
transparency , ethical conduct, and mutual respect between
brands and creators.
Here’ s how we can collectively advocate for standardization:
Collabor ation : Industry stak eholders, including br ands,
creators, agencies, and platforms, need to work together to
develop clear standards for creator-first partnerships.
Transparency : Brands should be tr ansparent about their
collabor ations with creators, including disclosure of
partnerships and compensation terms.
Education : We need to educate the mark et about the
benefits and best pr actices of creator-first str ategies,
fostering trust and understanding among all parties.
By working together, we can build a sustainable and mutually
beneficial ecosystem where creator-first partnerships thrive
and contribute to the growth and success of the B2B mark eting
landscape.
Bridging the Gap: Educational Initiatives for
Creator-First Success
To facilitate widespread adoption of creator-first str ategies, we
need to invest in knowledge sharing and skill development.
Here are some k ey initiatives:
Training progr ams for mark eting professionals : Equipping

Integr ation of creator-first principles into mark eting
curricula : Preparing the next gener ation of mark eters for a

Industry events and webinars : Providing platforms for

How to Measure Success in Creator-First Campaigns
So, you’ve embark ed on the thrilling journey of creator-first
collabor ations, and your content is buzzing with authenticity
and engagement. But how do you know if you’re truly on the
path to success? Just lik e an y journey , measuring progress is
crucial to ensure you’re heading in the right direction.
Beyond Clicks and Impressions
Gone are the da ys of obsessing over vanity metrics lik e clicks
and impressions. While they hold some value, they don’t paint
the whole picture. T o truly gauge the success of your creator-
first campaigns, we need to dive deeper.
Here are some k ey metrics that can be your compass:
Engagement : Lik es, comments, shares, and discussions
reveal how deeply your audience is inter acting with the
content. Are they actively participating? Are meaningful
conversations happening?
Brand awareness : Track how your br and recognition and
recall are evolving. Are people remembering your br and
after seeing the influencer content?
Website tr affic and conversions : Are the collabor ations
driving qualified leads and ultimately leading to
conversions and sales?
Sentiment analysis : Understand how people perceive your
brand through social media mentions and online reviews.
Is the sentiment positive and aligned with your br and
values?
Continuous Monitoring and Optimization
Just lik e a plant needs consistent care, your creator-first
campaigns require ongoing monitoring and optimization.
Regularly analyze the data, tr ack trends, and identify areas for
improvement. Are certain creators performing better than
others? Is the content resonating with your target audience?
This valuable feedback allows you to refine your str ategy and
maximize your results.
Tailoring the Approach
Remember, there’ s no one-size-fits-all approach to creator-first
campaigns. What works for one br and or industry might not be
suitable for another. Consider factors lik e your specific
industry , target audience, and br and goals to tailor your
evaluation metrics and optimization str ategies.
A Case-by-Case Approach
Let’s tak e two examples:
1. A tech compan y targeting IT professionals : They might
prioritize metrics lik e website tr affic and lead gener ation,
demonstr ating the effectiveness of their campaign in
driving qualified leads.
2. A fashion br and targeting Gen Z consumers : They might
focus on engagement metrics lik e social media shares and
mentions, measuring the campaign’ s ability to gener ate
buzz and br and awareness among their target audience.
By understanding the unique context of each campaign and
applying relevant metrics, br ands can mak e informed decisions
and optimize their creator-first str ategies for maximum impact.
Final Thoughts
Measuring success in creator-first campaigns is an ongoing
process, requiring a str ategic approach and customized metrics.
By embr acing continuous monitoring, data-driven insights, and
case-b y-case adjustments, br ands can ensure their creator-first
collabor ations thrive and contribute to achieving their
mark eting goals. So, k eep your eyes on the data, adapt your
strategies, and unlock the immense potential of authentic
storytelling through creator-first partnerships.
Remember, the journey to a creator-first future is an ongoing
process. There will be challenges and obstacles along the wa y,
but b y working together, we can overcome them and build a
B2B mark eting landscape where creators are recognized and
valued as the essential partners they truly are.
